بيان تقسيم الوجوب "من ۹۵ بيان حكم الواجب بالأمر من" نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها، فإن ذلك وقتها"، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ كَانَ مَرِيضاً أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ (البقرة : ١٨٥) بل إنما وردا للتنبيه على أن الأداء باقٍ في ذمتكم بالنصين السابقين لم يسقط بالفوات؛ لأن بقاء الموجبين للأداء الصلاة والصوم في نفسه للقدرة على مثل من عنده، وسقوط فضل الوقت لا إلى مثل وضمان للعجز عنه أمر معقول في نفسه، فعدّينا حكم القضاء إلى ما لم يرد فيه نص، وهو المنذور فعدة إلخ: أي فعليه إفطار أيام المرض والسفر، وعدة من أيام أُخر. (القمر) بل إنما وردا: أي النصان الجديدان للتنبيه إلخ، ولتعريف المثل القائم مقام الأداء، ولذا ما لم يعرف مثله لا يجب قضاءه كصلاة الجمعة والعيدين. (القمر) لم يسقط بالفوات: فإن الأداء صار مستحقاً عليه وفراغ من عليه الحق عن الحق إما بالأداء و لم يوجد ، وإما بالعجز و لم يوجد، فإنه قادر على أصل العبادة، وإن عجز عن إدراك فضيلة الوقت، وإما بإسقاط صاحب الحق وهو لم يوجد لا صراحةً كما هو الظاهر، ولا دلالة، فإنه لم يحدث إلا خروج الوقت وهو لا يصلح مسقطا، بل يقرر ما على ذي الحق من العهدة (القمر) لأن إلخ : دليل على أن النص الموجب للأداء دال بعينه على وجوب القضاء، أو هو مرتبط بقوله : لم يسقط بالفوات. (القمر) في نفسه أي بدون وصفه وهو كونه في وقت كذا. (القمر) وسقوط إلخ : معطوف على البقاء وههنا تضمين معنى الانتهاء أي سقوط فضل الوقت وشرفه غير منتبه سقوطه إلى مثل كان من جنسه وإلى زمان كان من خلاف جنسه؛ إذ لم يشرع للعبد ما يماثل شرف الوقت ولا قرر له ضمان . (القمر) للعجز عنه: أي عن فضل الوقت، وهذا متعلق بالسقوط. (القمر) فعدينا إلخ أي إذا ثبت أن نص الأداء موجب للقضاء فيما ورد فيه نص جديد كالصلاة والصوم، فعدينا وجاوزنا حكم القضاء إلى ما لم يرد فيه نص جديد للقضاء. (القمر) وهو المنذور إلخ النص الموجب للأداء فيه قوله: ﴿وَلْيُوفُوا نُذُورَهُمْ (الحج: ٢٩) والمراد بالمنذور: المنذور المؤقت، إذ لا قضاء في غير المؤقت لعدم الفوات الذي هو مناط القضاء. (القمر) أخرجه مسلم رقم ٦٨٤ ، باب قضاء الصلاة الفائتة واستحباب تعجيل قضائها وابن حبان في "صحيحه" رقم ١٥٥٦، ٤٢٣/٤ ، وأحمد في مسنده" رقم: ۱۱۹۹۱، عن أنس بن مالك له، والنسائي رقم: ٦١٥، باب فيمن نام عن صلاة، والترمذي رقم: ۱۷۷ ، باب ما جاء في النوم عن الصلاة وابن ماجه رقم: ٦٩٨، باب من نام عن الصلاة أو نسيها والدار قطني في " سننه ٣٨٦/١ ، عن أبي قتادة وليس فيها لفظ: فإن ذلك وقتها، قال العلي القاري: إنه زاد في التوضيح" فإن ذلك وقتها.

مبحث الخاص من 97 بيان حكم الواجب بالأمر له الصلاة والصيام والاعتكاف وعند الشافعي به لابد للقضاء من نص جديد موجب سوى نص الأداء، فقضاء الصلاة والصوم عنده لابد أن يكون بقوله عليه: "من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها، فإن ذلك وقتها، وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنْكُمْ مَرِيضًا أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ وما لم يرد النص فيه إنما يثبت القضاء بسبب التفويت الذي يقوم مقام (البقرة : ١٨٤) نص القضاء، فلا تظهر ثمرة الخلاف بيننا وبينه إلا في الفوات فعندنا يجب القضاء في الفوات. وعنده لا ، وقيل : الفوات أيضًا قائم مقام النص كالتفويت ولا تظهر ثمرة الخلاف إلا في أي تخريج الحكم فعندنا يجب في الكل بالنص السابق، وعنده يجب بالنص الجديد أو بالفوات الموجب للأداء التخريج، والتفويت، وقضاء الحضر في السفر أربع ركعات وقضاء السفر في الحضر ركعتين، وقضاء الجهر في النهار جهرًا وقضاء السرّ في الليل سرا يؤيد ما ذكرنا، وقضاء الصحيح صلاة كالمغرب والعشاء كالظهر والعصر المرض بعنوان الصحة وقضاء المريض صلاة الصحة بعنوان المرض يؤيد ما ذكره يقوم إلخ: فكأنه إذا فوت فقد التزم القضاء، فالتفويت تعد، والتعدي سبب الضمان . (القمر) إلا في الفوات بأن مرض أو جن في اليوم المنذور فيه مثلاً. (القمر) يجب القضاء لأن النص الموجب للأداء موجب القضاء. (القمر) وعنده لا : أي لا يجب القضاء؛ لأن وجوب القضاء عنده بسبب جديد، وإذ ليس التفويت أيضًا، فلا يجب القضاء في الفوات. (القمر) وقيل إلخ كما يفهم من كلام شمس الأئمة: أن الفوات بمنزلة التفويت عندهم (القمر) في الكل أي ما وجد فيه نص جديد أو فوات أو تفويت. (القمر) جهرا أي وجوبًا للإمام وأفضلية للمنفرد. (القمر) سرًا أي وجوبًا للإمام وللمنفرد. (القمر) يؤيد ما ذكرنا فإن هذه المسائل تدل على أن القضاء يجب بالسبب السابق. قال ابن الملك: ولقائل أن يقول: وجوب مراعاة الجهر ،وعدمه، وكذا القصر والإتمام باعتبار أن وجوب القضاء باعتبار المثل لا لأنه الأول. (القمر) يؤيد ما ذكره فإن هاتين المسألتين تدلان على أن موجب القضاء غير سبب الأداء وإلا لم يتفاوت الأداء والقضاء، وأجاب عنه بعض شراح أصول البزدوي (أي صاحب الكشف بما توضيحه: أن السبب في حق الأداء انعقد في هاتين الصورتين موجبًا للقيام والركوع والسجود باعتبار توهم القدرة مع جواز الانتقال إلى الخلف أي القعود والإيماء عند العجز إن اختار الفعل في حالة العجز ، وكذلك انعقد في حق القضاء بلا تفاوت، فإذا فاتته = وجب بالسبب
Section on the division of obligation. From page 95: Exposition of the ruling of the obligatory by command. "Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it, for that is its time." And His statement: "And whoever is ill or on a journey, then a number of other days" (al-Baqarah 2:185). Rather they came only to alert that performance remains in your liability by the two previous texts, not fallen by being missed; because the continuity of the two obligators of performance—prayer and fasting—in themselves due to ability for its like from him, and the loss of the merit of time without a like and guarantee for incapacity for it is something rational in itself. So we extended the ruling of qada to what has no text in it, such as the vowed [act]... 'a number of other days' i.e. he must break the fast of the days of illness and travel and fast a number of other days. (al-Qamar) Rather they came: i.e. the two new texts for the alert, and to define the equivalent that stands in place of performance. Hence, when its equivalent is not known, its qada is not obligatory, like Friday and Eid prayers. (al-Qamar) Not fallen by being missed: for performance became due upon him, and the person liable is free from the right either by performance—which did not occur—or by incapacity—which did not occur, for he is able to do the basic act even if unable to attain the merit of time, or by waiver of the right-holder—which did not occur explicitly nor implicitly, for nothing happened except the exit of time, which is not a valid ground for waiver; rather it confirms the liability of the debtor. (al-Qamar) Because etc.: proof that the text obligating performance itself indicates the obligation of qada, or it is connected to his statement: not fallen by being missed. (al-Qamar) In itself i.e. without its description of being at such a time. (al-Qamar) And the loss etc.: conjoined to 'the continuity', and there is an implication of termination here: i.e. the loss of the merit and honor of time is not something that falls into a like from its kind and into a time from a different kind; for the servant has not been prescribed anything that matches the honor of time nor has a guarantee been assigned for him. (al-Qamar) Due to incapacity for it: i.e. for the merit of time, and this relates to the falling. (al-Qamar) So we extended etc.: i.e. when it is established that the text of performance necessitates qada in matters where a new text has come, like prayer and fasting, then we extended the ruling of qada to matters where no new text for qada has come. (al-Qamar) And it is the vowed etc.: the text obligating performance in it is His statement: "Let them fulfill their vows" (al-Hajj 29). And by the vowed is meant the time-bound vow, for there is no qada in non-time-bound vows due to the absence of being missed which is the basis of qada. (al-Qamar) Narrated by Muslim no. 684, chapter on qada of missed prayer and preference for hastening its qada, and Ibn Hibban in his Sahih no. 1556, 4/423, and Ahmad in his Musnad no. 11991 from Anas ibn Malik, and al-Nasa'i no. 615, chapter on one who sleeps through prayer, and al-Tirmidhi no. 177, chapter on sleep through prayer and Ibn Majah no. 698, chapter on one who sleeps through or forgets a prayer, and al-Daraqutni in his Sunan 1/386 from Abu Qatada, and in it is not the wording 'for that is its time.' Al-Qari said: It is added in al-Tawdih: 'for that is its time.'

Section on al-Khas from page 97: Exposition of the ruling of the wajib by command. For him—prayer, fasting, i'tikaf. And according to al-Shafi'i, for qada a new text is necessary besides the text of performance. So qada of prayer and fasting according to him must be by his statement: "Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it, for that is its time." And His statement: "So whoever among you is ill or on a journey, then a number of other days" (al-Baqarah 2:184). And where no text has come, qada is only established due to the causing to miss which stands in place of the text of qada. So the fruit of the disagreement between us and him appears only in [the case of] being missed unintentionally. According to us, qada is obligatory in being missed unintentionally. According to him, no. And it is said: being missed unintentionally is also like causing to miss, so the fruit of disagreement appears only in takhrij al-hukm. According to us, it is obligatory in all by the previous text; according to him, it is obligatory by the new text or by being missed unintentionally. The text obligating performance: takhrij and causing to miss. And qada of a resident during travel [as] four rak'ahs, and qada of a traveler during residence [as] two rak'ahs, and qada of loud [prayers] during the day aloud, and qada of quiet [prayers] at night quietly supports what we have said. And qada of a healthy person for the prayer of illness under the title of health, and qada of a sick person for the prayer of health under the title of illness supports what he mentioned. 'Stands in place' etc.: as if when he causes to miss, he has undertaken qada. So causing to miss is transgression, and transgression is a cause of guarantee. (al-Qamar) Except in being missed unintentionally: such as if he becomes ill or insane on the day he vowed, for example. (al-Qamar) Qada is obligatory because the text obligating performance necessitates qada. (al-Qamar) According to him no: i.e. qada is not obligatory because for him the obligation of qada is due to a new cause, and since there is no causing to miss either, qada is not obligatory in being missed unintentionally. (al-Qamar) And it is said etc.: as understood from the words of Shams al-A'imma that being missed unintentionally is like causing to miss according to them. (al-Qamar) In all: i.e. matters where a new text, being missed unintentionally, or causing to miss exists. (al-Qamar) Aloud: i.e. obligatory for the imam and recommended for the individual. (al-Qamar) Quietly: i.e. obligatory for the imam and for the individual. (al-Qamar) Supports what we have said: for these issues indicate that qada is obligatory by the prior cause. Ibn al-Malik said: One could say that the obligation of observing aloud or not, similarly shortening and completing, is based on the fact that qada is by way of like, not because of the original. (al-Qamar) Supports what he mentioned: for these two issues indicate that the cause of qada is other than the cause of performance; otherwise performance and qada would not differ. And some commentators on Usul al-Bazdawi (i.e. the author of al-Kashf) replied with the clarification that: the cause in respect of performance was established in these two cases as obligating standing, bowing, and prostrating due to hypothetical ability with the permissibility of transitioning to the next [i.e. sitting and gesturing] in case of incapacity if he chooses to act in the state of incapacity. Similarly, it was established in respect of qada without difference. So when it is missed, it is obligatory by the cause.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational Hanafi usul principle: the original command (amr) to perform an act at its designated time (ada) is also a command to make it up (qada) if the act is missed, whether due to forgetfulness, sleep, or other reasons. The author begins by citing two primary proofs: the hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it, for that is its time' and the Quranic verse on making up missed fasts (al-Baqarah 2:185). The Hanafi argument is that these texts do not introduce a new obligation; rather, they clarify that the original obligation remains in the person's liability and is not nullified by the mere passage of time. The commentary explains that the obligation to perform the act 'in itself' (i.e., without its time qualification) persists, and the loss of the time's merit does not extinguish the original duty; instead, it necessitates a substitute ('like') that compensates for the missing time-based virtue. From this, the Hanafis extend the ruling of qada to acts not explicitly mentioned in these texts, such as time-bound vows (al-nadhr al-muwaqqat), using the principle that the underlying cause (al-sabab) is the existence of an original command that was not fulfilled. The passage then contrasts this with the Shafi'i position, which requires a separate, new textual evidence for qada, and hence does not obligate qada in cases of involuntary missing (fawat) as opposed to deliberate forfeiture (tafwit). Practical differences are illustrated: qada of a resident's prayer during travel is four rak'ahs (not shortened), while qada of a traveler's prayer at home is two rak'ahs; similarly, qada of loud prayers during the day is aloud, and quiet prayers at night are quiet. These examples demonstrate that the Hanafi view treats qada as a 'like' (mithl) of the original act, maintaining the same attributes. Further, the passage addresses an objection about two specific cases (prayer of a healthy person qada of an ill person's prayer, and vice versa) and provides a response that the cause (sabab) for both ada and qada is the same, but the specific attributes may differ due to the circumstances of inability.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; a legal requirement that is firmly established by a definitive evidence.
القضاء (al-qada): Making up a missed obligatory act after its designated time has passed, by performing its like.
الفوات (al-fawat): Being missed unintentionally, e.g., due to sleep, forgetfulness, illness, or insanity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the basis for the obligation to make up a missed prayer?
A) A separate hadith specifically commanding qada for every missed prayer.
B) The original command to perform the prayer, which remains effective after the time passes.
C) The consensus of the Companions that qada is always required.
D) Rational necessity, independent of any textual evidence.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that the original command implies qada is grounded in the continuity of obligation and the nature of the command as applying to the act in itself, not merely its time.

The Cause of Qada: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Vowed I'tikaf
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i objection on qada of vowed i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that qada of a vowed i'tikaf requires an intentional supererogatory fast, and evaluate the Shafi'i objection based on the concept of tafwit.

Core Idea
The cause of qada is loss (tafwit), not the original vow, so conditions may change in make-up.

This lesson examines a famous usul dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is over the nature of make-up (qada) for a vowed i'tikaf that was missed in Ramadan. The Shafi'is argue that qada must be identical to the original obligation, since both arise from the same vow (ayat 22:29). The Hanafis disagree, using the principle that the cause of qada is the loss of the act (tafwit), which is unrestricted, allowing the condition of fasting to revert to its full requirement.

Guided Path
1
1. State the Hanafi ruling on qada for a vowed i'tikaf missed in Ramadan.
Identify the ruling: qada is performed with an intentional supererogatory fast, not in another Ramadan. Note that the fast must be intentional (supererogatory) because the condition of i'tikaf (fasting) must be fulfilled deliberately.
The original obligation in Ramadan combined the fast of Ramadan with i'tikaf due to the virtue of Ramadan.
2
2. Identify the Shafi'i objection and their proof.
The Shafi'is (and Zufar and Abu Yusuf in one view) argue that the cause of both original obligation and qada is the vow (nadhr) commanded in ayat 22:29. Therefore, qada should be identical to the original: either valid in another Ramadan (Zufar) or dropped entirely (Abu Yusuf).
The ayat 'وَلْيُوفُوا نُذُورَهُمْ' is their dalil.
3
3. Locate the Hanafi response: the cause of qada is tafwit, not the original vow.
The author states that the cause of qada is tafwit (loss of the act), which is unrestricted with respect to time. Since the original obligation included the virtue of Ramadan as an interfering factor, in qada that factor is absent, so the condition of fasting returns to its full requirement (intentional fast).
Tafwit is a separate cause, not bound by the original vow's conditions.
4
4. Understand the role of the virtue of Ramadan in the original obligation.
The original i'tikaf in Ramadan was valid even without an intentional fast because the mere fast of Ramadan sufficed. In qada, the virtue of Ramadan is lost, so the fast must be intentional (supererogatory) to fulfill the condition of i'tikaf.
This shows that conditions may change in qada due to different circumstances.
5
5. Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
The practical difference: Hanafi says qada with supererogatory fast; Shafi'i says either in another Ramadan or no qada. This affects how a mufti advises someone who missed a vowed i'tikaf due to illness.
The Hanafi position is upheld by the author's reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حكم الواجب بالأمر ثم ههنا سؤال مشهور لهم علينا وهو: أنه إن نذر أحد أن يعتكف شهر رمضان فصام ولم يعتكف لمرض منع من الاعتكاف لا يقضي اعتكافه في رمضان آخر، بل يقضيه في ضمن صومٍ مقصود وهو صوم النفل، ولو كان القضاء واجبًا بالسبب الذي أوجب الأداء وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيُوفُوا نُذُورَهُمْ﴾ لوجب أن يصح القضاء في الرمضان الثاني كما هو مذهب زفر له، أو يسقط القضاء أصلاً؛ لعدم الأداء في الرمضان الأول كما هو مذهب أبي يوسف له، فعلم أن سبب القضاء التفويت والتفويت مطلق عن الوقت فينصرف إلى الكامل وهو الصوم المقصود. فأجاب المصنف له عنه بقوله: وفيما إذا نذر أن يعتكف شهر رمضان فصام ولم يعتكف إنما وجب القضاء بصوم مقصود؛ لعود شرطه إلى الكمال لا لأن القضاء وجب بسبب آخر وهو التفويت. يعني في صورة نذر أن يعتكف هذا الرمضان المعهود، فصام ولم يعتكف لمانع مرض إنما وجب القضاء بصوم مقصود وهو النفل؛ لعود شرط الاعتكاف إلى الكمال، وهو صوم النفل لا لأن القضاء وجب بسبب آخر كما زعمتم. وتقريره أن الاعتكاف لا يصح إلا بالصوم، فإذا نذر بالاعتكاف، فقد نذر بالصوم، فكان ينبغي أن يجب الصوم المقصود ابتداء بمجرد نذر الاعتكاف، ولكن شرف الرمضان الحاضر عارضه؛ لأن العبادة في رمضان أفضل من العبادة.
Statement on the ruling of the wajib by command: Then here is a famous objection they raise against us: that if someone vows to observe i'tikaf in the month of Ramadan, then fasts but does not observe i'tikaf due to illness preventing i'tikaf, he does not make up his i'tikaf in another Ramadan, but rather makes it up within an intentional fast, which is supererogatory fasting. If the make-up were obligatory by the same cause that obliged the performance—namely His statement, 'And let them fulfill their vows'—then it would be necessary that the make-up be valid in the second Ramadan, as is the position of Zufar, or that the make-up be dropped entirely due to non-performance in the first Ramadan, as is the position of Abu Yusuf. So it is known that the cause of make-up is loss (tafwit), and loss is unrestricted with respect to time, so it turns to the complete (form), which is intentional fasting. The author replied to him by saying: In the case where one vows to observe i'tikaf in Ramadan, then fasts and does not observe i'tikaf, make-up is only obligated with an intentional fast because its condition returns to perfection, not because the make-up became obligatory by another cause—namely loss. That is, in the scenario of vowing this specific Ramadan, then fasting and not observing i'tikaf due to an illness preventing it, make-up is only obligated with an intentional fast, which is supererogatory fasting, because the condition of i'tikaf returns to perfection—namely supererogatory fasting—not because make-up became obligatory by another cause as you claimed. Its explanation is that i'tikaf is not valid except with fasting, so when one vows i'tikaf, he has vowed fasting, so it would have been necessary that intentional fasting be obligated initially merely by the vow of i'tikaf, but the honor of the present Ramadan interfered because worship in Ramadan is superior to worship (in other times).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is concerning the nature of qada (make-up) for a vowed i'tikaf. The Shafi'is object that if someone vows to perform i'tikaf in Ramadan, but due to illness cannot observe i'tikaf, the Hanafis rule that the make-up must be accompanied by an intentional fast (supererogatory), not merely the fast of another Ramadan. The Shafi'is argue that the cause of obligation is the vow (ayat 22:29), so the make-up should be identical to the original—either valid in another Ramadan (Zufar's view) or dropped entirely (Abu Yusuf's view). The Hanafi author responds by clarifying that the cause of make-up is not the original vow but the loss (tafwit) of the act, and loss is unrestricted with respect to time. The original obligation combined the fast of Ramadan with i'tikaf because of the virtue of Ramadan. In make-up, that virtue is absent, so the condition (shart) of i'tikaf—fasting—must be fulfilled by an intentional fast (supererogatory) to achieve the requisite perfection. Thus, the make-up requires a distinct intentional fast, not merely the fast of another Ramadan. This reasoning relies on the principle that obligations may change in qada due to circumstances.

Key Terms
الواجب بالأمر (al-wajib bi al-amr): An obligation that becomes obligatory by a command (amr), as opposed to being inherently obligatory.
القضاء (al-qada): The make-up of a missed obligatory act performed after its time.
التفويت (al-tafwit): Causing the loss of the act; the cause that necessitates qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the cause that obligates qada (make-up) for a missed vowed i'tikaf?
A) The original vow (nadhr) itself
B) The loss (tafwit) of the act
C) The verse 'fulfill your vows'
D) The virtue of Ramadan

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the cause of the original obligation (vow) and the cause of qada (tafwit), allowing conditions to change in make-up acts.

Ihtiyat as a Method: Extending Fidyah from Fasting to Prayer
Defends the Hanafi use of ihtiyat to extend fidyah from fasting to prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of ihtiyat to justify extending a textual ruling to a new case when the 'illa is ambiguous, and distinguish ihtiyat from qiyas.

Core Idea
When a Quranic ruling’s cause is unclear, ihtiyat (precaution) extends it to similar cases—this is not qiyas but a distinct Hanafi method.

The Hanafi school holds that if a person dies owing missed prayers and bequeaths fidyah, the heir must give fidyah for each prayer, analogous to fidyah for missed fasts. But is this based on strict analogy (qiyas) or something else? The passage reveals that it is based on ihtiyat (precaution), because the Quranic verse for fasting fidyah (Al-Baqarah 2:184) could be specific to fasting or could have a general cause (incapacity). To avoid missing an obligation, the Hanafis extend the ruling. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and shows how ihtiyat operates in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the implicit objection
The passage begins with an implicit question: Since fidyah for fasting is established by a text (2:184) that is 'ghayr ma’qul' (not rationally comprehensible), you should confine it to that text and not extend it to prayer. Recognize that this objection assumes that any extension must be qiyas.
‘Ghayr ma’qul’ means the text’s ruling is based on pure divine command, not on a readily understandable rationale.
2
Analyze the ambiguity of the Quranic text
The author points out that the verse (2:184) can be read in two ways: either the ruling is specific to fasting (khass) or it is based on a general cause (‘illa) of incapacity (ajz) that applies to both fasting and prayer. This ambiguity (ihtimal) is key.
This is a typical Hanafi approach: when a text is susceptible to multiple interpretations, they do not jump to qiyas but consider ihtiyat.
3
Understand ihtiyat as distinct from qiyas
Given the two probabilities, the Hanafis adopt ihtiyat (precaution), meaning they follow the safer option—extending the ruling to prayer—rather than making a formal qiyas. Ihtiyat is a method used when the scope of a text is uncertain, not a derivation of a new ruling from a known cause.
This distinguishes the Hanafi approach from other schools that might require a clear ‘illa for qiyas.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: with ihtiyat, fidyah for missed prayers is obligatory (mufta bihi). If one rejected ihtiyat and insisted on strict qiyas, fidyah would not be required because the text is non-reasoned. Thus, the debate has real impact on fatwa.
The passage also notes that the view of Muhammad ibn Muqatil (equating a day of prayer to a day of fast) is retracted; the relied-upon view is ihtiyat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجوب الفدية في الصلاة للاحتياط، جواب سؤال مقدر تقريره أن الفدية في الصوم للشيخ الفاني لما كانت ثابتة بنص غير معقول ينبغي أن تقتصروا عليه ولم تقيسوا عليه من مات وعليه صلاة مع أنكم قلتم إنه إذا مات وعليه صلاة وأوصى بالفدية يجب على الوارث أن يفدي بعوض كل صلاة ما يفدي لكل صوم على الأصح، فأجاب بأن الوجوب الفدية في قضاء الصلاة للاحتياط لا للقياس؛ وذلك لأن نص الصوم يحتمل أن يكون مخصوصا بالصوم، ويحتمل أن يكون معلومًا لعلة عامة توجد في الصلاة أعني العجز، فعند الاحتمالين أخذنا بالاحتياط في الصلاة تبعًا للصوم لا قياسًا. على الأصح أي على المذهب، وما روي عن محمد بن مقاتل من أن صلاة يوم بليلة كصوم يوم فمرجوع عنه. الصوم: أي النص الوارد في باب فدية الصوم للشيخ الفاني، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ يُطِيقُونَهُ فِدْيَةٌ طَعَامُ مسكين﴾ (البقرة: ١٨٤) أن يكون مخصوصاً إلخ أي يكون الحكم معلولاً بعلة خاصة بالصوم وهو العجز الخاص بالصوم أعني العجز فإن الصوم عبادة بدنية مقصودة، وهي من الخمس التي بني الإسلام عليها، فإذا عجز عن أدائه جعل الشرع الفدية خلفا له، وهذا موجود في الصلاة أيضًا.
And the obligation of fidyah in prayer is due to precaution (ihtiyat), in response to an implicit question whose formulation is that the fidyah in fasting for the decrepit old person is established by a text that is not rationally comprehensible, so they should confine themselves to it and not analogize from it to the one who dies owing prayers, while you have said that if someone dies owing prayers and bequeaths fidyah, it is obligatory upon the heir to give fidyah in exchange for each prayer just as he gives fidyah for each fast in the most correct view. So he answered that the obligation of fidyah in making up prayer is due to precaution, not analogy; because the text of fasting can be specific to fasting, and it can also be known that it has a general cause that exists in prayer, namely incapacity. So given the two probabilities, we took precaution in prayer following fasting, not analogy. 'On the most correct view' meaning the school's view. And what is narrated from Muhammad ibn Muqatil that 'a day's prayer like a day's fast' is retracted. 'Fasting' meaning the text that came in the chapter of fidyah of fasting for the decrepit old person, which is His statement the Exalted: 'And upon those who can afford it, a fidyah of feeding a poor person' (Al-Baqarah 2:184) 'It could be specific' etc. meaning that the ruling is caused by a cause specific to fasting, which is the special incapacity for fasting, I mean incapacity, for fasting is a physical worship that is one of the five pillars of Islam. When one is incapable of performing it, the Lawgiver made fidyah a substitute for it. And this also exists in prayer.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Hanafi ruling that fidyah is obligatory for missed prayers of a deceased person who bequeaths it, analogous to fidyah for missed fasts. The text addresses an implicit objection: Since the fidyah for fasting is established by a specific Quranic text (2:184) and is not rationally reasoned (ghayr ma'qul), it should be confined to that text and not extended to prayer. The response asserts that the ruling is not based on qiyas (pure analogy) but on ihtiyat (precaution). The reason is that the text about fasting fidyah is ambiguous: it could be specific to fasting, or it could be based on a general 'illa (cause) of incapacity (ajz) that applies to both fasting and prayer. Given this uncertainty, the Hanafi school adopts the cautious approach by extending the ruling to prayer in order to ensure the obligation is fulfilled. This is not qiyas but rather a precautionary measure following the same principle. The passage then clarifies the definition of 'al-shaykh al-fani' and confirms that the text in question is the verse from Surah al-Baqarah. It notes that the view of Muhammad ibn Muqatil (that a day's prayer equals a day's fast in fidyah) is retracted; the relied-upon view is the madhhab's position as stated.

Key Terms
فدية (fidyah): A compensatory payment (feeding a poor person) for missed acts of worship due to permanent incapacity
شيخ فاني (shaykh fani): A decrepit old person who is permanently unable to fast
عجز (ajz): Incapacity or inability to perform an act of worship
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precaution; adopting the safer legal option when there is ambiguity or conflicting probabilities

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is fidyah required for missed prayers of a deceased person who bequeaths it?
A) Because of a clear analogy (qiyas) between fasting and prayer.
B) Because of a specific Quranic text for prayer.
C) Because of precaution (ihtiyat) due to the possibility that the 'illa of incapacity applies to both.
D) Because of the consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, ihtiyat (precaution) is a distinct method used to extend a textual ruling when its scope is ambiguous—it is not a form of qiyas but a cautious application to avoid missing an obligation.

The Minimal Possible Ability: Condition for Obligation, Not Performance
Defines the minimal possible ability and its role in obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi concept of 'al-qudra al-mumkina al-adna', identify its role as a condition for the obligation of a command (wujub al-ada'), and distinguish it from actual ability required for performance.

Core Idea
Ability for obligation is the minimal presumed capacity; actual ability is for performance only.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar unpacks a critical principle in Hanafi usul: what kind of ability (qudra) is required before a person can be obligated to perform an act? The answer is not 'full ability' but the minimal possible ability—just enough time to perform four rak'ahs. This ability does not need to be actual; its mere presumption suffices. This distinction has direct consequences for cases at the edge of time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term and its category
The passage defines 'al-qudra al-mumkina al-adna' (minimal possible ability). It is a type of ability (qudra) that serves as a condition (shart) for the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'), not for performance itself. Note that it is the 'absolute' (mutlaq) type of ability, as opposed to 'complete' (kamil).
2
Understand the distinction between absolute and complete ability
The author divides ability into absolute (mutlaq) and complete (kamil). The absolute is the minimal ability that suffices for obligation; the complete includes ease. Focus on absolute: it is defined as the least by which one can perform the commanded act (e.g., time for four rak'ahs).
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The Quranic verse 2:286 is cited: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' This proves that taklif requires capacity (wus'), and the minimal ability is the lowest level of that capacity. The verse is a general (amm) text negating burden beyond capacity.
The wajh al-dalalah: negation of taklif beyond capacity implies that capacity is a condition; the minimal ability is the threshold.
4
Analyze the condition: presumption not actuality
The condition for obligation is not actual existence of the minimal ability but its presumption (tawahhum). The text says 'al-shartu tawahhumuhu la haqiqatahu'. Example: a boy reaching puberty at the end of Asr time is obligated because one presumes the time might extend to allow four rak'ahs.
This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) according to Abu Hanifa, overriding the strict qiyas.
5
Contrast with the opposing view (Zufar)
Zufar rejects this presumption and follows qiyas: if ability is actually absent, no obligation arises. The cause (sabab) of obligation is the time that accommodates prayer; if such time is lacking, neither performance nor qada is required. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence): under Abu Hanifa, if time does not extend, qada is required; under Zufar, no qada.

الاستطاعة
يسع
Section on the Specific. Explanation of the division of ability. Then he divided this ability into absolute and complete, saying: It is two types: absolute, i.e., the ability through which the servant is able, and it means soundness of instruments and causes, of two types: one is absolute, i.e., not restricted by the quality of ease and facility as in the following division, and it is the least by which the commanded person is able to perform what is incumbent upon him, and it is a condition in performing every command. That is, the absolute is the least by which the servant is able, and this amount of ability is a condition in performing every command, and the rest is extra. It is the amount that accommodates four rak'ahs of Zuhr. If he is content with this ability, it is called 'possible ability,' which the author called absolute. He should have said: absolute and restricted for proper comparison, or complete and deficient. And by adding the word 'least' there is a distinction between the divided and the division; because the divided is what the servant is able with, and the division is the least by which the servant is able. So the objection that the thing is divided into itself and something else does not arise. He restricted it to performing every command because qada' does not require this ability absolutely. The author (said): 'this ability' i.e., the ability through which the servant is able to perform what is incumbent. (Al-Qamar) 'what he is able' etc.: the word 'ma' is a metaphor for ability. (Al-Qamar) 'in performing' etc.: the annexed is elided, i.e., in the obligation of performing every command, i.e., something commanded, whether religious or financial, like prayer and zakat. We estimated the annexed because the apparent meaning of the author's words is incorrect, for this ability is a condition for the obligation of performance, not for performance itself, for the condition of performance is real ability, not this ability. (Al-Qamar) 'the least by which the servant is able': since it could be objected that they said provisions and mount in Hajj are from possible ability, while Hajj occurs without the mount as well, so provisions and mount are not the least by which the servant is able. Some added another restriction: in a manner free from hardship, and Hajj without mount occurs, but it is not free from hardship, so ponder. (Al-Qamar) 'condition' and obligation is an impossible burden, which is negated by His saying: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity' (2:286). (Al-Qamar) 'it': i.e., this amount, i.e., the least. (Al-Qamar) 'And by adding the word least' etc.: repelling an anticipated objection. Its explanation: here the divided becomes identical with the division, because the divided was the ability through which the servant is able, and the division is exactly it. He answered that it is not so, rather there is a difference between them by adding the word 'least' in the division and its absence in the divided. (Al-Sanabli) Page 137: Rather, if the required is the action. But if the required is the asking and sin, then that is not required. For one who owes a thousand prayers, it is said to him at the last moment: This prayer is obligatory upon you, and its effect appears in the obligation of bequeathing fidya and sin. The condition is its presumption, not its actuality. That is, the condition regarding this minimal possible ability is that it is presumed to exist, not actually existing. That is, it is not necessary that the time accommodating four rak'ahs exist actually at the moment; rather its presumption suffices. If this presumed thing actually occurs, by the time being extended from Allah's side, he performs it in it; otherwise its effect appears in qada'. So if a boy reaches puberty, or an infidel converts, or a menstruating woman becomes pure at the end of the time, prayer becomes obligatory upon him/her due to the presumption of extension at the end of the time by the stopping of the sun. Clarification: possible ability is a condition in qada' if the required from him is the action, i.e., performing the missed prayer, for requesting action without ability is not permissible as is obvious. But if the required from him is the bequeathing of fidya for the heir, that he should ransom after his death, and sin if he leaves the bequest of fidya, then that possible ability is not required. For one who owes a thousand prayers, it is said to him at the last moment: This prayer is obligatory upon you, while he is not able to perform at that time. So the fruit of this obligation is not the performance, but the bequeathing of fidya and sin upon failure to bequeath. Thus said Bahr al-Ulum (i.e., our master Abdul Ali). (Al-Qamar) The required action etc.: requesting action without ability is not permissible. For example, if prayer becomes obligatory in health standing, he makes it up in illness sitting; if it becomes obligatory in illness lying down, he makes it up in health standing, not lying down. It is known from this the condition of ability at the time when action is required; otherwise the ruling would be opposite. (Al-Sanabli) Al-Shart: i.e., the condition of obligation of performance. (Al-Qamar) Rather, its presumption suffices etc., because the ability on which taklif is based, i.e., actual, does not precede action, as known in the issue that its actuality is with the action, not before it, so ponder. (Al-Sanabli) Prayer becomes obligatory upon him. This with the Greatest Imam (Abu Hanifa) is istihsan. Zufar differed with him, and it is qiyas: He says ability to perform is actually nonexistent, and there is no basis for considering the possibility of ability arising by extension of time because this possibility is far-fetched and not suitable as a basis for taklif. And the cause of obligation of prayer is time, which the prayer fills, not any time, even if little. Then, at that time, performance is not obligatory, so qada' is not obligatory either because it is a substitute for it. (Al-Qamar) Due to the presumption of extension, i.e., as an honor, and the establishment of honor for humans is definitive, as said. (Al-Qamar) Al-Istita'a: capacity. Yasa': accommodates.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar explains the division of ability (qudra) that is a condition for the obligation of performing commands. The author states that ability is of two types: absolute (mutlaq) and complete (kamil) or deficient (qasir). The absolute ability is the minimal capacity (adnā) by which a person can perform what is required of him—for prayer, this is the amount of time needed for four rak'ahs. This minimal ability is a condition for the obligation (wujūb) of performing a command, not for the actual performance itself (which requires real ability). The commentary clarifies that this is derived from the Quranic verse 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity' (2:286).

The text then addresses a nuance: the condition is not actual existence of this ability but its presumption (tawahhum). For example, if a boy reaches puberty or an infidel converts or a menstruating woman becomes pure at the very end of the prayer time, they must pray because one presumes the time might extend. This is based on istihsan according to Abu Hanifa, while Zufar follows qiyas and says no obligation exists since the ability is not real. The fruit of this obligation may be the duty to bequeath fidya (ransom) if one cannot perform, and sin for neglecting that bequest.

The lesson thus defines a key usul concept—the role of capacity in taklif—and shows how differing views on the nature of ability (actual vs. presumed) lead to different fiqh rulings in edge cases.

Key Terms
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): أدنى ما يتمكن به العبد من أداء المأمور به، وهي شرط لوجوب الأداء لا للأداء
التوهم (al-tawahhum): اعتقاد إمكان وجود القدرة في المستقبل، وهو كافٍ في تحقق شرط الوجوب
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): ترك القياس للأخذ بما هو أرفق وأولى بالعدل، كما في إيجاب الصلاة عند توهم الامتداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
ما هو شرط وجوب الأداء عند الحنفية في الصلاة؟
A) القدرة الحقيقية على أداء الصلاة كاملة
B) القدرة الممكنة الأدنى التي تسع أربع ركعات
C) وجود الوقت الفعلي المتسع للصلاة
D) الصحة والبلوغ والعقل

Key Takeaway
The minimal possible ability (al-qudra al-mumkina al-adna) is a condition for the obligation of a command, and its presumption suffices; this is proven by Quran and supported by istihsan in edge cases.

Possible Capacity vs. Ease: Hanafi Criterion for Obligation
Usul dispute: threshold for obligation of Hajj and Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i criteria for capacity (qudra) in Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr and evaluate the Hanafi objection to the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Minimal possible capacity suffices for obligation; requiring complete ease is excessive and leads to absurdity.

This passage addresses a key usul dispute: what level of capacity triggers the obligation of Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr? The Hanafi school adopts the criterion of 'possible capacity' (qudra mumkina) — minimal means without hardship. The Shafi'i school, however, holds that mere surplus food beyond one day's need suffices for Fitr. The text presents the Hanafi position, the Shafi'i counter, and a powerful rebuttal exposing a logical absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Position on Capacity
The Hanafi school holds that permissibility (jawaz) and obligation are established by possible capacity (qudra mumkina). For Hajj, this means minimal provisions and a mount; for Sadaqat al-Fitr, possession of nisab at the time of Eid. Note that ease (yusr) with abundant means is not required.
Qudra mumkina is the threshold; it does not require surplus wealth beyond the act itself.
2
Identify the Shafi'i Position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that for Sadaqat al-Fitr, anyone with surplus food beyond one day's need must give charity, even if they do not own nisab. This is based on a broader interpretation of capacity.
The Shafi'i criterion is broader and includes more people.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Rebuttal
The Hanafi response points out a logical flaw: if a person with only surplus food gives it as charity, he becomes needy and will ask for that same charity the next day. This reversal (qalb al-mawdu') contradicts the purpose of zakat, which is to prevent need.
The argument is based on maqasid (objectives) of the law.
4
Recognize the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The dispute results in different rulings: Hanafis require nisab for Fitr; Shafi'is obligate anyone with surplus food. The Hanafi position avoids the circularity that the Shafi'i position entails.
The tarjih favors the Hanafi view because of the absurd consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(القمر) بخدم بفتحتين جمع خادم كذا في "المنتخب". (القمر) قوتا: هو ما يقوم به بدن الإنسان من الطعام. (القمر) يلزم في هذا إلخ :توضيحه أنه لو لم يكن رجل مالكًا للنصاب، ويملك نصف صاع من بر مثلاً فارغا عن يومه، فهو حينئذ غني عن السؤال، فقادر على إغناء الفقير عن السؤال، فلو اعتبر هذا الغناء وأمر بإعطاء وصدقة الفطر كما هو عند الشافعي حه يلزم قلب الموضوع بأنه يعطى التوم الفقير هذا القدر، فيصير محتاجًا إلى السؤال، فيسأل من ذلك الفقير غدًا عين تلك الصدقة، وهذا لا يجوز؛ لأن دفع حاجته نفسه لئلا يحتاج إلى المسألة أولى من دفع حاجة الفقير كذا في شرح "الحسامي". (القمر)
Statement of establishing the attribute of permissibility for the commanded act and its absence. And because Hajj is established by possible capacity; because the little provisions and one mount are the minimum by which a person can perform Hajj. As for ease, it requires many servants, mounts, different helpers, and much wealth. So when capacity is lost, Hajj remains in its state, and that appears in terms of sin and bequest. Likewise, Zakat al-Fitr is established by possible capacity; do you not see that annual passage and growth are not required for it? Rather, if the nisab perishes on the day of Eid, the charity is still obligatory. So when this nisab is lost, the obligation remains upon him. According to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him: Everyone who possesses surplus food beyond his day must give charity, and possession of nisab is not required. We said: This leads to a reversal of the subject, that he gives charity today and then asks for that same charity from him tomorrow. Statement of establishing the attribute of permissibility for the commanded act and its absence. Then when the author finished explaining the goodness of the commanded act, he began explaining its permissibility. It was said about it: The requirement of provisions and other things for Hajj indicates that it is established by easy capacity, because possible capacity is sufficient by mere imagination, while in Hajj and Zakat al-Fitr actual possession is a condition. So how can it be from possible capacity? (al-Sanabili) It is established because the condition for Hajj is capability itself, as Allah said: 'Whoever is able to find a way to it' (Al-Imran 97). And capability for one far from the Kaaba is only through provisions and mount; these are necessities for such travel according to the norm. Their requirement is to indicate minimum ability without hardship usually, not for ease. As in Sharh al-Husami. (al-Qamar) 'Bikhidam' with two fathas is plural of 'khadim' (servant). (al-Qamar) 'Qutan' is what sustains the human body from food. (al-Qamar) 'It leads to reversal' etc.: Its clarification: If a man does not own the nisab, but owns half a sa' of wheat, for example, beyond his day's need, he is then wealthy enough not to ask, able to enrich the poor from asking. If this wealth is considered and he is ordered to give Zakat al-Fitr, as according to al-Shafi'i, it leads to a reversal: he gives this amount to the poor today, then becomes needy and asks, so he asks from that poor person tomorrow the very same charity. This is not permissible, because fulfilling his own need so he does not need to ask is more important than fulfilling the poor's need. As in Sharh al-Husami. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This is a discussion of the principle that permissibility (jawaz) of an act is established by the capacity (qudra) of the person. The passage addresses the threshold for obligation of Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr. The Hanafi position is that minimal possible capacity suffices: for Hajj, one mount and provisions, and for Sadaqat al-Fitr, possession of nisab (wealth) at the time. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that for Fitr, anyone with surplus food beyond the day's need is obligated, even without nisab. The Hanafi response points out that this leads to a practical absurdity: a person gives charity from his surplus, becomes needy, and then asks for that same charity back the next day. The passage also includes commentary clarifying that the condition for Hajj is capability (istita'ah) as in the Quranic verse (Al-Imran 97), which is interpreted by Hanafis as minimal means without hardship, not ease (yusr). The text thus defends the Hanafi criterion of 'possible capacity' (qudra mumkina) against the Shafi'i criterion.

Key Terms
قدرة ممكنة (qudra mumkina): Minimal capacity that enables performance without excessive hardship.
يسر (yusr): Complete ease with abundant means.
قلب الموضوع (qalb al-mawdu'): Reversal of the subject; a logical fallacy where the condition is inverted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Hanafi school consider sufficient for the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) Possession of any food surplus beyond the day's need.
B) Possession of nisab at the time of Eid.
C) Possession of nisab and annual passage.
D) Ability to afford both provisions and mount.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses minimal possible capacity (qudra mumkina) as the threshold for obligation, rejecting the requirement of complete ease (yusr).

Disbelievers and Obligations That Can Be Dropped: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on disbelievers and dropable obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which obligations disbelievers are addressed with according to the Hanafi school and apply the hadith of Mu'adh as evidence for the distinction between dropable and non-dropable obligations.

Core Idea
Disbelievers are addressed with faith, not with acts that can drop like prayer.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text tackles a critical question: Are disbelievers obligated to perform Islamic acts of worship in this world? The answer hinges on a unique Hanafi criterion—whether the obligation can be dropped from a Muslim due to excuses. By examining the famous hadith of Mu'adh, the author establishes that only faith and non-dropable obligations are demanded from disbelievers. This lesson will guide you through the textual evidence, the rational argument, and the practical consequence of this view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Locate the key phrase 'ma yahtamil al-suqut' (what can be dropped). The author argues that disbelievers are not addressed with such obligations (e.g., prayer, fasting) because these can drop from Muslims due to menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or continuous insanity.
This is the crux of the Hanafi position.
2
Analyze the proof from the hadith
Read the hadith of Mu'adh quoted in the text. The Prophet first calls to the shahada (faith), then to prayer, then to zakat. Note the sequential order—obligations follow faith. The author argues this shows that taklif (address) with acts of worship is conditional upon faith.
The hadith is the primary dalil (Sunnah ahad, zanni thubut but qati dalala according to the text).
3
Understand the rational argument (sirr)
The commentary explains the inner reason: the command to worship aims at reward, and a disbeliever is not worthy of reward. The objection that reward is conditional on performing with conditions is addressed—the condition of faith is missing.
This rational argument (talil) reinforces the textual proof.
4
Distinguish the Hanafi view from the opposing view
The passage mentions an opposing position (apparently Mu'tazila) that holds disbelievers are addressed with all obligations and punished for abandoning them. Note the thamarah (practical difference): Hanafis punish for disbelief, the opposition punishes for abandoning prayer as well.
The text sides with the Hanafi view as 'al-madhab al-sahih' and the majority of Transoxiana scholars.
5
Apply the distinction to a hypothetical case
Suppose a non-Muslim dies without having prayed. Under the Hanafi view, he is punished only for disbelief, not for abandoning prayer. Under the opposing view, he would be punished for both. Verify how the criterion of 'dropability' leads to this conclusion.
This shows the legal consequences (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute.

Source Text

بيان موجب الأمر في حق الكفار في الدنيا لما عُذِّبوا في الآخرة بتركها هذا غاية ما قيل في "التلويح" في تحقيق هذا المقام. والصحيح أنهم لا يخاطبون بأداء ما يحتمل السقوط من العبادات أي المذهب الصحيح لنا: أن الكفار لا يخاطبون بأداء العبادات التي تحتمل السقوط مثل الصلاة والصوم، فإنهما يسقطان عن أهل الإسلام بالحيض والنفاس ونحوهما؛ لقوله علي المعاذ حين بعثه إلى اليمن: "التأتي قوما من أهل الكتاب، فادعهم إلى شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأنّي رسول الله، فإن هم أطاعوك فأعلمهم أنّ
الله فرض عليهم خمس صلوات في كل يوم وليلة الحديث، فإنه تصريح بأنهم لا يكلفون بالعبادات إلا بعد الإيمان، وأما الإيمان فلما لم يحتمل السقوط من أحد لا جرم كانوا مخاطبين به.
في الآخرة هذا على مذهبه لا على مذهبنا؛ لأنهم يؤاخذون عنده بترك فعل الصلاة، وعندنا على ترك الاعتقاد.

(القمر) ونحوهما كالجنون المستوعب وسيجيء التفصيل في آخر الكتاب. (القمر) لتأتي قوما إلخ روى الترمذي عن ابن عباس أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعث معاذا إلى اليمن، فقال: إنك تأتي قوماً أهل الكتاب فادعهم إلى شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأنى رسول الله، فإن هم أطاعوا لذلك فأعلمهم أن الله افترض عليهم خمس صلوات في اليوم والليلة فإن هم أطاعوا لذلك فأعلمهم أن الله افترض عليهم صدقة أموالهم تؤخذ من أغنيائهم وترد على فقرائهم، فإن هم أطاعوا لذلك فإياك وكرائم أموالهم، واتق دعوة المظلوم، فإنها ليس بينها وبين الله حجاب". والمراد بقوله: "فإياك وكرائم"، أي اتق كرائم أموالهم أي نفائسها التي تتعلق بها نفس مالكها كذا في "مجمع البحار". (القمر)
لا يكلفون :إلخ والسرّ فيه أن الأمر بالعبادة لنيل الثواب على فعلها، والكافر ليس بأهل الثواب؛ لأنه إحسان وفضل لا يليق بالكافر وأجيب عنه بأن الأمر بالعبادة لنيل الثواب على تقدير الإتيان مع الشرائط، ولاستحقاق العقاب على تقدير الترك، فالكفار إن أتوا بالمأمور به بتحصيل شرائطه فيثابوا، وإلا فلهم العقاب، وعدم أهليتهم للثواب إنما هو على تقدير عدم تحصيل الشرط أعني الإيمان ولا كلام فيه تدبر. (القمر)
بعد الإيمان لأن الحديث صريح بأن وجوب أداء الشرائع تفريع يترتب على الإجابة بالإيمان. (المحشي) أخرجه البخاري في صحيحة : رقم ١٤٢٥ ، باب أخذ الصدقة من الأغنياء، وترد إلى الفقراء حيث كانوا، ومسلم رقم: ۱۹ ، باب الدعاء إلى الشهادتين وشرائع الإسلام والنسائي رقم ٢٤٣٥ ، باب وجوب الزكاة، وأبو داود رقم: ١٥٨٤ ، باب في زكاة السائمة ،والترمذي رقم: ٦٢٥ ، باب في كراهية أخذ خيار المال في الصدقة وابن ماجه رقم: ۱۷۸۳ ، باب فرض الزكاة، وأحمد في مسنده رقم: ۲۰۷۱، عن ابن عباس ها،
Statement of the implication of the command regarding disbelievers in this world when they are punished in the Hereafter for abandoning it. This is the utmost that has been said in al-Talwih in investigating this point. And the correct view is that they are not addressed with performing what may be dropped from acts of worship. That is, the correct madhhab for us is that disbelievers are not addressed with performing acts of worship that may be dropped such as prayer and fasting, for they are dropped from Muslims due to menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and the like; due to his statement to Mu'adh when he sent him to Yemen: 'You will come to a people from the People of the Book, so call them to testify that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah. If they obey you in that, then inform them that Allah has obligated upon them five prayers in every day and night' — the hadith. For it is explicit that they are not charged with acts of worship except after faith. As for faith, since it cannot drop from anyone, they are indeed addressed with it. In the Hereafter, this is according to his [al-Tawdih's] madhhab, not ours; because according to him they are taken to account for abandoning the act of prayer, while according to us for abandoning belief. (al-Muhashi) 'with performing what may be dropped': he restricted it thus; because they are addressed with performing what cannot be dropped like faith by agreement. (al-Qamar) The correct madhhab is the madhhab of the generality of the shaykhs of Transoxiana. (al-Qamar) 'and the like' like continuous insanity, and the detail will come at the end of the book. (al-Qamar) 'you will come to a people etc.' — al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that the Messenger of Allah sent Mu'adh to Yemen and said: 'You will come to a people from the People of the Book, so call them to testify that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah. If they obey you in that, inform them that Allah has obligated upon them five prayers in the day and night. If they obey you in that, inform them that Allah has obligated upon them charity from their wealth, taken from their rich and given to their poor. If they obey you in that, beware of their precious property, and fear the supplication of the oppressed, for between it and Allah there is no veil.' And the meaning of his saying 'beware of their precious' is: fear their precious properties, i.e., their valuables to which their owners' souls cling, as in Majma' al-Bihar. (al-Qamar) 'They are not charged etc.' — the secret in it is that the command to worship is to attain reward for doing it, and the disbeliever is not worthy of reward because it is a favor and grace not befitting a disbeliever. And it was answered that the command to worship is for attaining reward on condition of performing it with conditions, and for deserving punishment on condition of abandoning it. So if the disbelievers perform the commanded act by fulfilling its conditions, they are rewarded; otherwise they have punishment. And their lack of worthiness for reward is only on the condition of not fulfilling the condition, i.e., faith; there is no speech in it, ponder. (al-Qamar) 'after faith' because the hadith is explicit that the obligation of performing the laws is a branch that depends on responding with faith. (al-Muhashi) It was recorded by al-Bukhari in his Sahih: no. 1425, chapter on taking charity from the rich and returning it to the poor wherever they are; Muslim no. 19, chapter on calling to the two testimonies and the laws of Islam; al-Nasa'i no. 2435, chapter on obligation of zakat; Abu Dawud no. 1584, chapter on zakat of grazing animals; al-Tirmidhi no. 625, chapter on disliking taking the best of wealth in charity; Ibn Majah no. 1783, chapter on obligation of zakat; Ahmad in his Musnad no. 2071, from Ibn 'Abbas, end.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and proof from the Hanafi usul al-fiqh tradition. The author clarifies the correct Hanafi position (madhhab) regarding whether disbelievers (kuffar) are addressed (mukhatabun) with the obligations (takalif) of Islam in this world. The key distinction is between obligations that can be dropped (ma yahtamil al-suqut) and those that cannot. Acts like prayer and fasting can drop from Muslims due to menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or continuous insanity, so they are not demanded from disbelievers. However, faith (iman) cannot drop from anyone, so disbelievers are addressed with it. The author cites the well-known hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal as proof, where the Prophet (s.a.w.) enjoined calling to the shahada first, then prayer, then zakat, showing that obligations follow faith. The commentary by al-Qamar (likely the commentator) and al-Muhashi further explain the reasoning, addressing potential objections and noting that the correct madhhab is that of the majority of scholars of Transoxiana. The passage also touches on a difference of opinion about punishment in the Hereafter: according to some (possibly the Mu'tazila), disbelievers are punished for abandoning acts like prayer, while according to the Hanafis, they are punished for abandoning belief, not the acts themselves.

Key Terms
ما يحتمل السقوط (ma yahtamil al-suqut): Obligations that can be dropped from a person due to valid excuses such as menstruation, postpartum bleeding, continuous insanity, etc.
تكليف (taklif): Addressing someone with a legally binding command or prohibition.
المذهب الصحيح (al-madhab al-sahih): The correct school opinion, here referring to the Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why are disbelievers not addressed with the obligation of prayer?
A) Because prayer was only revealed to Muslims, not to previous nations.
B) Because prayer can be dropped from Muslims due to excuses like menstruation, and thus it is not demanded from disbelievers.
C) Because disbelievers do not have the physical ability to pray.
D) Because the command to pray is only for those who have already believed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between obligations that can be dropped (like prayer) and those that cannot (like faith); disbelievers are only addressed with the latter.

Definition and Ruling of Mutashabih and the Dispute over its Ta'wil
Definition and dispute over ta'wil of mutashabih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mutashabih, state the Hanafi ruling regarding its ta'wil, and evaluate the dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the interpretation of Quran 3:7.

Core Idea
Mutashabih verses are known only to Allah; scholars affirm faith without knowing the true interpretation.

This passage defines mutashabih (ambiguous verses) and explains the Hanafi position that only Allah knows their true interpretation (ta'wil). The 'rasikhun fi al-ilm' (those firmly rooted in knowledge) simply affirm faith and submit. The core of the passage is the linguistic dispute over Quran 3:7: does the phrase 'wa al-rasikhun' indicate that scholars also know the ta'wil, or is it a separate statement of their submission? We will walk through the Hanafi argument and its response to the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Define mutashabih and its ruling
Identify the technical definition: mutashabih is that from which hope of knowing the intended meaning is cut off. The ruling is to believe it is true without knowing the specifics until the Day of Resurrection.
The Prophet ﷺ knew the meanings; this does not apply to the ummah.
2
Identify the contested issue
The dispute: Do the rasikhun (scholars) know the ta'wil of mutashabih verses? Hanafi: No. Shafi'i/Mu'tazila: Yes, speculatively.
This affects whether speculative interpretation (ta'wil zanni) is permitted.
3
Locate the primary dalil
Quran 3:7 is the key verse. Both schools use it. Identify the exact wording and the point of contention: the conjunction 'wa' and the pause before 'al-rasikhun'.
The Hanafi position relies on a pause (waqf) at 'illa Allah'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation
Hanafis stop at 'illa Allah' and treat 'wa al-rasikhun' as a new subject. They support this with variant readings (without waw) and context (following mutashabihat is blameworthy).
The phrase 'yaquluna amanna bihi' shows their submission, not knowledge.
5
Contrast the Shafi'i interpretation and evaluate
Shafi'is conjoin 'wa al-rasikhun' to 'Allah', making them know. Hanafi response: this would allow speculative knowledge, but the verse emphasizes exclusivity of knowledge and testing through submission.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi prohibits definitive ta'wil; Shafi'i permits speculative ta'wil.

تعريف المتشابه وحكمه
وأما المتشابه فهو اسم لما انقطع رجاء معرفة المراد منه، ولا يرجى بدوه أصلاً، فهو في غاية الخفاء بمنزلة المحكم في غاية الظهور، فصار كرجل مفقود عن بلده وانقطع أثره، وانقضى أقرانه وجيرانه.
أي مات
وحكمه اعتقاد الحقية قبل يوم الإصابة أي اعتقاد أن المراد به حق وإن لم نعلمه قبل يوم القيامة، وأما بعد القيامة فيصير مكشوفا لكل أحد إن شاء الله تعالى، وهذا في حق الأمة،
وأما في حق النبي عليه، فكان معلومًا وإلا تبطل فائدة التخاطب، ويصير التخاطب
بالنبي
灶
بالمهمل كالتكلم بالزنجي مع العربي، وهذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي ليه وعامة المعتزلة: إن العلماء الراسخين أيضًا يعلمون تأويله.
ومنشأ الخلاف: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا يَعْلَمُ تَأْوِيلَهُ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَالرَّاسِحُونَ فِي الْعِلْمِ يَقُولُونَ آمَنَّا بِهِ ، (آل عمران:۷) فعندنا يجب الوقف على قوله إلا الله وقوله وَالرَّاسِخُونَ فِي الْعِلْمِ جملة مبتدأة؛ (آل عمران: ۷

ولا يرجى بدوه بدوه أصلاً: سواء كان عدم رجاء بدو المراد عارضيا كالمجمل الذي توفي النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بلا بيانه، أو ذاتيا

(القمر) أي اعتقاد أن المراد إلخ المراد بالاعتقاد الاعتقاد الإجمالي، فإنه يكون قبل الإصابة إلى المراد، وأما بعد الإصابة إلى المراد فيكون الاعتقاد تفصيلاً فاحفظه، ولا تكن مائلاً إلى ما يتوهم من ظاهر عبارة المصنف من أن بعد الإصابة إلى المراد لا يكون اعتقاد ما أصلاً. (القمر) بالزنجي مع العربي: أي باللسان الزنجي (أي لسان الحبش مع الرجل العربي (القمر) وهذا: أي انقطاع رجاء معرفة المراد من المتشابه. (القمر) جملة مبتدأة وليس معطوف على الله ؛ لأن الوقف على المعطوف عليه قبل ذكر المعطوف في موضع الاشتباه ممتنع عند القراء كذا قال بحر العلوم أي مولانا عبد العلي له. (القمر)

بيان المتقابلات للأقسام الأربعة السابقة
٢٦٢
تعريف المتشابه وحكمه
لأن الله تعالى جعل اتباع المتشابهات حطّ الزائغين، فيكون حظ الراسخين هو التسليم والانقياد ؛ ولقراءة البعض: الراسخون بدون الواو، والبعض ويقول الراسخون، وعند الشافعي له لا يوقف على قوله : إلا الله بل قوله والراسخون معطوف على قوله: الله، ويقول حال منه فيكون المعنى إلا الله والعلماء الراسخون في العلم، ولكن هذا نزاع قال : يعلم الراسخون تأويله يريدون يعلمون تأويله الظني، ومن قال:
لفظي؛ لأن
من
لا يعلمون الراسخون تأويله يريدون لا يعلمون التأويل الحق الذي يجب أن يعتقد عليه. فإن قلت: فما فائدة إنزال المتشابهات على مذهبكم؟ قلت: الابتلاء بالوقف والتسليم؛ لأن الناس على ضربين :ضرب بيتلون بالجهل فابتلاؤهم أن يتعلمون العلم، ويشتغلوا بالتحصيل،
لأن إلخ: دليل لوجوب الوقف على إلا الله (القمر) جعل إلخ حيث قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ زَيْغٌ فَيَتَّبِعُونَ
مَا تَشَابَهَ مِنْهُ ابْتِغَاءَ الْفِتْنَةِ وَابْتِغَاءَ تَأْوِيلِهِ وَمَا يَعْلَمُ إلى آخر الآية، (آل عمران:۷) والزيغ: الميل عن الحق إلى الباطل.(القمر) فيكون إلخ : قال صاحب "التلويح": وفيه نظر كما لا يخفى على الراسخين في العربية أنه لو قصد ذلك لكان الأليق بالنظم أن يقول الله تعالى: أما الراسخون في العلم إلخ ليستقيم مقابلته بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ (آل عمران: ٧) إلخ، أقول وبه نستعين أنه لا يخفى على الراسخين في العربية أنه جاء حذف أما اعتمادًا على
القرائن، فلو قيل بحذفها فلا حرج تأمل. (القمر) ولقراءة إلخ : معطوف على قوله: لأن الله تعالى إلخ. (القمر) والبعض : معطوف على البعض في قوله: ولقراءة البعض. معطوف إلخ ويأباه ما في قراءة ابن مسعود: وأن تأويله إلا عند الله، فإن لفظ الله مجرور، والراسخون مرفوع، فكيف يعطف عليه، وما في قراءة أبي: ويقول الراسخون إلخ، فإن لفظ الراسخون على هذه القراءة فاعل يقول . (القمر) حال منه: وضمير به راجع إلى الكتاب أو إلى المتشابه. (القمر) هذا: أي النزاع بيننا وبين الشافعي بأنا نقول: لا يعلم الراسخون تأويله وهو يقول: إنهم يعلمون . (القمر) يعلمون إلخ فإن الصحابة والتابعين عليه يفسرون متشابهات القرآن، وهذه التفسيرات كلها ظنية (القمر) لا يعلمون التأويل الحق إلخ في الصبح الصادق لكنه يرد أن مدعاهم لا يثبت، فإن المدعى أن المتشابه لا يدرك أصلاً والمنفى إنما هو العلم، فليجزأن يكون إدراك المتشابه من قبيل سائر الفروع الظنية الثابتة بالأقيسة وأخبار الآحاد (القمر) فما فائدة إلخ اعتراض من الشافعية على الحنفية بأنه إذا لم يكن للراسخين حظ في العلم بالمتشابهات فما فائدة إلخ.(القمر)
Statement of the contrasts for the four previous divisions. Definition of mutashabih and its ruling. 261. Definition of mutashabih and its ruling. As for mutashabih, it is a name for that from which hope of knowing the intended meaning is cut off, and its disclosure is not hoped for at all. So it is in extreme hiddenness, comparable to muhkam in extreme clarity. So it became like a man lost from his country, his trace cut off, and his contemporaries and neighbors have passed away. i.e., he died. Its ruling is to believe in its truth before the day of attainment, i.e., to believe that the intended meaning is true even if we do not know it before the Day of Resurrection. As for after the Resurrection, it becomes unveiled to everyone, Allah willing. This applies to the ummah. As for the Prophet, peace be upon him, it was known, otherwise the benefit of address would be nullified, and addressing the Prophet would be like speaking unintelligibly, like speaking Zanjī with an Arab. This is our view. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, and the general Mu'tazila said that the firmly rooted scholars also know its ta'wil. The source of the dispute is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And none knows its ta'wil except Allah and those firmly rooted in knowledge say: We believe in it' (Al 'Imran:7). According to us, it is necessary to stop at His saying 'except Allah', and His saying 'and those firmly rooted in knowledge' is a new sentence (mubtada'). ... because Allah Most High has made following the mutashabihat the lot of the deviators, so the lot of the firmly rooted is submission and compliance. And due to the recitation of some: 'al-rasikhun' without the waw, and some: 'and those firmly rooted say.' According to al-Shafi'i, one does not stop at His saying 'except Allah', rather His saying 'and those firmly rooted' is conjoined to His saying 'Allah', and 'they say' is a circumstantial clause from it, so the meaning is 'except Allah and the scholars firmly rooted in knowledge.' But this is a verbal dispute. Some said: the firmly rooted know its ta'wil, meaning they know its speculative ta'wil. And whoever said: they do not know its ta'wil, means they do not know the true interpretation which must be believed in. If you say: What is the benefit of revealing the mutashabihat in your view? I say: The test of stopping and submission; because people are of two types: a type tested by ignorance, so their test is to learn knowledge and occupy themselves with acquisition. ...
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul sharh (likely on Noor al-Anwar) defines mutashabih (ambiguous verses) and explains the Hanafi position that only Allah knows the true ta'wil (interpretation) of such verses, while the 'rasikhun fi al-ilm' (those firmly rooted in knowledge) simply affirm faith in them. The author first defines mutashabih as that which cannot be understood in this life, using the analogy of a lost man. The ruling is to believe in its truth without knowing the specifics. The Prophet, however, knew the meanings. The core of the passage is the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i and the Mu'tazila, who hold that the rasikhun also know the ta'wil. The source of dispute is the ayah in Surah Al 'Imran (3:7). Hanafis interpret the structure by pausing at 'illa Allah' and treating 'wa al-rasikhun' as a new subject, meaning they do not know but only say 'we believe'. Shafi'is see 'wa al-rasikhun' as conjoined to 'Allah', meaning they too know. The author provides linguistic arguments for the Hanafi position, including variant readings and the purpose of testing. The passage concludes with an objection from the Shafi'is about the benefit of revealing ambiguous verses, answered by the Hanafi point about testing through submission. The authority weight is typical of Hanafi usul works; this is a standard Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Key Terms
المتشابه (al-mutashabih): That from which hope of knowing the intended meaning is cut off, and its disclosure is not hoped for at all.
الراسخون في العلم (al-rasikhun fi al-ilm): Those firmly rooted in knowledge, i.e., the scholars.
التأويل (al-ta'wil): The interpretation or final meaning of a verse, especially of mutashabih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, the Quranic phrase 'wa al-rasikhun fi al-ilm yaquluna amanna bihi' indicates that the rasikhun:
A) know the ta'wil of mutashabih verses.
B) affirm faith in mutashabih verses without knowing the specific ta'wil.
C) are not required to believe in mutashabih verses.
D) only the Prophet knew the ta'wil; others have no access.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the true interpretation of mutashabih verses is known only to Allah; the scholars' role is to submit and affirm faith in them without speculating on the exact meaning.

The Verbal Contextual Indicator (Qarinat Siyaq al-Nazm)
Explains first type of qarina: dalaalat siyaq al-nazm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a qarinat siyaq al-nazm in a legal text and apply it to derive a metaphorical interpretation.

Core Idea
A verbal contextual indicator can override the literal meaning and redirect to a metaphorical one.

In usul al-fiqh, the literal meaning (haqiqah) is the default presumption for any word. However, when the flow of the text (siyaq) contains a verbal indicator that conflicts with the literal sense, the interpreter must adopt the metaphorical meaning (majaz). This lesson explores the first type of qarina: the contextual indicator derived from the verbal structure itself, with examples from the Quran and legal statements.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the default use of haqiqah
Start with the presumption that words carry their literal meanings unless a contextual indicator (qarina) suggests otherwise. In the examples, note the literal meaning of 'uff' (annoyance) and 'take agency' (tawkil) and 'volition' (mashi'a).
The default is haqiqah, but a qarina can shift to majaz.
2
Identify the presence of a verbal qarina
Look for verbal cues in the text—such as a condition (e.g., 'if you are a man') or the broader context of honoring parents (for 'uff')—that indicate the literal meaning is not intended. These cues are the qara'in.
The qarina can be a preceding or following part of the text (sabiq or muta'akhkhir).
3
Determine how the qarina overrides the literal meaning
Explain why the literal meaning is impossible or inappropriate given the qarina. For example, in 'So do not say to them 'uff'' (17:23), the context of honoring parents shows that the prohibition is not merely against saying 'uff' but against any form of annoyance, including hitting and reviling.
The shift is from a specific verbal annoyance to general disrespect, i.e., from haqiqah to majaz.
4
Apply the analysis to the Quranic and legal examples
Work through the two main examples: (1) 'Do not say to them 'uff'' → includes hitting/reviling due to the qarina of honoring parents. (2) 'Divorce my wife if you are a man' → the condition 'if you are a man' shows the statement is for rebuke, not actual agency to divorce.
The phrase 'if you are a man' is a clear verbal qarina that changes the meaning from a literal empowerment to a sarcastic challenge.
5
Note the role of custom as a qarina in the fruit dispute
The passage discusses a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his students regarding whether grapes, fresh dates, and pomegranates are 'fruits' in an oath. Abu Hanifa followed the custom of his time (where these were not considered fruits), while the Sahibayn followed later custom. This shows that custom can function as a qarina to determine the intended meaning.
This exemplifies that qara'in can be extra-textual (like custom) but still affect interpretation.
