بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث
بيان قرائن العمل بالمجاز وترك الحقيقة
فيشتمله كاشتمال "أي" في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا تَقُلْ لَهُمَا أُفٍّ﴾ للضرب والشتم، بخلاف (الإسراء : ۲۳) زيادة العنب، فإنه مغير لمعنى التفكه ومضر، له وعندهما يحنث بذلك كله؛ لأنها من أعز الفواكه هذا إذا لم ينو، وأما إذا نوى ذلك يحنث اتفاقا
وبدلالة سياق النظم أي بسبب سوق الكلام بقرينة لفظية التحقت به سواء كانت سابقة أو متأخرة.
القرينة
كقوله: طلق امرأتي إن كنت رجلاً حتى لا يكون توكيلاً، فإن حقيقة هذا الكلام هو التوكيل بالطلاق لكن ترك ذلك بقرينة قوله : "إن كنت رجلاً؛ لأن هذا الكلام إنما يقال: أي إن كنت رجلاً عند إرادة إظهار عجز المخاطب عن الفعل الذي قرن به فيكون الكلام للتوبيخ مجازا،
ومثله قوله تعالى: فَمَنْ شَاءَ فَلْيُؤْمِنْ وَمَنْ شَاءَ فَلْيَكْفُرْ إِنَّا أَعْتَدْنَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ نَاراً حيث تركت (الكهف : ٢٩)
ولا تقل لهما : أي للوالدين ،أفٍ وهو صوت يدل على تضجر وقيل اسم الفعل الذي هو التضجر كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) للضرب والشتم متعلق بالاشتمال فالضرب والشتم مكملان لمعنى الإيذاء. (القمر) فإنه مغير لمعنى التفكه التلذذ والتنعم؛ لأن الغذاء مقصود ، والتفكه أمر زائد غير مقصود، فيكون مغيرا معنى التبعية كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) وعندهما يحنث إلخ : قيل: نقل هذا القول صاحب "التحقيق"إن هذا الاختلاف اختلاف عصر ،وزمان فأبو حنيفة له أفتى على عرف ،زمانه فإن أهل زمانه لا يعدونها أي العنب والرطب والرمان من الفواكه وتغير العرف في زمانهما (القمر) لأنها أي العنب والرطب والرمان. (القمر) أي بسبب سوق الكلام إيماء إلى أن السياق مصدر بمعنى السوق، فليس المراد بالسياق ههنا، ما يتعارف استعماله فيه، وهو المتأخر مقابلاً للسباق بالباء الموحدة بمعنى المتقدم، وكذا قال الشارح فيما سيأتي سواء كانت إلخ والمراد بالنظم الكلام . (القمر) سوق إشارة إلى كون السياق بمعنى السوق والنظم بمعنى الكلام. (المحشي) عند إشارة إلى أن هذا داخل في قرينته دلالة العادة (المحشي) فيكون الكلام للتوبيخ والمعنى: أنك لا تستطيع ولا تقدر على تطليق امرأتي فإنه من المعلوم القطعي امتناع قدرة الرجل على طلاق امرأة الغير فهذا مجاز من قبيل إطلاق اسم أحد الضدين على الآخر باعتبار أن الضدين متجاوران في الذهن حيث يستلزم تصور أحدهما تصور الآخر. (القمر) حيث تركت إلخ: فإن حقيقة المشيئة رفع الإثم، وقرينة السياق لا تناسبه، فإنها حاكمة بتحقق الإثم للظالمين أي الكافرين (القمر)
بيان قرائن العمل بالمجاز وترك الحقيقة
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث حقيقة المشيئة، وحقيقة قوله: "فَلْيَكْفُرُ" بقرينة قوله تعالى: وَأَعْتَدْنَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ نَاراً، وحمل فليكفر على التوبيخ. وبدلالة معنى يرجع إلى المتكلم ،وقصده فيحمل على الأخص مجازا وإن كان اللفظ دالا على العموم بحقيقته. كما في يمين الفور، وهو مشتق من فارت القدر إذا غلت واشتدت، ثم سميت به الحالة التي لا لبث فيها ولا ريث باعتبار فوران الغضب كما إذا أرادت امرأة الخروج فقال لها الزوج: "إن خرجت فأنتِ طالق" فمكثت ساعة حتى سكن غضبه ثم خرجت لا تطلق، فإن حقيقة هذا الكلام أن تطلق في كل ما خرجت ولكن معنى الغضب الذي حدث في المتكلم وقت خروجها يدل على أن المراد هي هذه الخرجة المعينة، فيحمل الكلام عليها مجازا بهذه القرينة، ومثله قول الرجل لأحد : تعال تغدّ معي، "فقال": "إن تغديت فعبدي" فإن حقيقته أن يعتق عبده أينما تغدي، سواء كان مع الداعي أو وحده في بيته،
وحقيقة قوله فليكفر إلخ وهي وجوب الكفر. (القمر) وقصده إلخ معطوف على قول المصنف معنى تفسيريا أي حال التكلم وقصده يدل على ترك الحقيقة. (القمر) كما في يمين الفور: هذا القسم من اليمين استخرجه الإمام بحديث، وهو أن جابرًا وابنه دعيا إلى نصرة ،إنسان فحلفا أن لا ينصراه ثم نصراه بعد ذلك و لم يحنثا، وكان القوم سابقًا يقولون اليمين مؤقتة نحو: "والله لا أفعل اليوم كذا" ومطلقة: نحو "والله لا أفعل كذا"، والإمام استخرج مؤقتة معنى مطلقة لفظًا كذا قال أعظم العلماء مولانا عبد السلام أعظمي له. (القمر) سميت إلخ : يقال: جاء فلان من فوره أي من ساعته. (القمر)
باعتبار إلخ أي إنما سميت هذا اليمين بيمين الفور لصدورها من المتكلم باعتبار فوران الغضب أي شدته. (القمر) يعتق عبده إلخ لأنه دال لغة على مصدر منكر واقع تحت النفي، فإن التقدير لا أتغدى تغديًا كذا قيل. (القمر) أينما تغدى إلخ أي حقيقة هذا الكلام العموم لدلالته لغة على مصدر منكر واقع في موضع النفي؛ إذا التقدير لا أتغدى تغديًا، فيقتضي أن يحنث بكل تغد يوجد بعد كما لو قاله ابتداء، وقد تركت بدلالة حال المتكلم؛ إذ من المعلوم أنه أخرج الكلام مخرج الجواب لكلام الداعي، فإنه قد دعاه إلى تغدي الغداء الذي بين يديه لا إلى غيره، فيتقيد به، وإذا تقيد كلام الداعي به تقيد الجواب به أيضًا؛ لأنه بناء عليه وصار كأنه قال: "والله لا أتغدى الغداء الذي دعوتني إليه"، وقس عليه ما سبق من قوله لامرأته حين قامت تريد الخروج: "إن خرجت فأنت طالق".(السنبلي)
Statement of the divisions of the third division. Statement of the contextual indicators for working with metaphor and leaving the literal meaning. It includes it like the inclusion of 'ay' in His statement: 'So do not say to them 'uff'' for hitting and reviling, unlike (al-Isra 17:23) adding grapes, for it changes the meaning of enjoyment and is harmful, and according to them both he breaks the oath by all that because they are among the most excellent fruits. This is if he did not intend; if he intended that, he breaks the oath unanimously. And by the indication of the flow of the text, i.e., due to the flow of speech with a verbal contextual indicator attached to it, whether it precedes or follows. The contextual indicator, like his statement: 'Divorce my wife if you are a man' so that it is not an agency. For the literal meaning of this statement is agency in divorce, but that is left due to the contextual indicator of his statement: 'if you are a man', because this statement is only said, meaning: if you are a man, when intending to show the addressee's inability to do the action linked to it. So the statement becomes for rebuke metaphorically. Similarly His statement: 'So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve; indeed We have prepared for the wrongdoers a Fire' (al-Kahf 18:29) where the literal meaning of volition is left. And by the indication of a meaning that refers to the speaker and his intent, it is taken metaphorically to the specific even if the word indicates generality in its literal sense. As in the oath of al-fawr, which is derived from 'the pot boiled' when it bubbles and becomes intense, then the state in which there is no delay and no hesitation is named after it, considering the boiling of anger. For example, when a woman wants to go out and her husband says: 'If you go out, you are divorced,' and she waits an hour until his anger subsides then goes out, she is not divorced. For the literal meaning of this statement is that she is divorced in every instance of going out, but the meaning of anger that occurred in the speaker at the time of her going out indicates that the intended is this specific outing, so the statement is taken metaphorically to it by this contextual indicator. Similarly, a man's statement to someone: 'Come, eat lunch with me,' and he said: 'If I eat lunch, my slave is free,' the literal meaning is that his slave becomes free wherever he eats lunch, whether with the inviter or alone in his house.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on usul al-fiqh explaining the types of contextual indicators (qara'in) that necessitate taking a metaphorical meaning (majaz) over the literal meaning (haqiqah). The author presents two main types: first, the indication of the flow/context of the text (siyaq al-nazm), which is a verbal contextual indicator attached to the speech, whether preceding or following. Examples include the Quranic verse 'So do not say to them 'uff'' (17:23), which literally indicates annoyance but is taken to include hitting and reviling due to the context of honoring parents. The second type is the indication of a meaning referring to the speaker's intent (ma'na al-mutakallim wa qasdihi), which causes the general word to be taken specifically. The key example is the oath of al-fawr (instantaneous oath), derived from a hadith of Jabir. If a husband says to his wife 'If you go out, you are divorced' while angry, and she waits for his anger to subside before going out, the oath is not triggered because the contextual indicator of his anger shows that he meant only that specific outing. Similarly, if a man is invited to eat and responds 'If I eat lunch, my slave is free,' the slave is only freed if he eats that specific lunch with the inviter, not if he eats elsewhere. The passage also discusses a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students regarding whether grapes, fresh dates, and pomegranates are considered fruits in oaths, attributed to change in custom. This illustrates the role of custom ('urf) as a contextual indicator. Throughout, the commentary follows the order of the matn, first explaining the qarina of text flow, then the qarina of speaker's intent, with detailed examples and cross-references.

Key Terms
القرينة (al-qarīnah): A contextual indicator (verbal or situational) that shows the intended meaning is metaphorical, not literal.
سياق النظم (siyāq al-nazm): The flow or sequence of the verbal text, which can serve as a qarina for shifting from literal to metaphorical meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary qarina that causes the literal meaning of 'do not say to them 'uff'' to be interpreted metaphorically as including hitting and reviling?
A) The literal meaning of 'uff' itself
B) The following threat of fire in the next verse
C) The broader context of honoring parents in the surrounding verses
D) The speaker's individual intention

Key Takeaway
Verbal contextual indicators (qarinat siyaq al-nazm) can override the literal meaning and redirect to a metaphorical interpretation, as seen in the Quranic and legal examples.

The Contextual Indicator of Speaker's Intent (Qarinat Ma'na al-Mutakallim)
Explains second type of qarina: dalaalat ma'na al-mutakallim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a qarinat ma'na al-mutakallim (speaker's intent indicator) and apply it to restrict a general condition to a specific instance.

Core Idea
The speaker's emotional state or specific purpose can serve as a qarina, restricting a general condition to a particular instance.

The second type of qarina is derived from the meaning that refers back to the speaker's intent (ma'na al-mutakallim wa qasdihi). Even if the words are general, the speaker's state—such as anger or a specific invitation—can indicate that the intended meaning is specific, not general. This lesson examines the classic case of yamin al-fawr (the impulsive oath) and the example of an invited meal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of yamin al-fawr
Yamin al-fawr is an oath made impulsively in a state of anger. The term 'fawr' derives from the bubbling of a pot, symbolizing the boiling of anger. This type of oath is interpreted restrictively because the speaker's anger shows he only meant the specific triggering situation.
The hadith of Jabir is the basis: he and his son swore not to help someone but later did so and were not held to have broken the oath because it was a fawr.
2
Apply the example of the angry husband
The husband says 'If you go out, you are divorced' while his wife is about to go out and he is angry. Literally, this condition applies to any future going out. But the qarina of his anger (a state of the speaker) shows he meant only that specific intended outing. If she waits until his anger subsides and then goes out, the divorce does not occur.
Anger is a qarina because it restricts the general condition to the immediate situation.
3
Apply the example of the invited meal
A man is invited to eat lunch and responds 'If I eat lunch, my slave is free.' Literally, this would free his slave wherever he eats lunch later. But the qarina of the invitation (the specific meal) shows he only meant that particular lunch with the inviter. If he eats elsewhere, the slave is not freed.
The inviter's invitation and the responder's reply are linked; the qarina of the context restricts the condition to that specific lunch.
4
Generalize the principle
Whenever a speaker's statement is accompanied by a clear state or purpose that conflicts with the literal generality, the interpreter must adopt the specific metaphorical meaning. This is a qarinat ma'na al-mutakallim.
This type of qarina is not verbal but inferred from the speaker's circumstances.

بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث
بيان قرائن العمل بالمجاز وترك الحقيقة
فيشتمله كاشتمال "أي" في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا تَقُلْ لَهُمَا أُفٍّ﴾ للضرب والشتم، بخلاف (الإسراء : ۲۳) زيادة العنب، فإنه مغير لمعنى التفكه ومضر، له وعندهما يحنث بذلك كله؛ لأنها من أعز الفواكه هذا إذا لم ينو، وأما إذا نوى ذلك يحنث اتفاقا
وبدلالة سياق النظم أي بسبب سوق الكلام بقرينة لفظية التحقت به سواء كانت سابقة أو متأخرة.
القرينة
كقوله: طلق امرأتي إن كنت رجلاً حتى لا يكون توكيلاً، فإن حقيقة هذا الكلام هو التوكيل بالطلاق لكن ترك ذلك بقرينة قوله : "إن كنت رجلاً؛ لأن هذا الكلام إنما يقال: أي إن كنت رجلاً عند إرادة إظهار عجز المخاطب عن الفعل الذي قرن به فيكون الكلام للتوبيخ مجازا،
ومثله قوله تعالى: فَمَنْ شَاءَ فَلْيُؤْمِنْ وَمَنْ شَاءَ فَلْيَكْفُرْ إِنَّا أَعْتَدْنَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ نَاراً حيث تركت (الكهف : ٢٩)
ولا تقل لهما : أي للوالدين ،أفٍ وهو صوت يدل على تضجر وقيل اسم الفعل الذي هو التضجر كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) للضرب والشتم متعلق بالاشتمال فالضرب والشتم مكملان لمعنى الإيذاء. (القمر) فإنه مغير لمعنى التفكه التلذذ والتنعم؛ لأن الغذاء مقصود ، والتفكه أمر زائد غير مقصود، فيكون مغيرا معنى التبعية كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) وعندهما يحنث إلخ : قيل: نقل هذا القول صاحب "التحقيق"إن هذا الاختلاف اختلاف عصر ،وزمان فأبو حنيفة له أفتى على عرف ،زمانه فإن أهل زمانه لا يعدونها أي العنب والرطب والرمان من الفواكه وتغير العرف في زمانهما (القمر) لأنها أي العنب والرطب والرمان. (القمر) أي بسبب سوق الكلام إيماء إلى أن السياق مصدر بمعنى السوق، فليس المراد بالسياق ههنا، ما يتعارف استعماله فيه، وهو المتأخر مقابلاً للسباق بالباء الموحدة بمعنى المتقدم، وكذا قال الشارح فيما سيأتي سواء كانت إلخ والمراد بالنظم الكلام . (القمر) سوق إشارة إلى كون السياق بمعنى السوق والنظم بمعنى الكلام. (المحشي) عند إشارة إلى أن هذا داخل في قرينته دلالة العادة (المحشي) فيكون الكلام للتوبيخ والمعنى: أنك لا تستطيع ولا تقدر على تطليق امرأتي فإنه من المعلوم القطعي امتناع قدرة الرجل على طلاق امرأة الغير فهذا مجاز من قبيل إطلاق اسم أحد الضدين على الآخر باعتبار أن الضدين متجاوران في الذهن حيث يستلزم تصور أحدهما تصور الآخر. (القمر) حيث تركت إلخ: فإن حقيقة المشيئة رفع الإثم، وقرينة السياق لا تناسبه، فإنها حاكمة بتحقق الإثم للظالمين أي الكافرين (القمر)
بيان قرائن العمل بالمجاز وترك الحقيقة
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث حقيقة المشيئة، وحقيقة قوله: "فَلْيَكْفُرُ" بقرينة قوله تعالى: وَأَعْتَدْنَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ نَاراً، وحمل فليكفر على التوبيخ. وبدلالة معنى يرجع إلى المتكلم ،وقصده فيحمل على الأخص مجازا وإن كان اللفظ دالا على العموم بحقيقته. كما في يمين الفور، وهو مشتق من فارت القدر إذا غلت واشتدت، ثم سميت به الحالة التي لا لبث فيها ولا ريث باعتبار فوران الغضب كما إذا أرادت امرأة الخروج فقال لها الزوج: "إن خرجت فأنتِ طالق" فمكثت ساعة حتى سكن غضبه ثم خرجت لا تطلق، فإن حقيقة هذا الكلام أن تطلق في كل ما خرجت ولكن معنى الغضب الذي حدث في المتكلم وقت خروجها يدل على أن المراد هي هذه الخرجة المعينة، فيحمل الكلام عليها مجازا بهذه القرينة، ومثله قول الرجل لأحد : تعال تغدّ معي، "فقال": "إن تغديت فعبدي" فإن حقيقته أن يعتق عبده أينما تغدي، سواء كان مع الداعي أو وحده في بيته،
وحقيقة قوله فليكفر إلخ وهي وجوب الكفر. (القمر) وقصده إلخ معطوف على قول المصنف معنى تفسيريا أي حال التكلم وقصده يدل على ترك الحقيقة. (القمر) كما في يمين الفور: هذا القسم من اليمين استخرجه الإمام بحديث، وهو أن جابرًا وابنه دعيا إلى نصرة ،إنسان فحلفا أن لا ينصراه ثم نصراه بعد ذلك و لم يحنثا، وكان القوم سابقًا يقولون اليمين مؤقتة نحو: "والله لا أفعل اليوم كذا" ومطلقة: نحو "والله لا أفعل كذا"، والإمام استخرج مؤقتة معنى مطلقة لفظًا كذا قال أعظم العلماء مولانا عبد السلام أعظمي له. (القمر) سميت إلخ : يقال: جاء فلان من فوره أي من ساعته. (القمر)

Statement of the divisions of the third division. Statement of the contextual indicators for working with metaphor and leaving the literal meaning. It includes it like the inclusion of 'ay' in His statement: 'So do not say to them 'uff'' for hitting and reviling, unlike (al-Isra 17:23) adding grapes, for it changes the meaning of enjoyment and is harmful, and according to them both he breaks the oath by all that because they are among the most excellent fruits. This is if he did not intend; if he intended that, he breaks the oath unanimously. And by the indication of the flow of the text, i.e., due to the flow of speech with a verbal contextual indicator attached to it, whether it precedes or follows. The contextual indicator, like his statement: 'Divorce my wife if you are a man' so that it is not an agency. For the literal meaning of this statement is agency in divorce, but that is left due to the contextual indicator of his statement: 'if you are a man', because this statement is only said, meaning: if you are a man, when intending to show the addressee's inability to do the action linked to it. So the statement becomes for rebuke metaphorically. Similarly His statement: 'So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve; indeed We have prepared for the wrongdoers a Fire' (al-Kahf 18:29) where the literal meaning of volition is left. And by the indication of a meaning that refers to the speaker and his intent, it is taken metaphorically to the specific even if the word indicates generality in its literal sense. As in the oath of al-fawr, which is derived from 'the pot boiled' when it bubbles and becomes intense, then the state in which there is no delay and no hesitation is named after it, considering the boiling of anger. For example, when a woman wants to go out and her husband says: 'If you go out, you are divorced,' and she waits an hour until his anger subsides then goes out, she is not divorced. For the literal meaning of this statement is that she is divorced in every instance of going out, but the meaning of anger that occurred in the speaker at the time of her going out indicates that the intended is this specific outing, so the statement is taken metaphorically to it by this contextual indicator. Similarly, a man's statement to someone: 'Come, eat lunch with me,' and he said: 'If I eat lunch, my slave is free,' the literal meaning is that his slave becomes free wherever he eats lunch, whether with the inviter or alone in his house.

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on usul al-fiqh explaining the types of contextual indicators (qara'in) that necessitate taking a metaphorical meaning (majaz) over the literal meaning (haqiqah). The author presents two main types: first, the indication of the flow/context of the text (siyaq al-nazm), which is a verbal contextual indicator attached to the speech, whether preceding or following. Examples include the Quranic verse 'So do not say to them 'uff'' (17:23), which literally indicates annoyance but is taken to include hitting and reviling due to the context of honoring parents. The second type is the indication of a meaning referring to the speaker's intent (ma'na al-mutakallim wa qasdihi), which causes the general word to be taken specifically. The key example is the oath of al-fawr (instantaneous oath), derived from a hadith of Jabir. If a husband says to his wife 'If you go out, you are divorced' while angry, and she waits for his anger to subside before going out, the oath is not triggered because the contextual indicator of his anger shows that he meant only that specific outing. Similarly, if a man is invited to eat and responds 'If I eat lunch, my slave is free,' the slave is only freed if he eats that specific lunch with the inviter, not if he eats elsewhere. The passage also discusses a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students regarding whether grapes, fresh dates, and pomegranates are considered fruits in oaths, attributed to change in custom. This illustrates the role of custom ('urf) as a contextual indicator. Throughout, the commentary follows the order of the matn, first explaining the qarina of text flow, then the qarina of speaker's intent, with detailed examples and cross-references.

Key Terms
يمين الفور (yamīn al-fawr): An oath made impulsively in a state of anger, interpreted restrictively based on the speaker's immediate intent.

Prohibition Attached to Substances: Haqiqah or Majaz?
Stating the Hanafi position on prohibition attached to substances and defending the istiqra-based list of indicators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on prohibition attached to substances as haqiqah, explain the dalil, and evaluate the critique against the istiqra-based confinement.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, prohibition attached to substances is literal (haqiqah) unless proven otherwise.

This passage completes the author's list of five indicators for using majaz over haqiqah. It then addresses a key dispute: whether prohibition linguistically attached to entities (like 'your mothers are forbidden') is literal or metaphorical. The Hanafi school insists it is haqiqah, contrary to some others. This distinction affects many fiqh rulings, ranging from impurity of wine to validity of oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that al-tahrim al-mudaf ila al-a'yan is the prohibition attached directly to substances (e.g., 'your mothers are forbidden', 'wine is forbidden'). The dispute is whether this is haqiqah or majaz.
The Hanafi position is that such prohibition is haqiqah – the substance itself is forbidden, not merely the act.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Look at the Quranic verse 4:23 and the Hadith 'Hurrimat al-khamr li-'aynihi'. These texts attach prohibition directly to the entity (mothers, wine) without any clear qarina for metaphor.
The Hanafi principle is to retain haqiqah unless there is a valid reason to abandon it.
3
Understand the opposing view
Some scholars claim it is majaz, arguing that prohibition is a ruling on actions, not on inert substances. They consider the attachment to substances metaphorical.
This view would affect rulings like the impurity of the substance itself.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the texts are explicit and without qarina for majaz. The default in legal discourse is haqiqah, so the literal meaning must be upheld.
This response is rooted in the usul rule: al-asl fi al-kalam al-haqiqah.
5
Consider the critique on confinement
A critic might argue that the five situations for abandoning haqiqah are not exhaustive. The text responds that the istiqra is limited to legal (shar'i) matters, so other linguistic contexts do not invalidate the rule. Possibility of other factors does not undermine inductive confinement.
This shows the methodological soundness of the Hanafi approach.

Source Text

فتم الآن بيان المواضع الخمسة على استقراء المصنف له وفيه كلام كما لا يخفى. والتحريم المضاف إلى الأعيان كالمحارم والخمر حقيقة عندنا خلافًا للبعض، جملة مبتدئة تتمة لقوله: وبدلالة محل الكلام جيء بها ردًا لزعم البعض، فإنّهم زعموا أن التحريم المضاف إلى العين كالمحارم في قوله تعالى: ﴿ حُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْكُمْ أُمَّهَاتُكُمْ ﴾ (النساء: 23) والخمر في قوله عليه: "حرمت الخمر لعينها" فلا يصح التمسك بهذا الحديث للشافعي في بقاء الصلاة بالتكلم خطاء، والصوم بالأكل خطأ. وفيه كلام أي في حصر ما يترك به الحقيقة في الخمسة كلام والله أعلم ماذا أراد به الشارح؟ إن أراد به أنه قد يترك الحقيقة بقرائن أخرى في المحاورات واللغويات، فالحصر باطل، فيجاب عنه بأن البحث في الشرعيات فلا يضره ما في المحاورات واللغويات، وإن أراد به أن الحصر في الخمسة باطل؛ لاحتمال أن يترك الحقيقة بأمر آخر، فيجاب عنه بأن الاحتمال لا يضر الحصر الاستقرائي فتدبر.
Now the explanation of the five situations based on the istiqra of the author is completed, though there is discussion about it as is not hidden. And prohibition attached to substances like maharim (forbidden relatives) and wine is a real (haqiqah) according to us, contrary to some. This is an independent sentence completing his statement: 'And by the indication of the context of speech' it is brought as a response to the claim of some, for they claimed that prohibition attached to the substance, like maharim in His statement 'Forbidden to you are your mothers' (Quran 4:23) and wine in his statement 'Wine is forbidden in its essence' — so it is not valid to cling to this hadith for al-Shafi'i in the continuation of prayer upon speaking mistakenly and fasting upon eating mistakenly. And there is discussion regarding confining that which causes leaving the literal meaning to only five: perhaps haqiqah may be left with other indicators in ordinary speech and language, so the confinement is invalid; the response is that the investigation is in legal matters, so what happens in ordinary speech and language does not harm it. And if he meant that the confinement to five is invalid due to the possibility that haqiqah is left by another matter, the response is that possibility does not harm istiqra'i confinement. Commentary
Passage type: statement of an usul rule. The author has identified five specific situations where haqiqah (literal meaning) is abandoned in favor of majaz (metaphor) based on qara'in (indicators). These five are based on istiqra (inductive survey). Then, the text discusses that prohibition attached to entities like maharim and wine is to be taken literally (haqiqah) in Hanafi usul, contrary to some who claim it is metaphorical. This is introduced as an independent statement to rebut a claim. The five situations include context of speech (dalaalat al-mahall) and custom. The author then addresses a potential critique: that the confinement to five is incomplete because haqiqah may be left in other contexts (like ordinary language). The response: the scope is limited to legal (shar'i) matters, so non-legal uses do not affect the rule. Another critique: possibility of other factors; response: possibility does not undermine inductive confinement. The discussion ties back to the previous debate about the hadith of error and forgetfulness, showing that Shafi'i cannot use that hadith to support his view because the prohibition on wine is literal and not negated by metaphorical interpretation.

Key Terms
التحريم المضاف إلى الأعيان (al-tahrim al-mudaf ila al-a'yan): Prohibition linguistically attached to substances like 'forbidden to you are your mothers' or 'wine is forbidden', which according to Hanafis is literal (haqiqah) prohibition of the entity itself.
الاستقراء (al-istiqra'): Inductive survey of legal texts to derive a general rule, here used to identify the five situations where haqiqah is abandoned.
قرينة (qarina): An indicator (linguistic, contextual, or rational) that signals whether a word is to be taken literally or metaphorically.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, prohibition attached to substances is taken literally (haqiqah) as the default, and the five indicators for abandoning haqiqah are based on inductive survey (istiqra) limited to legal texts.

Prohibition of the Entity vs. Prohibition of the Act
Explaining two types of prohibition and refuting Mu'tazila claim of ambiguity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibition of the entity and prohibition of the act, and evaluate the Mu'tazila argument that the verse is mujmal.

Core Idea
Prohibiting the entity itself is more emphatic than prohibiting the action—the entity becomes impermissible.

This passage addresses a subtle but crucial usul point: when Allah says 'حرمت عليكم أمهاتكم', does the prohibition attach to the action of marrying mothers or to the entity of mothers themselves? The Hanafi school argues that it is literal and more emphatic, while some Mu'tazila claim it is ambiguous (mujmal) because only actions can be haram. We will unpack the reasoning and see why the Hanafi position is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of prohibition
From the passage, note that prohibition can be of two types: one that meets the action (the servant is prohibited from the action), and one that meets the locus (the entity becomes prohibited). Understand the difference: the first leaves the entity permissible, the second removes permissibility from the entity itself.
2
Understand the Hanafi argument for the more emphatic type
The passage illustrates with the analogy of a child and bread. The first way is saying 'do not eat the bread' while bread is present; the second is removing the bread entirely. Which is stronger? Clearly removing the bread. Similarly, prohibiting the entity (e.g., mothers, wine) removes the possibility of any action involving it.
This shows why the Hanafis consider the literal prohibition of the entity as the stronger form.
3
Examine the Mu'tazila objection
Some Mu'tazila argue that the text is mujmal because only actions can be described as haram, not entities. They claim that an unspecified action must be intended, making the meaning ambiguous. This forces pausing for clarification according to their usul.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the context of speech (the verse) specifies the action—it clearly refers to marriage of mothers. There is no ambiguity because the phrase 'حرمت عليكم أمهاتكم' encompasses all actions related to them, and the strongest prohibition is to render the entity itself impermissible. The Mu'tazila position is dismissed as poor understanding.
The key is that the entity's prohibition is literal, not metaphorical.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: Mu'tazila would require the jurist to pause and seek clarification (which action is prohibited), while Hanafis apply the prohibition immediately to all actions connected to the entity. This affects how we derive rulings from such texts.
The Hanafi view gives immediate legal effect without suspension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث مجاز عن الفعل أي نكاح أمهاتكم وشرب الخمر، فتكون الحقيقة متروكة بدلالة محل الكلام؛ لأن المحل عين لا يقبل الحرمة؛ لأن الحل والحرمة من أوصاف الفعل، فقلنا نحن: إن هذه الحرمة على حالها وحقيقتها؛ لأنه أبلغ من أن يقول حرمت نكاح أمهاتكم؛ وذلك لأن الحرمة نوعان: نوع: يلاقي الفعل فيكون العبد ممنوعا والفعل ممنوعا عنه، ونوع: يلاقي المحل فيخرج المحل من أن يكون مباحًا، وصار العين ممنوعا والعبد ممنوعا عنه، وهذا أبلغ الوجهين في المنع ، فإن الأول كما يقال للطفل: "لا تأكل الخبز" وهو بين يديه، والثاني كما يرفع الخبز من بين يديه، ويقال له: لا تأكل فهو بمنزلة النفي والنسخ وهو أبلغ من النهي الحقيقي هما مترادفان على ما مرّ تقريره وقال بعض المعتزلة : إنه مجمل؛ لأن العين لا يكون حراما فلا بد من تقدير الفعل وهو غير معين لاستواء جميع الأفعال فيه، فيجب التوقف وهو خلف منشؤه سوء الفهم.
Statement of the divisions of the third division: metaphor from the action, i.e., the marriage of your mothers and drinking wine. So the literal meaning is abandoned by the indication of the context of speech, because the locus is an entity that does not accept prohibition, because permissibility and prohibition are attributes of the action. So we said: This prohibition is in its state and its reality, because it is more emphatic than if it said 'I forbade marriage of your mothers'. That is because prohibition is of two types: a type that meets the action so the servant is prohibited and the action is prohibited from him; and a type that meets the locus so the locus exits from being permissible, and the entity becomes prohibited and the servant is prohibited from it. This is the more emphatic of the two ways in prohibition. The first is like saying to a child: 'Do not eat the bread' while it is before him. The second is like removing the bread from before him and saying to him: 'Do not eat'. It is in the category of negation and abrogation, and it is more emphatic than the real prohibition. They are synonymous as established earlier. Some Mu'tazila said: It is ambiguous (mujmal) because the entity cannot be haram, so an action must be estimated, and it is unspecified due to the equality of all actions concerning it, so one must pause. This is incorrect, arising from poor understanding.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the nature of prohibition in the Qur'anic verse 'حرمت عليكم أمهاتكم' (Forbidden to you are your mothers). The author explains that the prohibition attached to the entity (the mothers themselves) is literal and more emphatic than a prohibition attached to the action (marriage). This is a Hanafi position against some Mu'tazila who claim the text is ambiguous (mujmal) because only actions can be prohibited, not entities. The author clarifies that prohibition can be of two types: one that prohibits the action while the entity remains permissible, and one that removes the permissible status of the entity itself. The latter is stronger, as illustrated by the analogy of a child being told not to eat bread while it is present versus having the bread removed entirely. The Mu'tazila argument that the verb 'setime is unspecified is refuted by noting that the context determines the action. This dispute has practical implications: for the Mu'tazila, one must stop and seek clarification; for the Hanafis, the prohibition is immediately clear and applicable.

Key Terms
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage where the word is used for other than its original meaning due to a connection
حقيقة (haqiqah): Literal, original meaning of a word as established in language
التحريم (al-tahrim): Legal prohibition, which can attach to the act or the entity
مجمل (mujmal): Ambiguous text requiring external clarification due to multiple possible meanings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, what is the practical consequence of prohibiting the entity (al-'ayn)?
A) One must pause and seek clarification before applying the ruling.
B) The entity remains permissible, but the action is prohibited.
C) The entity itself becomes forbidden, and all related actions are prohibited immediately.
D) The prohibition is weaker than if it were attached to the action.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that prohibition of the entity is literal and more emphatic than prohibition of the act, settling the meaning of the verse without ambiguity.

Ruling on Expiation with 'Or': One Obligatory Option
Explains the Hanafi rule on 'aw' in expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that the disjunctive particle 'aw' in expiation texts imposes only one obligatory option, and evaluate the Mu'tazili counter-interpretation.

Core Idea
The word 'aw' in Quranic expiations obligates only one of the listed acts, not all.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi usul principle: when the Quran or Sunna presents multiple expiatory acts connected by 'aw' (or), the mukallaf must fulfill only one. We will explore three Quranic examples, the Hanafi proof from language, and a verbal dispute with the Mu'tazila. Understanding this clarifies a common confusion about the nature of choice in Islamic obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source texts
Locate the three Quranic verses where expiation options are listed using 'aw': Quran 5:89 (oath), 2:196 (shaving head in ihram), and 5:95 (hunting game in ihram). Recognize that each verse presents multiple acts connected by 'aw'.
2
Isolate the operative phrase
Focus on the word 'aw' (أو) in each verse. This disjunctive particle is the key linguistic element that determines the legal nature of the listed options.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul rule
According to Hanafi usul, the particle 'aw' linguistically indicates takhyir (choice). Therefore, the mukallaf may choose any one of the listed acts; only that one is wajib. Performing multiple acts does not count as multiple expiations.
This rule is derived from the literal meaning of 'aw', not from a secondary principle.
4
Contrast with the opposing interpretation
The Iraqis and Mu'tazila interpret 'aw' as indicating badal (substitution): all options are obligatory in principle, but performing one substitutes for the rest. The well-known Mu'tazili view, however, leads to the same practical outcome as the Hanafi position.
The author clarifies that the difference is merely verbal (lafzi) in the well-known Mu'tazili view, though some Mu'tazila hold a stricter view akin to communal obligations.
5
Recognize the practical equivalence
In both the Hanafi and the well-known Mu'tazili positions, the mukallaf is only punished for neglecting one act and only rewarded for performing one act. The choice is functionally identical.
This illustrates a legitimate ikhtilaf where the dispute does not affect the fiqh ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن في كل كفارة يجب أحد الأشياء عندنا خلافًا للبعض يعني أن في كل كفارة ردد فيها بين الأشياء بكلمة "أو" كما في كفارة اليمين من قوله تعالى: ﴿إِطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطِ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ أَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ أَوْ تَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ وكما في كفارة حلق الرأس من عذر من قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنْكُمْ مَرِيضا أَوْ بِهِ أَذىً مِنْ رَأْسِهِ فَفِدْيَةٌ مِنْ صِيَامٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ أَوْ نُسُكٍ وكما في كفارة جزاء الصيد من قوله تعالى: ﴿فَجَزَاء مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ يَحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ هَدْياً بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ أَوْ كَفَّارَةٌ طَعَامُ مَسَاكِينَ أَوْ عَدْلُ ذَلِكَ صِيَاماً يجب عندنا أحد الأشياء على سبيل الإباحة، فلو أدى الكل لا يقع عن الكفارة إلا واحد والباقي تبرع، وإن عطل الكل يعاقب على واحد منها، بخلاف البعض وهم العراقيون والمعتزلة، فإن الكل واجب عندهم على سبيل البدل، جزاء الصيد إلخ أي في الإحرام قال الله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنْتُمْ حُرُم﴾ (المائدة: 95) أي محرمون جمع حرام، وَمَنْ قَتَلَهُ مِنْكُمْ مُتَعَمِّداً فَجَزَاء مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَم أي فعليه جزاء يماثل ما قتل في القيمة به أي بالمثل ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ هَدْيا حال من جزاء بالغ الكعبة، فيذبح بالحرم أَوْ كَفَّارَةٌ عطف على جزاء طَعَامُ مَسَاكِينَ عطف بيان أَوْ عَدْلُ ذَلِكَ صِيَاماً (المائدة: 95) أي ما ساواه من الصوم، والحاصل أنه يقوم الصيد حيث صيد، فإن بلغت ثمن هدي يخير بين أن يهدي ما قيمته وبين أن يشتري بقيمة طعامًا، فيعطي كل مسكين نصف صاع من بر، أو صاعا من غيره، وبين أن يصوم عن طعام كل مسكين يوما، وإن لم تبلغ يخير بين الإطعام والصوم. (القمر) أو عدل ذلك صيامًا إلخ: قال في شرح الوقاية فإن قتل محرم صيدا إلى قوله وجزاءه ما قومه عدلان في مقتله، أو أقرب مكان منه في السبع لا يزيد على شاة، ثم له أن يشتري به هديًا ويذبحه بمكة أو طعامًا ويتصدق على كل مسكين نصف صاع من بر أو صاعا من تمر أو من شعير، لا أقل منه أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوما، وإن فضل من طعام مسكين تصدق به أو صام يوما. (السنبلي) صيامًا: أي صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوما. (المحشي) إلا واحد وهو الذي أعلاها قيمة، فيستحق ثواب واجب. (القمر) يعاقب على واحد وهو الذي كان أدناها قيمة للإخلال بواجب واحد وهو أحدها (القمر) على سبيل البدل هذا عند المشاهير من المعتزلة فهم يدعون وجوب الجميع بمعنى أنه لا يجوز الإخلال بالكل، ولو أخل بالكل لا يعاقب إلا على ترك واحد ولا يجب الإتيان بالكل ولو أتى بالكل لا يثاب إلا على فعل واحد، والمكلف مخير فأيها فعل خرج عن عهدة التكليف وهذا هو عين مذهبنا فلا فرق بيننا وبينهم إلا بحسب اللفظ، فإنا قائلون بوجوب واحد منها وهم قائلون بوجوب الكل على سبيل البدل وأما بعض المعتزلة فقالوا: إن كل واحد منها واجب لكنه إذا أتى بواحد سقط الآخر كالواجب على الكفاية فإنه واجب على الكل، ويسقط بفعل البعض، ولو أتى بالكل امتثل بالإتيان بالكل فاستحق ثواب واجبات فيثاب ثواب الواجب على كل واحد، =
That in every expiation, one of the things is obligatory with us, contrary to some. Meaning that in every expiation in which there is a choice among things by the word 'or', as in the expiation of the oath from His statement: 'The feeding of ten needy persons from the average of what you feed your families or their clothing or the freeing of a slave' (5:89), and as in the expiation of shaving the head due to an excuse from His statement: 'But whoever among you is ill or has an ailment of the head then a ransom of fasts or charity or sacrifice' (2:196), and as in the expiation of the penalty of hunting from His statement: 'Then a compensation: an equivalent of what he killed from livestock, as judged by two just men among you, as an offering reaching the Ka'bah, or expiation: feeding needy persons, or the equivalent of that in fasting' (5:95). With us, one of the things is obligatory on the basis of permission. So if he performs all, only one counts for the expiation and the rest are voluntary; if he neglects all, he is punished for one of them. Contrary to some, namely the Iraqis and the Mu'tazila, for with them all are obligatory on the basis of substitution. 'Penalty of hunting' etc. means in ihram. Allah said: 'O you who believe, do not kill game while you are in a state of ihram' (5:95). That is, those who are in a state of consecration. 'And whoever of you kills it intentionally, then compensation is the equivalent of what he killed from livestock' meaning he owes a compensation similar in value to what he killed, 'as judged by two just men among you, as an offering reaching the Ka'bah', so it is slaughtered in the sanctuary, 'or expiation: feeding needy persons, or the equivalent of that in fasting' (5:95). That is, what equals it in fasting. The conclusion: the game is valued where it was hunted; if the price reaches that of a sacrificial animal, he is given a choice between offering what is equivalent, or buying food with the value and giving each poor person half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of other grain, or fasting a day for each poor person's food. If it does not reach that, he is given a choice between feeding and fasting. (al-Qamar) 'Or the equivalent of that in fasting' etc. He said in Sharh al-Wiqaya: if a pilgrim kills game... up to his statement: and its compensation is what two just men evaluate at the place of killing, or the nearest place to it within the haram, not exceeding a sheep. Then he may buy with it a sacrificial animal and slaughter it in Mecca, or food and give charity to each poor person half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley, not less, or fast a day for each poor person's food. If there is surplus from the food of a poor person, he gives it in charity or fasts a day. (al-Sunbuliyya?) 'Fasting': that is, he fasts a day for each poor person's food. (al-Muhashshi) 'Except one, which is the highest in value, for which he deserves the reward of an obligatory act. (al-Qamar) He is punished for one, which is the lowest in value, due to neglecting one obligatory act, which is one of them. (al-Qamar) 'On the basis of substitution': this is the position of the well-known Mu'tazila. They claim the obligation of all, meaning that it is not permissible to neglect the whole; but if he neglects all, he is only punished for omitting one, and it is not necessary to perform all; if he performs all, he is only rewarded for one act. The obligated person is given a choice: whichever he does, he is discharged from the obligation. This is exactly our doctrine, so there is no difference between us and them except in wording. For we say one of them is obligatory, and they say all are obligatory on the basis of substitution. As for some Mu'tazila, they said that each one of them is obligatory, but if he performs one, the others fall away, like a communal obligation: it is obligatory on all, but falls away by the action of some. If he performs all, he has complied by performing all, so he deserves the reward of multiple obligatory acts; he is rewarded with the reward of an obligatory act for each one. =
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the word 'or' (أو) in the context of expiations (kaffarat) in Islamic law. The author explains the Hanafi position: when the Quran or Sunna prescribes multiple options for an expiation connected by 'or', only one of these acts is wajib (obligatory). The text cites three examples: the expiation for breaking an oath (feeding or clothing or freeing a slave), the expiation for shaving the head during ihram due to illness (fasting or charity or sacrifice), and the expiation for killing game while in ihram (offering an equivalent animal or feeding the poor or fasting). In all cases, the Hanafi school holds that the mukallaf (obligated person) may choose any one of the listed acts, and performing all does not count the extra acts as part of the expiation—they become voluntary. Neglecting all results in punishment for omitting one obligatory act. The passage then contrasts this with the view of the Iraqis and Mu'tazila, who say all acts are obligatory on the basis of substitution (badal), meaning that one act substitutes for the obligation and it is as if all are required potentially. The author clarifies that the well-known Mu'tazili view is actually identical in practical effect to the Hanafi view: the person chooses one, and is only rewarded or punished for one. The difference is merely verbal (lafzi). However, some Mu'tazila hold a different view akin to communal obligations, where each act is individually obligatory but becomes unnecessary once one is performed. The passage thus demonstrates the usul principle that 'or' in legal texts creates a choice of one, not a requirement of all.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A disjunctive particle that, in expiation texts, requires the mukallaf to fulfill only one of the mentioned options.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): A compensatory act prescribed to expiate certain sins or violations, such as breaking an oath, shaving the head in ihram, or killing game.
على سبيل البدل (ala sabili al-badal): On the basis of substitution; meaning that the different options are considered substitutes for one another, and only one is actually required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

The disjunctive 'or' (أو) in expiation texts imposes only one obligation; performing additional acts does not count as multiple expiations.

The Hanafi Rule on 'Aw' in Kaffarah Verses
Explaining the Hanafi ruling that 'aw' obligates only one option in expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that 'aw' in kaffarah verses obligates only one option, and distinguish the Hanafi position from Mu'tazilite views.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' in alternatives obligates one, not all – doing extra is voluntary.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar tackles a classic usul question: when the Quran uses 'or' (aw) between expiation options, does it make all of them obligatory or just one? The Hanafi school takes a clear position grounded in linguistic usage (lugha) and shari'ah. Understanding this ruling is essential for deriving correct fiqh rulings from similarly structured texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal text
Point to the Quranic verses cited (2:196 and 5:95) that contain 'aw' between alternatives.
These verses are the primary dalil.
2
Recognize the usul principle
'Aw' in legal contexts indicates obligation of one of the things (li ahad al-ashya'), not all.
This is the Hanafi position based on language and shari'ah.
3
Apply the principle to kaffarah
Only one option is wajib; performing all counts only one, the rest are tatawwu'.
Neglecting all leads to punishment for one.
4
Contrast the Mu'tazilite view
Some Mu'tazilites claim all options are obligatory individually, leading to different consequences.
The well-known Mu'tazilite view (badal) is similar in outcome to Hanafi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The rejected view contradicts linguistic and legal usage, so it is not considered.
This evaluation reinforces the correct usul principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بحث كلمة "أو" من قوله تعالى: ﴿فَفِدْيَةٌ مِنْ صِيَامٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ أَوْ نُسُكِ وكما في كفارة جزاء الصيد من قوله تعالى: ﴿فَجَزَاء مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ يَحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ هَدْياً بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ أَوْ كَفَّارَةٌ طَعَامُ مَسَاكِينَ أَوْ عَدْلُ ذَلِكَ صِيَاما يجب عندنا أحد الأشياء على سبيل الإباحة، فلو أدى الكل لا يقع عن الكفارة إلا واحد والباقي تبرع، وإن عطل الكل يعاقب على واحد منها، بخلاف البعض وهم العراقيون والمعتزلة، فإن الكل واجب عندهم على سبيل البدل، جزاء الصيد إلخ أي في الإحرام قال الله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنْتُمْ حُرُم (المائدة: ٩٥) أي محرمون جمع حرام، وَمَنْ قَتَلَهُ مِنْكُمْ مُتَعَمِّداً فَجَزَاءً مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَم أي فعليه جزاء يماثل ما قتل في القيمة به أي بالمثل ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ هَدْيار حال من جزاء بالغ الكعبة، فيذبح بالحرم أَوْ كَفَّارَةٌ عطف على جزاء طَعَامُ مَسَاكِينَ عطف بيان أَوْ عَدْلُ ذَلِكَ صِيَاماً (المائدة : ٩٥) أي ما ساواه من الصوم، والحاصل أنه يقوم الصيد حيث صيد، فإن بلغت ثمن هدي يخير بين أن يهدي ما قيمته وبين أن يشتري بقيمة طعامًا، فيعطي كل مسكين نصف صاع من بر، أو صاعا من غيره، وبين أن يصوم عن طعام كل مسكين يوما، وإن لم تبلغ يخير بين الإطعام والصوم. (القمر) أو عدل ذلك صيامًا إلخ : قال في شرح الوقاية فإن قتل محرم صيدا إلى قوله وجزاءه ما قومه عدلان في مقتله، أو أقرب مكان منه في السبع لا يزيد على شاة، ثم له أن يشتري به هديًا ويذبحه بمكة أو طعامًا ويتصدق على كل مسكين نصف صاع من بر أو صاعا من تمر أو من شعير، لا أقل منه أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوما، وإن فضل من طعام مسكين تصدق به أو صام يوما . (السنبلي) صيامًا : أي صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوما. (المحشي) إلا واحد وهو الذي أعلاها قيمة، فيستحق ثواب واجب . (القمر) يعاقب على واحد وهو الذي كان أدناها قيمة للإخلال بواجب واحد وهو أحدها (القمر) على سبيل البدل هذا عند المشاهير من المعتزلة فهم يدعون وجوب الجميع بمعنى أنه لا يجوز الإخلال بالكل، ولو أخل بالكل لا يعاقب إلا على ترك واحد ولا يجب الإتيان بالكل ولو أتى بالكل لا يثاب إلا على فعل واحد، والمكلف مخير فأيها فعل خرج عن عهدة التكليف وهذا هو عين مذهبنا فلا فرق بيننا وبينهم إلا بحسب اللفظ، فإنا قائلون بوجوب واحد منها وهم قائلون بوجوب الكل على سبيل البدل وأما بعض المعتزلة فقالوا: إن كل واحد منها واجب لكنه إذا أتى بواحد سقط الآخر كالواجب على الكفاية فإنه واجب على الكل، ويسقط بفعل البعض، ولو أتى بالكل امتثل بالإتيان بالكل فاستحق ثواب واجبات فيثاب ثواب الواجب على كل واحد، فإن فعل أحدها سقط وجوب باقيها، وإن أدى الكل يقع الكل واجبًا وإن عطل الكل يعاقب على الجميع، قلنا: هذا خلاف وضع اللغة والشرع فلا يعتبر.
Statement of the divisions of the third division. Discussion of the word 'aw' from His statement: 'then a ransom of fasting or charity or sacrifice' and similarly in the expiation of the penalty for hunting from His statement: 'then a penalty like what he killed of livestock, judged by two just persons among you, as an offering reaching the Kaaba, or an expiation: feeding the poor or the equivalent of that in fasting' – according to us, one of the things is obligatory on the basis of permission (ibaha). If he performs all, only one counts for the expiation and the rest are voluntary. If he neglects all, he is punished for one of them. Contrary to some, namely the Iraqis and Mu'tazilites, for all are obligatory according to them on a substitution basis (badal). 'Penalty for hunting' etc. meaning during ihram. Allah said: 'O you who believe, do not kill game while you are in a state of ihram' – meaning those in ihram, plural of haram. 'And whoever kills it among you intentionally, then a penalty like what he killed of livestock' – meaning upon him is a penalty resembling what he killed in value. 'Judged by two just persons among you, as an offering reaching the Kaaba' – a state from 'penalty' – so it is slaughtered in the sanctuary. 'Or an expiation' – coordinated with 'penalty' – 'feeding the poor' – explanatory apposition – 'or the equivalent of that in fasting' – meaning what equals it of fasting. The summary: that the game is valued where it was killed. If it reaches the price of a sacrificial animal, he is given a choice between sacrificing what is its value and buying food with its value and giving every poor person half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of other grain, and between fasting for each poor person a day. If it does not reach that, he is given a choice between feeding and fasting. (al-Qamar) 'or the equivalent of that in fasting' etc.: He said in Sharh al-Wiqaya: If a muhrim kills game... until his statement: its penalty is what two just persons appraise at the place of killing, or the nearest place to it among the seven (types) not exceeding a sheep. Then he may buy with it a sacrificial animal and slaughter it in Mecca, or food and give in charity to every poor person half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley, not less, or fast for each poor person a day. If there is an excess from the food of a poor person, he may give it in charity or fast a day. (al-Sanbali) 'fasting': meaning he fasts for each poor person a day. (al-Muhashi) 'Except one' which is the highest in value, he deserves the reward of an obligatory act. (al-Qamar) 'He is punished for one' which is the lowest in value, for neglecting one obligatory act which is one of them. (al-Qamar) 'On a substitution basis' – this is according to the well-known among the Mu'tazilites: they claim the obligation of all in the sense that it is not permissible to neglect the whole, but if he neglects the whole, he is only punished for abandoning one, and it is not necessary to perform the whole, and if he performs the whole, he is not rewarded except for one act. The obligated person is given a choice: whichever he does, he fulfills the duty. This is exactly our school, so there is no difference between us and them except in wording. For we say an obligation of one of them, and they say an obligation of all on a substitution basis. As for some Mu'tazilites, they said: Each one of them is obligatory, but if he does one, the other drops, like the obligation on sufficiency which is obligatory on all but drops by the action of some. If he does all, he has complied by doing all and deserves the reward of obligatory acts, so he is rewarded as an obligatory act for each one. If he does one of them, the obligation of the rest drops. If he performs all, all count as obligatory. If he neglects all, he is punished for all. We said: This is contrary to the usage of language and law, so it is not considered.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the word 'aw' in legal texts, specifically in expiation verses. The author first states the Hanafi position: when 'aw' appears between alternatives (like in fidyah and kaffarah for hunting), it indicates that only one of the options is obligatory (wajib) on the basis of permission (ibaha). If a person performs all the alternatives, only one counts towards the expiation; the rest are supererogatory. If he neglects all, he is punished for one. This is contrasted with the view of the Iraqis and Mu'tazilites, who hold that all alternatives are obligatory on a substitution basis (badal). The passage then explains the verse on hunting penalty in detail, including the valuation and the choice between offering, feeding, and fasting. The author then examines the Mu'tazilite views more closely: the well-known Mu'tazilites say all are obligatory but on a badal basis, meaning only one act is required and rewarded, which is effectively the same as the Hanafi view (only terminological difference). However, some Mu'tazilites claim each is obligatory but they drop upon performance of one, like communal obligations (fard kifaya); if one does all, all count as obligatory and he is punished for all if he neglects all. The author dismisses this as contrary to linguistic and legal usage.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle indicating that one of the alternatives is sufficient; in legal usage, it obligates one of the listed options.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for a sin or violation, here for hunting in ihram or breaking a vow.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; the legal quality of being required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person performs all three options of fidyah (fasting, charity, sacrifice), what is the ruling?
A) All count as obligatory
B) Only one counts, the rest are voluntary
C) The person is punished
D) It is invalid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the particle 'aw' in legal alternatives obligates only one option; performing extra is voluntary, and any interpretation contradicting this is rejected.

Metaphorical Interpretation of 'أو' in Usul al-Fiqh
Analyzing the linguistic and usul interpretation of 'أو' in a Quranic verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the linguistic conditions under which the particle 'أو' can be interpreted metaphorically as 'حتى' or 'إلا أن' and apply this analysis to derive the correct meaning of a Quranic verse.

Core Idea
أو can mean 'until' when literal disjunction breaks the logical flow of an extended negation.

In this lesson, we delve into the usul al-fiqh analysis of the Quranic particle 'أو' (or) in Surah Al-Imran 3:128. While its primary meaning is disjunction, Hanafi usul scholars show that context may require a metaphorical reading, such as 'until' or 'except that'. This lesson will guide you through the reasoning behind that interpretation, using the verse as a case study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the literal meaning of 'أو'
Start with the basic lexical meaning: 'أو' is a particle of disjunction, indicating a choice between two things.
This is the haqiqah (literal) meaning.
2
Test literal application to the verse
Apply the literal meaning to 'ليس لك من الأمر شيء أو يتوب عليهم أو يعذبهم'. If 'أو' is literal, the verse would mean: 'You have no part in the matter, or He turns to them, or He punishes them.' This is incoherent because it suggests the negation (no part) only applies if one of the two events does not happen.
The negation 'ليس لك من الأمر شيء' extends indefinitely, and the literal reading contradicts this extension.
3
Recognize the need for metaphorical shift
Because literal disjunction leads to incoherence, the particle must be interpreted metaphorically (majaz). Hanafi usul allows such shifts when context demands.
The context includes the sabab al-nuzul (the Prophet's supplication after Uhud).
4
Establish the relationship between 'أو' and 'حتى' or 'إلا أن'
The passage explains that 'أو' can be used metaphorically to indicate ghayah (endpoint) like 'حتى' or istithna (exception) like 'إلا أن'. The condition for 'حتى' is that the second element is a part or close associate of the first; for 'إلا أن' it is a negated exception.
In this verse, the second and third elements (turning and punishing) are outcomes that end the period of the Prophet's lack of authority.
5
Derive the intended meaning
Since the first part is an extended negation, 'أو' indicates the endpoint of that negation. Thus the verse means: 'You have no part in the matter until He turns to them or punishes them.'
This interpretation aligns with the sabab al-nuzul: the Prophet was forbidden from cursing them until Allah's decision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بحث كلمة "أو" حتى ممتدا بحيث يحتمل ضرب الغاية فيما بعدها شرط لكونها بمعنى "حتى" أو "إلا أن"؛ لأن للغاية ينتهي بها المغيا كما أن أحد الشيئين في "أو " ينتهي بوجود الآخر، و"إلا أن" استثناء في الواقع حكمه مخالفة ما سبق في الأحكام كما أن حكم المعطوف بـ"أو" يخالف حكم المعطوف عليه بوجود أحدهما فقط، فيتحقق بين "أو " وبين كل من "حتى" و "إلا أن مناسبة يجوز استعارتها لهما، لكن الفرق بين "حتى" و"إلا أن"؛ أنَّ "حتى" تجيء بمعنى العطف أيضًا دون "إلا أن" ، وأَنَّ كون الثاني جزء من الأول عنده شرط في "حتى" دون "إلا أن" وسيجيء تحقيقه في بحث "حتى". كقوله تعالى: لَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ شَيْءٌ أَوْ يَتُوبَ عَلَيْهِمْ أَوْ يُعَذِّبَهُمْ، فإن قوله: ﴿وَأَوْ يَتُوبَ لا يصلح أن يكون معطوفا على قوله : لَيْسَ لَكَ أي المعطوف (آل عمران: ۱۲۸) ممتدا إلخ: يعني لكون السابق أمرًا ممتداً يوجب كون ما بعد "أو " غاية له فيتحقق ما هو شرط لوقوع حتى أي الغاية، فيكون "أو " بمعنى "حتى" مجازا كما مر في المثال سابقا منا في الحاشية.(السنبلي) حتى للغاية دليل المناسبة بين "أو " و "حتى" للاستعارة. (المحشي) أن أحد إلخ الغرض منه بيان العلاقة بين المعنى الحقيقي أي أحد الشيئين وبين المعنى المجازي أي الغاية (القمر) كما أن حكم إلخ الغرض منه بيان المناسبة بين المعنى الحقيقي لـ أو والمعنى المجازي وهو ههنا الاستثناء. (القمر) استعارتها لهما أي استعارة "أو" لـ حتى، و "إلا أن (القمر) وأن إلخ معطوف على قوله أن حتى إلخ. (القمر) جزء من الأول: أي المعطوف عليه حقيقة كما في أكلت السمكة حتى رأسها أو كالجزء بالاختلاط كما في ضربني السادات حتى عبيدهم. (القمر) عنده أي عند الإمام عبد القاهر، ويكفي ذكر المرجع حكمًا، وقد رأيت بخط الشارح أو عنده، ولعل المعنى أن كون المعطوف جزء من المعطوف عليه أو عنده أي قريبا من الجزء شرط إلخ فتأمل (القمر) عنده إلخ والأصح أو عنده والمعنى أن كون الثاني جزء من الأول أو كونه عند الأول ومتصلاً به شرط في "حتى"، مثال الأول أي الجزئية أكلت السمكة حتى رأسها، ومثال الثاني قوله تعالى: ﴿سَلامٌ هِيَ حَتَّى مَطْلَعِ الْفَجْرِ) (القدر:٥)، وقول القائل: نمت البارحة حتى الصباح، فإن الصباح شيء ينتهي عند الليل، وإرجاع ضمير عنده إلى عبد القاهر والقراءة عنده بغير "أو " تكلف بارد وليس هكذا كلمة " إلى "؛ لأن مجرورها يجب أن يكون متصلاً بما قبلها فحسب. (السنبلي) لعدم اتساق النظم ولا على قوله: الأمر أو شيء، وهو ظاهر، ولكنه يصلح قوله: "لَيْسَ لَكَ" أن يمتد إلى غاية التوبة أو التعذيب، فيكون "أو " بمعنى "حتى" أو "إلا أن فيكون المعنى ليس لك من أمر الكفار شيء في دعاء الشر أو طلب الشفاعة حتى يتوب الله تعالى عليهم؛ فإنه حينئذٍ يكون لك طلب الشفاعة أو يعذبهم، فيكون لك الدعاء بالشر، وروي استأذن الله أن يدعو عليهم فنزلت، وقيل: إنه لما شج وجهه عليها يوم أحد أن النبي دعاء الشر اهد سأل أصحابه أن يدعو عليهم، فقال عليه : ما بعثني الله لَعَانًا ولكن بعثني داعيًا اللهم قومي، فإنهم لا يعلمون فنزلت، ونهى الله عن الدعاء عليهم أو سؤال الهداية لهم، لعدم اتساق النظم : لاختلاف المعطوف والمعطوف عليه مضارعًا وماضيًا، ولقائل أن يقول: إنه إذا كان المطلوب من الماضي الإخبار عن الماضي، ومن المضارع الإخبار عن المستقبل، فعطف المضارع على الماضي حسن تأمل. (القمر) ولا على قوله إلخ لاختلاف المعطوف والمعطوف عليه فعلاً واسعًا، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه يجوز أن يعطف على الأمر أو على شيء بإضمار أن والمعنى ليس لك من الأمر أو التوبة عليهم أو تعذيبهم شيء، أو المعنى ليس لك من الأمر شيء أو التوبة عليهم، أو التعذيب عليهم كذا قال البيضاوي، وهذا عطف الاسم على الاسم لا عطف الفعل على الاسم. (القمر) قوله لأجل كونه تحريما وهو يحتمل الامتداد. (المحشي) يتوب الله تعالى في الصراح: تاب الله عليه أي وفقه للتوبة. (القمر) أو يعذبهم معطوف على قوله: يتوب الله تعالى (القمر) لما شج: ويقال: شجت السفينة البحر أي شقته، وفي الدر المختار: وتختص الشجة بما يكون بالوجه والرأس لغة، وما يكون بغيرها تسمى جراحة (القمر) يوم أحد بضم الألف والحاء جبل بقرب المدينة فيه واقعة عظيمة. (القمر) فنزلت في "التفسير الكبير : وروي أن عتبة شجه وكسر رباعيته فجعل يمسح الدم عن وجهه وسالم مولى = أخرج البخاري في صحيحه رقم ۳۸٤۲ ، باب وَلَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ (آل عمران: ۱۲۸) والنسائي رقم ۱۰۷۸ ، باب لعن المنافقين في القنوت والترمذي رقم: ۳۰۰٤ باب ومن سورة آل عمران، وأحمد في " مسنده " رقم: ٥٦٧٤ ، عن ابن عمر ، لفظ الترمذي: قال رسول الله يوم أحد : اللهم العن أبا سفيان، اللهم العن الحارث بن هشام، اللهم العن صفوان بن أمية، قال: فنزلت لَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ شَيْءٌ أخرجه البخاري في "صحيحه" باب لَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ الْأَمْرِ شَيْءٌ والترمذي رقم: ۳۰۰۲، باب ومن سورة آل عمران عن أنس ، لفظ البخاري عن أنس شج النبي يوم أحد فقال: كيف يفلح قوم شجوا نبيهم فنزلت لَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ أخر. جه ابن جرير عن قتادة. [إشراق الأبصار: ١١]
Explanation of the divisions of the third division. Discussion of the word 'أو' extending such that it can possibly take the meaning of 'until' or 'except that'; because the endpoint is where the thing described ends, just as one of two things in 'or' ends with the existence of the other, and 'except that' is an exception whose ruling differs from what preceded, just as the ruling of the conjunct with 'or' differs from the conjuncted upon by the existence of only one. So there is a relationship between 'or' and each of 'until' and 'except that' that allows metaphorical use. But the difference between 'until' and 'except that' is that 'until' also comes in the meaning of conjunction, unlike 'except that', and that the second being part of the first is a condition in 'until' but not in 'except that' – its verification will come in the discussion of 'until'. As in His saying: 'You have no part in the matter, or He turns to them or punishes them' (Al-Imran 3:128). For indeed His statement 'or He turns' cannot be a conjunct on 'You have no part' because the preceding is extended, requiring what follows 'or' to be its endpoint... [continues]
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh analysis of the word 'أو' (or) as it appears in the Quranic verse (3:128). The author explains that 'أو' can have multiple meanings: literal disjunction, or metaphorical meanings such as 'حتى' (until) or 'إلا أن' (except that), depending on context. The discussion centers on the syntactic and semantic conditions that determine which meaning is intended. Using the verse 'لَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ شَيْءٌ أَوْ يَتُوبَ عَلَيْهِمْ أَوْ يُعَذِّبَهُمْ' (You have no part in the matter, or He turns to them or punishes them), the author argues that the two 'أو's cannot be simple conjuncts because the first part is an extended negation; thus 'أو' must indicate an endpoint, equivalent to 'until' or 'except that'. The commentary traces the reasoning, citing earlier scholars like al-Sanbali and al-Qamar, and includes the sabab al-nuzul (occasion of revelation) related to the Battle of Uhud. The passage demonstrates how usul al-fiqh tools—especially linguistic analysis of particles—are applied to derive correct understanding of Quranic texts.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle of disjunction, but can metaphorically indicate ghayah (endpoint) or istithna (exception) depending on context.
حتى (hatta): A particle indicating ghayah (endpoint) or conjunction; the second element must be part of the first or closely associated.
إلا أن (illa an): Except that; indicates an exception with a ruling opposite to what preceded.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'أو' in Quranic context can metaphorically indicate an endpoint or exception, and its correct interpretation is determined by contextual coherence using usul al-fiqh principles.

The Particle 'Aw' in Quran 3:128 — Disjunction, Parenthesis, and Legal Implication
Exegetical analysis of the particle 'aw' in Quran 3:128

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the multiple grammatical interpretations of 'aw' in Quran 3:128 and explain how the Hanafi usul scholars and al-Zamakhshari derive different legal implications from the verse's syntactic structure.

Core Idea
The scope of 'aw' determines whether the Prophet had authority to supplicate — a single particle changes the ruling.

In this passage, the author examines the particle 'aw' (أو) in Surah Al-Imran 3:128. The verse appears to restrict the Prophet's authority over the disbelievers. However, different readings of whether 'aw' means 'or', 'until', or 'unless' and whether certain clauses are parenthetical lead to different legal understandings. This lesson walks through the syntactic analysis and the resulting usul debate.

Guided Path
1
State the verse and identify the ambiguous particle
Read the verse (3:126-128) and locate the particle 'aw' in 'or He relents to them' and 'or He punishes them'. Note that the verse also contains 'you have no say in the matter.'
The particle appears twice; the first occurrence is the focus.
2
List the possible meanings of 'aw' and their impact
The passage mentions that 'aw' can mean 'or' (simple disjunction), 'until' (حتى), or 'unless' (إلا أن). Each changes the temporal or conditional relationship between the clauses.
The meaning 'until' suggests the Prophet's authority is suspended pending divine action.
3
Identify the grammatical dispute: parenthetical clause or not?
Al-Zamakhshari treats 'you have no say' as a parenthetical clause (جملة معترضة), conjoining 'or He relents' to 'to cut off a part'. The Hanafi usul scholars consider 'you have no say' as an independent statement that bars conjoining.
The parenthetical reading creates a unified divine control; the independent reading emphasizes the Prophet's limited role.
4
Compare the Hanafi usul reading with al-Zamakhshari's reading
The Hanafi position (الأصوليون) forbids conjoining 'or He relents' to 'you have no say' based on the plain text and historical context. Al-Zamakhshari allows it, making 'you have no say' a brief interruption.
The author ultimately accepts both as valid (فكلا الأمرين صحيح).
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The legal implication: whether the Prophet had any authority to supplicate for or against the disbelievers. According to the Hanafi reading, he had no say at all until Allah relented or punished; according to al-Zamakhshari's reading, the verse confirms that all outcomes are from Allah.
The dispute affects the ruling on prophetics seeking revenge or forgiveness in battle.

عليه والمعطوف
أو يتوب عليهم إن أسلموا أو يعذبهم إن أصروا على الكفر وليس لك من أمرهم شيء: إنما أنت عبد مبعوث لإنذارهم، فنظر الأصوليين إنما هو في مجرد قوله: لَيْسَ لَكَ مِنَ الْأَمْرِ شَيْءٍ حتى منعوا العطف عليه ولم يلتفتوا إلى ما سبق، فكلا الأمرين صحيح كما ترى.
Discussion of the word 'aw'. Explanation of the divisions of the third division: due to lack of harmony in the construction, and not upon his saying: 'the matter or something', and it is apparent, but his saying: 'you have no say' can extend to the extent of repentance or punishment, so 'aw' is in the meaning of 'until' or 'unless'. So the meaning is: you have no say in the matter of the disbelievers regarding supplication for evil or seeking intercession until Allah repents to them; then at that time you may seek intercession, or He may punish them, then you may supplicate for evil. And it is narrated that he (the Prophet) sought permission from Allah to supplicate against them, so it was revealed. And it is said: when his face was wounded on the day of Uhud, the Prophet... his companions asked him to supplicate against them, so he said: 'Allah did not send me as a curser, but He sent me as a caller. O Allah, guide my people, for they do not know.' So it was revealed, and Allah forbade supplication against them or asking for guidance for them. Due to lack of harmony in the construction: because of the difference between the conjoined and the conjunction in tense (present and past). And one may say: if what is required from the past is informing about the past, and from the present informing about the future, then conjoining the present to the past is good—ponder. (Al-Qamar) And not upon his saying etc. due to the difference between the conjoined and the conjunction in verb and noun. And it is not hidden from you that it is permissible to conjoin 'the matter' or 'something' by implying 'an' such that the meaning is: you have no say in the matter or concerning their repentance or their punishment, or the meaning is: you have no say in the matter or concerning their repentance or their punishment. Thus said al-Baydawi, and this is conjoining a noun to a noun, not a verb to a noun. (Al-Qamar) His saying: because it is a prohibition, and it may imply continuance. (Al-Muhashshi) 'He (Allah) relents to them' in al-Sirah: 'Allah relented to him' meaning He guided him to repentance. (Al-Qamar) 'Or He punishes them' is conjoined to 'Allah relents to them'. (Al-Qamar) 'When his face was wounded': it is said: the ship cleft the sea i.e. split it. In al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'shajjah' is specific to the face and head linguistically; what is on other parts is called 'jarahah'. (Al-Qamar) 'Day of Uhud' with dammah on alif and ha: a mountain near Medina where a great battle occurred. (Al-Qamar) 'So it was revealed' in al-Tafsir al-Kabir: It is narrated that Utbah wounded him and broke his incisor, so he began wiping the blood from his face while Salim, the freed slave of... = Al-Bukhari in his Sahih no. 3842, chapter on 'You have no say in the matter' (Al-Imran: 128); al-Nasa'i no. 1078, chapter on cursing hypocrites in qunut; al-Tirmidhi no. 3004, chapter from Surat Al-Imran; Ahmad in his Musnad no. 5674 from Ibn Umar. The wording of al-Tirmidhi: The Messenger of Allah said on the day of Uhud: 'O Allah, curse Abu Sufyan, O Allah, curse al-Harith ibn Hisham, O Allah, curse Safwan ibn Umayyah.' He said: Then was revealed: 'You have no say in the matter.' Also recorded by al-Bukhari in his Sahih, chapter 'You have no say in the matter' and al-Tirmidhi no. 3002, chapter from Surat Al-Imran from Anas. The wording of al-Bukhari from Anas: The Prophet's face was wounded on the day of Uhud, so he said: 'How can a people who wounded their prophet prosper?' Then was revealed: 'You have no say in the matter.' Also recorded by Ibn Jarir from Qatadah. [Ishraq al-Absar: 11] Explanation of the divisions of the third division, and this is what the usul scholars adhered to. The author of al-Kashshaf mentioned that His saying: 'or He relents to them' is conjoined to His saying: 'to cut off a part of those who disbelieve or suppress them', and His saying: 'you have no say in the matter' (Al-Imran: 128; 127) is a parenthetical clause between them. The meaning is that Allah is the owner of their affair; either He destroys them or defeats them (Al-Imran: 128), and what is conjoined: 'or He relents to them if they become Muslim, or He punishes them if they persist in disbelief, and you have no say in their matter: you are only a servant sent to warn them.' So the view of the usul scholars is only regarding the mere statement: 'You have no say in the matter' such that they forbade conjoining it to what preceded. But both views are correct, as you see.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a detailed grammatical and exegetical analysis of the word 'aw' (أو) in Quran 3:128. The author, following the Hanafi usul tradition, explores multiple interpretations of the verse to clarify the legal and theological implications. The core issue is the syntactic relationship of the clause 'or He relents to them' (أو يتوب عليهم) to the surrounding text.

The discussion begins by noting that some scholars interpret 'aw' as meaning 'until' (حتى) or 'unless' (إلا أن), especially given the narrative context of the Battle of Uhud where the Prophet was wounded. This interpretation yields the meaning that the Prophet had no authority to supplicate against the disbelievers until Allah either relented to them (if they repented) or punished them (if they persisted). The report that the Prophet sought permission to curse them but was instructed otherwise supports this.

The author then addresses a grammatical objection: lack of harmony (عدم اتساق النظم) if 'aw' is taken as a simple disjunction, because the conjoined verbs differ in tense (past and present). However, he offers a resolution: conjoining a present tense verb to a past tense verb is acceptable when the meaning distinguishes between past and future events. He further cites al-Baydawi's view that 'aw' can conjoin nouns rather than verbs by implying 'an' (أن), yielding alternative readings.

The passage also includes a historical report from al-Tafsir al-Kabir and other sources about the revelation of the verse. The key interpretative dispute is between al-Zamakhshari (author of al-Kashshaf) and the majority of usul scholars (الأصوليون). Al-Zamakhshari considered the clause 'you have no say' as a parenthetical (جملة معترضة) and conjoined 'or He relents' to 'to cut off' earlier in the verse. The usul scholars, however, focused on the plain text 'you have no say' and forbade conjoining it to what follows, but the author concludes that both interpretations are valid. This illustrates the Hanafi method of accommodating multiple valid readings of a text when they do not contradict definitive proofs.

Key Terms
أو (aw): In this passage, 'aw' is analyzed as possibly meaning 'until' (حتى) or 'unless' (إلا أن), or as a simple disjunctive particle ('or').
عطف ('atf): Syntactic conjoining of one clause or word to another using a conjunction (here 'aw').
جملة معترضة (jumla mu'tarida): A parenthetical clause inserted between two syntactically connected elements.

The Obligation of Permission for Each Entry: Rational and Linguistic Clues
Explaining rational and linguistic clues for permission condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of combining rational (aqli) and linguistic (lafzi) clues to derive a ruling from a Quranic text.

Core Idea
Permission must be sought for each entry because both reason and textual context require it.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary demonstrates how scholars employ both rational and linguistic clues to derive a precise legal obligation. The verse in Surah Al-Ahzab prohibits entering the Prophet's house without permission, and the subsequent verse explains that doing so caused harm. This dual evidence reinforces that a single blanket permission is insufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary textual evidence
Locate the key phrase in the verse that states the prohibition and exception: 'لا تدخلوا... إلا أن يؤذن لكم'.
The exception 'إلا أن يؤذن لكم' is the linguistic clue.
2
Distinguish the two types of clues
Separate the rational clue (aqli) — that entering without permission causes harm — from the linguistic clue (lafzi) — the explicit exception in the text.
Rational clues are based on general human reasoning, while linguistic clues are derived from the words themselves.
3
Understand how each clue supports the obligation
The linguistic clue shows permission is required; the rational clue shows that each instance of entry causes harm, so permission must be sought each time, not just once.
Thus, the obligation is for every entry, not a single general permission.
4
Recognize the Hanafi methodology
Hanafi usul validates using both types of clues to reach a ruling, emphasizing that the context (qarina) can specify the meaning of a text.
This is an example of 'al-istidlal bi al-qara'in' in action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما وجوب الإذن لكل دخول في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَدْخُلُوا بُيُوتَ النَّبِيِّ إِلَّا أَنْ يُؤْذَنَ لَكُمْ﴾ (الأحزاب: ٥٣) فمستفاد من القرينة العقلية واللفظية، وهي قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ ذَلِكُمْ كَانَ يُؤْذِي النَّبِيَّ﴾ أي القرينة اللفظية (الأحزاب: ٥٣) الآية.
As for the obligation of permission for every entry in His statement, the Exalted: 'Do not enter the houses of the Prophet unless permission is given to you' (Al-Ahzab:53) – it is derived from rational and linguistic clues, namely His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, that used to harm the Prophet' – meaning the linguistic clue – (Al-Ahzab:53) the verse.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining how the obligation of seeking permission for each entry is derived from the verse in Surah Al-Ahzab. The author points out that this obligation is based on two clues: a rational clue ('aqli) – that every rational person knows entering someone's house without permission is blameworthy – and a linguistic clue (lafzi) – the subsequent verse stating that the previous practice harmed the Prophet. Thus, no entry is allowed without explicit permission each time.

Key Terms
قرينة (qarina): A contextual clue that indicates the intended meaning

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) From both rational and linguistic clues
C) From consensus of the companions
D) From analogy with other houses

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, rulings can be sharpened by combining explicit textual evidence with rational contextual clues, ensuring a more precise legal obligation.
