Evidence for the Authority of Khabar al-Wahid
Explaining proofs for accepting solitary reports and refuting circularity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proofs for the authority of khabar al-wahid and explain how they refute the circularity objection.

Core Idea
The Companions' consensus and rational necessity establish that khabar al-wahid is binding for action.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar presents the Hanafi argument for accepting solitary reports as valid legal evidence. We will examine two proofs: the ijma of the Companions and the rational necessity (ma'qul) that prevents suspension of rulings. Additionally, we will see how the text refutes the objection that the proofs themselves rely on ahad reports, ensuring the argument is not circular.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main proofs
Read the passage and locate the two proofs mentioned: 'al-ijma' and 'al-ma'qul'. Understand that these are given as evidence for the authority of solitary reports.
These proofs are in addition to the initial point that ahad reports accepted by the ummah attain the status of mashhur.
2
Understand the ijma proof
Focus on the story of Abu Bakr's argument with the Ansar using the hadith 'الأئمة من قريش'. Note that the Companions accepted this solitary report without objection, demonstrating consensus on the practice of using ahad reports as evidence.
The ijma itself is transmitted by tawatur, avoiding circularity.
3
Understand the rational (ma'qul) proof
Consider the statement: 'al-mutawatir wa al-mashhur la yujadani fi kull hadith'. Why must ahad reports be accepted to avoid suspension of rulings? This is a rational necessity.
This proof does not rely on transmitted reports, so it is not subject to circularity.
4
Analyze the refutation of circularity
The text anticipates the objection that proving ahad reports by ahad reports is circular. Explain how the text responds: the ijma is transmitted by tawatur, and the ma'qul proof is rational, not based on ahad reports.
Thus the authority of khabar al-wahid is firmly established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The discussion lengthened until Abu Bakr said: 'You know, O Sa'd, that the Messenger of Allah said while you were seated: "Quraysh are the rulers of this affair."' Al-Kirmani said: The statement of the Ansar 'from us an amir and from you an amir' was according to Arab custom among the tribes, except one of them. When it became clear to them that the Prophet said 'the caliphate is in Quraysh', they submitted and pledged allegiance to Abu Bakr. (Al-Qamar) 'On accepting solitary reports' means when they are just. As for the report of a corrupt person about the impurity of water, it is not acted upon without critical examination, as Qadi Khan said. (Al-Qamar) 'Regarding purity' and likewise in transactions, such as a single person's report that so-and-so gave this as a gift to you, etc. (Al-Muhashshi)
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage establishes the authority of solitary reports (khabar al-wahid) in the Hanafi madhhab. It begins by noting that even ahad reports, when accepted by the entire ummah, attain the status of mashhur, so their authority is clear. Then it presents two proofs: (1) Ijma: the Companions used ahad reports as evidence, exemplified by Abu Bakr's argument with the Ansar using the hadith 'الأئمة من قريش', which they accepted without objection, and their general practice of accepting ahad reports on purity rulings. (2) Ma'qul (rational proof): because mutawatir and mashhur reports are not available for every incident, rejecting ahad reports would leave many rulings suspended, which is impractical. The passage then refutes an objection that the proofs for ahad reports are themselves based on ahad reports (circularity). The response is that the ijma of the Companions is transmitted by tawatur, not ahad, and the rational proof is a general rational principle, not a report. Finally, it clarifies that acceptance of ahad reports requires the narrator to be 'adl; a report from a fasiq is not accepted without further examination. The Hanafi position is that ahad reports are authoritative in practical matters (non-creedal) and binding for action.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators not reaching tawatur or mashhur.
المشهور (al-mashhur): A report known to have been transmitted by at least three narrators in each generation, but not reaching tawatur.
الإجماع (al-ijma): Consensus of the mujtahidun of the ummah after the Prophet's death on a ruling.
المعقول (al-ma'qul): Rational proof or analogy; here refers to the rational necessity of accepting ahad reports to avoid suspension of rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary evidence from the Companions that establishes the authority of khabar al-wahid?
A) The consultation of 'Umar with the Ansar
B) The argument of Abu Bakr using the hadith 'الأئمة من قريش' which was accepted without rejection
C) The declaration of Abu Bakr that 'We are the amirs'
D) The claim of Sa'd ibn 'Ubadah about leadership

Key Takeaway
The authority of khabar al-wahid is established by the consensus of the Companions and rational necessity, and the objection of circularity is refuted because the ijma is transmitted by tawatur.

Refutation of the Certainty Requirement and Narrator Classification
Responding to objections and classifying narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi response to the claim that khabar al-wahid requires certainty, and identify the basic classification of narrators.

Core Idea
The Quranic command to follow only what you know does NOT require absolute certainty; 'ilm includes strong probability, so khabar al-wahid is binding.

This passage addresses a key objection to the authority of solitary reports (khabar al-wahid): the verse 'Do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge' (17:36). Some scholars argue this requires certainty for all actions, invalidating khabar al-wahid. The Hanafi response is twofold—restricting the verse to false testimony and interpreting 'ilm as including predominant opinion. The passage then introduces the necessity of assessing narrators, as ahad reports do not reach tawatur.

Guided Path
1
Locate the disputed verse and the opposing claim
Identify the verse (17:36) cited by Ibn Dawood and some hadith scholars to argue that khabar al-wahid does not obligate action because it lacks certainty.
The opposing view requires 'ilm qat'i for all actions.
2
Understand the Hanafi linguistic argument
The Hanafi response uses the usul principle: an indefinite noun (nakira) in a negative context indicates generality (umum). Therefore, 'ilm in the verse includes any knowledge, even predominant opinion (zann).
This principle is key to expanding the scope of 'ilm.
3
Distinguish the two opposing camps and the Hanafi refutation
The text splits opponents into two: (1) those who say khabar al-wahid does not obligate action because it lacks 'ilm, and (2) those who say it necessitates 'ilm because action is entailed. The Hanafi response refutes both: (1) would reject zanni Quranic texts; (2) absurdly claims zanni yields certainty.
The first group is refuted by reductio; the second by absurdity.
4
Recognize the practical outcome: narrator classification
Since khabar al-wahid provides only zann, the narrator's reliability must be assessed. Narrators are classified as known (ma'ruf) or unknown (majhul); the known are further divided into those known for fiqh (mujtahidun) and those known for 'adala.
This classification prepares for evaluating hadith authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

باب أقسام السنة بيان أحوال الراوي أي لا تتبع ما لا علم لك، فالعلم لازم للعمل، والعمل ملزوم للعلم، فإذا كان كذلك فلا يوجب العمل؛ لأنه لا يوجب العلم، أو يوجب العلم؛ لأنه يوجب العمل لانتفاء اللازم أو لثبوت الملزوم ، نشر على ترتيب اللف أي لا يوجب العمل لانتفاء لازمه وهو العلم، أو يوجب العلم لثبوت ملزومه، وهو العمل والجواب أن النص محمول على شهادة الزور، أو المعنى لا تتبع ما ليس لك علم بوجه ما بدليل وقوع النكرة في سياق النفي. ثم لما كان خبر الواحد لم تبلغ رواته حد التواتر والشهرة، فلا بد أن يعرف حال راويه بأنه إما معروف أو مجهول والمعروف إمّا معروف بالفقه أو بالعدالة، والمجهول على خمسة أنواع، فاشتغل ببيانه. بيان أحوال الراوي]

على شهادة الزور فمراد الآية أن لا تشهد شهادة كاذبة بغير علم (القمر) بدليل وقوع إلخ يعني أن لفظ العلم نكرة وقعت في الآية تحت النفي، فيفيد العموم، وحينئذ فالمراد بالعلم هو الاعتقاد الراجح المستفاد من سند، سواء كان قطعًا أو ظنًا، واستعماله بهذا المعنى شائع، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) إن عرف أي بعد كونه عادلاً صاحب الورع. (القمر)
والتقدم في الاجتهاد كلمة "في" بمعنى اللام أي التقدم على غيره درجةً لأجل الاجتهاد.(القمر)
And it was said: There is no action etc.: That is, action is not obligatory unless there is knowledge, i.e., certainty, and the proponent is Ibn Dawood and some hadith scholars. (Al-Qamar) Al-Bayhaqi narrated it in his Sunan, no. 5081, vol. 3 p. 121 from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him), and Imam Ahmad narrated it from the hadith of Abu Burdah. [Ishraq al-Absar: 17]
Chapter on divisions of the Sunnah: Explanation of the states of the narrator. That is, do not follow what you have no knowledge of. So knowledge is necessary for action, and action is entailed by knowledge. Therefore, if that is the case, then the solitary report does not necessitate action because it does not necessitate knowledge, or it necessitates knowledge because it necessitates action due to the absence of the necessary condition or to the presence of the entailed condition. He arranged according to the order of the wording: i.e., either it does not necessitate action due to the absence of its necessary condition (knowledge), or it necessitates knowledge due to the presence of its entailed condition (action). And the answer is that the text is interpreted as bearing false witness, or the meaning is: do not follow what you have no knowledge at all, as indicated by the occurrence of the indefinite (nakira) in the context of negation. Then, since the solitary report's narrators do not reach the level of tawatur or shuhra, it is necessary to know the state of its narrator: whether he is known or unknown. The known is either known for fiqh or for 'adala, and the unknown is of five types, so he set about explaining them. Explanation of the states of the narrator.
And he said: The narrator, if he is known for fiqh and precedence in ijtihad, like the Rightly Guided Caliphs and the 'Abdullahs [Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Abbas, etc.], then does not... (by qiyas shar'i) ...necessitate etc.: This is the madhhab of Ibn Dawood. (Al-Qamar) Or it necessitates knowledge means that those who say there is no action except with knowledge split into two groups: one group said that the solitary report does not necessitate action due to the absence of its necessary condition (knowledge), and another group said that the solitary report necessitates knowledge because its entailed condition (action) is realized, so the necessary condition is also realized. The first group is refuted that from your statement it would follow that one should not act upon the apparent meanings of the Quran because they are not certain (zanni al-dalalah). The second group is refuted for claiming that a zanni al-dalalah text yields knowledge, which is absurd. (Al-Qamar) 'Or it necessitates knowledge' this is the madhhab of some hadith scholars, among them Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Dawud al-Zahiri, that the text is specifically about matters of creed, because following conjecture in creed is unlawful, and the address in that text is to the Prophet specifically, and this is one of his special characteristics, for it is possible for him to attain knowledge of everything through revelation, but this is not possible for individuals of the ummah, so they must follow conjecture. (Al-Qamar)
'On bearing false witness' so the meaning of the verse is: do not give false testimony without knowledge. (Al-Qamar) 'By the evidence of occurrence etc.' means that the word 'ilm is indefinite occurring in the context of negation, indicating generality, and then the meaning of 'ilm is the preponderant belief derived from a chain, whether it is certain or conjectural, and its usage in this sense is common, as al-Baydawi said. (Al-Qamar) 'If known' means after being 'adl and having piety. (Al-Qamar)
'And precedence in ijtihad' the word 'fi' is in the sense of 'lam', i.e., precedence over others in rank due to ijtihad. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection that only actions based on certain knowledge are obligatory, citing the verse 'ولا تقف ما ليس لك به علم'. The objectors (Ibn Dawood, some hadith scholars) argue that khabar al-wahid does not provide certainty, so it cannot obligate action. The Hanafi response is two-pronged: (1) The verse is interpreted as forbidding false testimony (shahadat al-zur), not as a condition for all actions. (2) The term 'ilm in the verse is indefinite in a negative context, giving it generality, and in common usage 'ilm includes both certainty and predominant opinion (zann). Therefore, the verse does not require absolute certainty. The text then discusses the classification of narrators: since ahad reports do not reach the level of tawatur or shuhra, the reliability of the narrator must be assessed. Narrators are either known (ma'ruf) or unknown (majhul). The known are further divided into those known for fiqh (i.e., mujtahidun) and those known for 'adala (justice). The unknown are of five types, which will be explained later. The passage also engages with the views of Ibn Dawood, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and Dawud al-Zahiri, who restrict the requirement of certainty to creedal matters (as the verse addresses the Prophet), while in practical matters the ummah must act on conjecture.

Key Terms
العلم (al-'ilm): Certainty or predominant opinion (zann) based on evidence; in the response, it is argued to include both.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or more narrators but not meeting tawatur or shuhra.
شهادة الزور (shahadat al-zur): False testimony; one interpretation of the verse.
العدالة (al-'adala): Integrity of the narrator, encompassing truthfulness and piety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi response to the claim that khabar al-wahid is invalid because it does not provide certainty ('ilm qat'i)?
A) Khabar al-wahid does provide certainty if it is sahih
B) The verse is only about false testimony, not a general requirement
C) Khabar al-wahid is only valid in matters of 'ibadah, not transactions
D) The requirement of certainty only applies to the Prophet, not the ummah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends the authority of khabar al-wahid by interpreting 'ilm in the Quran as including predominant opinion, and by restricting the verse to false testimony, thereby preserving the operative force of ahad reports.

Reconciling Hadith with the Quran: The Hanafi Method
Explains how to reconcile hadith that apparently contradicts the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of 'ard' to reconcile a hadith that appears to contradict a Quranic text, distinguishing between qat'i and zanni Quranic texts.

Core Idea
When a hadith contradicts a qat'i Quranic text, interpret the hadith, not abandon it.

One of the most important skills in usul al-fiqh is knowing how to handle apparent contradictions between primary sources. The Hanafi school has a clear method: present the hadith to the Quran and established principles. If the Quranic text is definitive (qat'i), the hadith must be interpreted in a way that does not conflict. This lesson walks through two classic examples and the reasoning behind the Hanafi approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle of 'Ard'
Read the opening sentence: 'And if it is [opposed] by way of presentation...' Understand that 'ard' means presenting a hadith to the established usul to test its applicability. This is a key Hanafi methodology.
The term 'ard' here is a technical term for testing hadith against stronger proofs.
2
Examine the First Example: Fatiha Hadith
Consider the hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatiha.' Compare it to Quran 73:20: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran.' Identify that the Quranic command is general (amm) and the hadith restricts it. Determine which is qat'i and which is zanni.
The Quranic text is qat'i al-dalala (definitive in meaning); the hadith is khabar al-wahid (zanni al-thubut).
3
Apply the Hanafi Reconciliation Method
Since the Quran is qat'i and the hadith is zanni, the hadith cannot override the Quran. Interpret the negation in the hadith as 'negation of perfection' (nafy al-kamal), not validity. Hence reciting Fatiha is wajib, not fard.
This is a classic Hanafi hermeneutical tool to harmonize texts.
4
Examine the Second Example: Touching Genitals Hadith
The hadith 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform ablution' seems to contradict Quran 9:108 which praises people who purify themselves, implying that touching the penis during istinja is not impure. Note the Hanafi response: they rely on a stronger hadith (from Talq ibn Ali) and interpret the Busra hadith metaphorically.
The Hanafis also argue that the hadith of men (Talq) is stronger in terms of preservation.
5
Contrast with Non-Definitive Quranic Texts
The text also mentions a case where the Quran is not qat'i: the hadith forbidding marrying a woman over her aunt. Here, the Quranic text is general (amm) but not definitive, so a sahih hadith can specify (takhsis) it. Understand when specification is allowed.
If the Quranic text is zanni al-dalala (like general permissibility), a sahih hadith can restrict it.

(القمر) من مس ذكره إلخ فالشافعي له عمل بهذا الحديث، ونحن عملنا بحديث طلق بن على عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: وهل هو إلا مضغة منه أو بضعة منه" فإن حديث الرجال أقوى، لأنهم أحفظ للعلم وأضبط، كذا قال ابن الهمام، وقد يؤوّل حديث بسرة بأن مس الذكر كناية عن إخراج شيء منه كذا في "الصبح الصادق". (القمر) وفيه مس الذكر أي لا بدّ في حال الاستنجاء من مس الذكر بباطن الكف، وهو بمنزلة البول حدث على حسب حكم الحديث؛ فلزم مدح الإنسان بالتطهير حال الحدث، وهو فاحش، ويمكن أن يقال: إن مدحه إنما هو بالاستنجاء بسبب إزالة النجاسة الحقيقية، وما لزم ههنا من الحدث فهو ضمني، فهو لا يضار المدح، تأمل. (القمر) أخرجه البخاري رقم: ۷۲۳ ، باب وجوب القراءة للإمام والمأموم في الصلوات كلها، ومسلم رقم ٣٩٤، باب وجوب قراءة الفاتحة في كل ركعة، والترمذي رقم: ۲٤٧ باب ما جاء أنه لا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب، وأبو داود رقم: ۸۲۲ باب من ترك القراءة في صلاته بفاتحة الكتاب وابن ماجه رقم: ۸۳۷، باب القراءة خلف الإمام، عن عبادة الصامت له بألفاظ مختلفة متقاربة المعنى. بن ** أخرجه الترمذي رقم: ۸۲ باب الوضوء من مس ،الذكر، وأبو داود رقم: ۱۸۱ ، باب الوضوء من مس الذكر، والنسائي رقم ٤٤٧ باب الوضوء من مس الذكر وابن ماجه رقم ٤٧٩، باب الوضوء من مس الذكر، عن بُسرة بنت صفوان قال الترمذي حديث حسن صحيح.
And if it is [opposed] by way of presentation, i.e., by contradicting the Book—like the hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book' contradicts the general meaning of His statement: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' [73:20], and the hadith 'Whoever touches his penis let him perform ablution' contradicts His statement: 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' [9:108] because it is in praise of people who cleanse themselves with water, and it involves touching the penis. Masjid Quba. That is, after the stone. By way of presentation: i.e., by presenting the hadith to the principles. (al-Qamar) That it contradicts the Book, i.e., that which is definitive in indication. And if the Book is not definitive in indication and the hadith is transmitted with a sahih chain, then that hadith is not abandoned, rather the verse is interpreted—like the hadith 'Do not marry a woman over her paternal aunt or maternal aunt,' for it is a sahih hadith acted upon, and it contradicts the general meaning of His statement: 'Lawful to you are [all] beyond those' [4:24] i.e., beyond the mentioned prohibitions. So the hadith is not abandoned, rather its general meaning is specified. Thus stated Bahral-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali, and the detail is in al-Tahqiq. (al-Qamar) 'No prayer except with Fatiha, etc.' So the Shafi'is used this hadith to argue that reciting the Fatiha is obligatory. And we say: the obligatory according to us is only absolute recitation, due to His statement: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' [73:20]. And restricting it to the Fatiha is an addition to the text, and that is not permissible by khabar al-wahid. So at most, the Fatiha is wajib (necessary), and the negation in his statement 'No prayer' is negation of perfection. Understand. (al-Qamar) 'Whoever touches his penis, etc.' So al-Shafi'i acted on this hadith, and we acted on the hadith of Talq ibn Ali from the Prophet: 'Is it anything but a piece of him or a part of him?' For the hadith of men is stronger because they are more retentive of knowledge and more precise. Thus said Ibn al-Humam. And the hadith of Busra may be interpreted that touching the penis is a metaphor for extracting something from it, as stated in al-Subh al-Sadiq. (al-Qamar) And in it is touching the penis: i.e., it is necessary during istinja' (cleansing after relieving oneself) to touch the penis with the inner part of the palm, and it is akin to urine, an event according to the ruling of the hadith. So it necessitates praising a person for purification while in a state of impurity, which is repulsive. And it can be said that the praise is only for istinja' due to removing real impurity, and what occurs here of impurity is incidental, so it does not harm the praise. Consider. (al-Qamar) It was transmitted by al-Bukhari no. 723, chapter: Obligation of recitation for the Imam and follower in all prayers, and Muslim no. 394, chapter: Obligation of reciting Fatiha in every rak'ah, and al-Tirmidhi no. 247, chapter: That there is no prayer except with Fatiha, and Abu Dawud no. 822, chapter: On leaving recitation of Fatiha in prayer, and Ibn Majah no. 837, chapter: Recitation behind the Imam, from Ubadah ibn al-Samit with different but similar wordings. ** It was transmitted by al-Tirmidhi no. 82, chapter: Ablution from touching the penis, and Abu Dawud no. 181, chapter: Ablution from touching the penis, and al-Nasa'i no. 447, chapter: Ablution from touching the penis, and Ibn Majah no. 479, chapter: Ablution from touching the penis, from Busra bint Safwan, al-Tirmidhi said: it is a hasan sahih hadith.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage addresses a key usul issue: how to handle a hadith that seems to contradict a Quranic text. It begins by defining the situation as 'by way of presentation' (bi al-ard), meaning the hadith is presented to the established principles (usul). Specifically, it deals with two cases: (1) the hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatiha' against the Quranic command to recite 'what is easy from the Quran' (73:20); (2) the hadith 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform ablution' against the verse praising the people of Quba who love to purify themselves (9:108) – which implies they touch their penis during istinja'. The Hanafi approach is as follows: If the Quranic text is definitive (qat'i) in indication, then a hadith that is zanni in transmission (khabar al-wahid) cannot override it. Therefore, the hadith must be interpreted in a way that reconciles it. For the 'Fatiha' hadith, the Hanafis interpret the negation 'No prayer' as negation of perfection, not validity; hence reciting the Fatiha is wajib (necessary) but not fard (obligatory), while the absolute Quranic command makes any recitation sufficient. For the 'touching penis' hadith, Hanafis rely on a stronger hadith from Talq ibn Ali that treats the penis as a part of the body that does not invalidate wudu, and interpret the Busra hadith metaphorically or limit it. If the Quranic text is not definitive (like the general permissibility of marrying any woman beyond those prohibited), a sahih hadith may specify (takhsis) that general rule, as in the hadith forbidding combining a woman with her aunt. This shows the Hanafi principle of giving precedence to the Quran when it is qat'i, and otherwise using the Sunnah to qualify the Quran.

Key Terms
عرض (Ard): Presenting a hadith to the established principles (usul) to test its authenticity or applicability
مخالفة الكتاب (Mukhalafat al-Kitab): Apparent contradiction between a hadith and a Quranic verse
نفي الكمال (Nafy al-Kamal): A negation that negates perfection, not existence or validity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatiha' interpreted as negation of perfection rather than validity?
A) Because the hadith is weak
B) Because the Quranic command is general and qat'i, and the hadith is zanni
C) Because the hadith was abrogated
D) Because the Fatiha is not obligatory at all

Key Takeaway
When a sahih hadith appears to contradict a qat'i Quranic text, the Hanafi method is to interpret the hadith (e.g., as nafy al-kamal) rather than to reject it, maintaining the epistemological priority of the Quran.

Classification of Revelation (Wahi) in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the types of divine revelation to the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four types of apparent revelation in Hanafi usul and explain how each is distinguished from the others.

Core Idea
Revelation is either apparent (zahir) or hidden (batin); the apparent includes Quran, angelic indication, divine inspiration, and hadith qudsi.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar presents the foundational Hanafi classification of wahi (revelation). Understanding this taxonomy is crucial for discerning the authority of different types of prophetic knowledge. The commentary expands the original three types to four, adding hadith qudsi, and refutes a fabricated story that impugns prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main division
Revelation is divided into apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin). The apparent is what reaches the Prophet through sensory means or clear perception.
2
List the three original types of apparent revelation
(a) Quran delivered by the angel Gabriel with audible words, (b) indirect indication from the angel without speech, (c) direct inspiration (ilham) into the heart.
The text states: 'the apparent is of three types'.
3
Note the commentary's addition of a fourth type
Hadith qudsi, revealed directly by Allah without angelic mediation, is added by later scholars as a separate category.
Bahr al-Ulum and others support this addition.
4
Understand the evidence for each type
The Quranic verse 16:102 is cited for the first type; the hadith about the Holy Spirit breathing into the heart for the second; and the concept of ilham for the third.
The verse 'Qul nazzalahu ruh al-qudus...' is the key proof.
5
Recognize the refutation of the gharaniq story
The text explicitly denies that the devil could interfere with the Prophet's recitation, preserving the integrity of prophetic transmission.
This refutes a fabricated story and upholds 'ismah.

(السنبلي ظاهر وباطن يطلق الوحي عليهما بالحقيقة والمجاز أو بالاشتراك. (القمر) ثلاثة أنواع لا بل أربعة أنواع، والنوع الرابع ما سمعه تعالى بلا توسط الملك، من وهو الحديث القدسي، كذا قال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي له وقال الكرماني في شرح البخاري: إن القرآن معجز لفظه بواسطة جبرائيل عليا والقدسي غير معجز، وينزل بدون الواسطة، وقال ابن الملك في شرح "المشارق": إن الحديث القدسي ما أخبر الله به نبيه بإلهام أو بمنام، فأخبر الله عن ذلك المعنى بعبارة نفسه. فالفرق بينه وبين الحديث النبوي أنه إذا عبر عن المعنى الموحى إليه بألفاظه ونَسَبها إليه تعالى فقدسي وإلا فنبوي كذا قال العلي القاري لله. (القمر) بآية قاطعة أي بعلم ضروري قطعي بأن هذا المبلغ مَلَك مرسل من الله تعالى، وما روي من سورة النجم، ووصل إلى هذه الآية: أفرأيتم اللات والعزى ومناة الثالثة "الأخرى أدرج الشيطان هذه الكلمة: "تلك الغرانيق العلى، إن شفاعتهن كترتجي" فبعضهم قالوا: إن النبي علم أن هذه الكلمة من قول جبريل عليه ومن الوحي الإلهي، فقرأها بلسانه المباركة وبعضهم قالوا: إنه قرأها الشيطان بحيث علم الحاضرون أنها على لسان النبي ، ففرح المشركون وقالوا إن محمدًا مدح ،آلهتنا واشتهر هذا، فجاء جبريل عليقة وقال: "إن هذه الكلمة ما قلته، وليست من الوحي، بل هي مقولة "الشيطان فهذا كله من الموضوعات وضعها الملاحدة لإبطال الشريعة والحق أنه لا دخل للشيطان في أقواله الشريفة التبليغية، ولو كان كذالك لارتفع الأمان عن أنه لما قرء جرت التبليغ، ويفنى الهداية رأسًا، نعوذ بالله ذالك، كذا قالوا. (القمر) وهو أي ما نزل بلسان الملك. (القمر) من الروح الأمين: أي جبريل عليه فإنه أمين. (القمر) الروح الأمين إلخ الروح بالضم ما به حياة الأنفس، يُذكر ويُؤنّث، وهو الأشهر، وعليه قول الحريري: وكادت تبلغ الروح التراقي، والوحي وجبريل وعيسى والنفخ وأمر = فصل في أفعال النبي 7.A بيان أقسام الوحي يعني القرآن الذي قال الله تعالى في حقه: قُلْ نَزَّلَهُ رُوحُ الْقُدُسِ مِنْ رَبِّكَ بِالْحَقِّ، والثاني (النحل : ١٠٢) ما بينه بقوله: أو ثبت عنده ال بإشارة الملك من غير بيان بالكلام كما قال علي: "إن روح القدس نفث في روعي أن نفسا لن تموت حتى تستكمل رزقها * والثالث ما بينه بقوله: أو تبدى بقلبه بلا شبهة بالهام من الله تعالى بأن أراه بنور من عنده ، وهذا هو المسمّى بالإلهام، ويشترك فيه الأولياء أيضًا وإن كان إلهامهم يحتمل الخطاء والصواب، وإلهامه عليه لا يحتمل نفس الإلهام إلا الصواب، ولم يذكر ما كان بالهاتف؛ لأنه لم يكن من شأنه عليه، أو لم تثبت به أحكام الشرع، وكذا لم يذكر ما كان في المنام؛ لأنه كان في ابتداء النبوة لم تثبت به أحكام الشرع. = و المنام القدس : النبوة وحكم الله وأمره، وتطلق الأرواح على قسم من المعدنيات، وعند أصحاب الكيمياء على المياه المقطرة من الأدوية وغيرها، ويقال: خرجوا بأرواح من العشي أي بأوائل منها، والروح الأعظم الله تعالى وروح أحد الأقانيم الثلاثة، والروح الأمين عند المسلمين لقب جبريل علية. "أقرب". (السنبلي) يعني القرآن الذي إلخ وأما الأحاديث فبعضها نزل به الروح الأمين، وبعضها نزل به الملك الآخر. (القمر) روح القدس: أضيف الروح إلى القدس وهو الطهر كما يقال حاتم الجود وزيد الخير، والمراد الروح المقدس، وحاتم الجوّاد، وزيد الخير والمقدّس المطهر من المأثم كذا في الكشاف، وإنما سُمي جبريل عليه روحًا لأن بالروح حياة الأبدان كذالك بجبريل عليه حياة الدين فإنه واسطة نزول الوحي، كذا في "التفسير الكبير". (القمر) أو ثبت أي مع علمه الضروري بأن المبلغ ملك مرسل من ملك مرسل من الله تعالى. (القمر) بإشارة الملك: وذلك بأن الروح للطافته يناسب الملكَ؛ فيخلق الله تعالى في الروح العلم بالملك، ويُعرف الروح ببعض هيأة الملك أن الملك يقصد هذا، وهذه إشارة الملك (القمر) رزقها تتمة الحديث : فاتقوا الله وأجملوا في الطلب. (المحشي) أو تُبدى: أي مع العلم الضروري بأن هذا الإلهام من الله تعالى (القمر) بإلهام من الله تعالى: أي إيقاع في القلب بلا كسب في اليقظة. (القمر) بالهاتف إلخ مأخوذ من الهتف يقال هتفت الحمامة هتفًا صاتت أو مدت صوتها، وفلان هتافا صاح به، ومنه أهتف "بالأنصار أي نادهم وادّعهم، وفي "القاموس": "هتف فلانا وبه" مدحه، "سمعت هاتفًا يهتف" إذا كنت تسمع الصوت ولا تبصر أحدًا، اللسان الهاتف أيضًا من يسمع صوته ولا يُرى شخصه. "أقرب". (السنبلي) لم تثبت به إلخ والغرض والوحي الذي يثبت به الأحكام الشرعية غالبًا. (القمر) أخرجه ابن حبان عن ابن مسعود لاله مرفوعا، وفي رواية أن روح القدس نفث في روعي أن نفسا لن تموت حتى تستكمل أجلها ورزقها، فاتقوا الله وأجملوا في الطلب" الحديث ولها معانٍ أخر رواه ابن أبي الدنيا في "القناعة" وصححه الحاكم و أورده أصحاب الغريب. [إشراق الأبصار ٢٧]
Chapter on the actions of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, an explanation of the types of revelation. Because he never did something forbidden or disliked at all, so it must be permissible. When he finished dividing the Sunnah regarding us, he began dividing it regarding him, and explaining his method in manifesting the rulings of the law by revelation. He said: Explanation of the types of revelation (i.e., relative to us). Revelation is of two types: apparent and hidden. The apparent is of three types: The first: what is established by the tongue of the angel, i.e., Gabriel, peace be upon him, so it falls into his ear, after his knowledge that the conveyer is Gabriel, peace be upon him, by a decisive sign that negates doubt and uncertainty about it being Gabriel or not. It is that which was revealed to him by the tongue of the Trustworthy Spirit, peace be upon him. (Al-Qamar:) "Revelation" etc. with fathah on the waw: everything you convey to another so that he may know it, howsoever it is. Then it became predominant for what is conveyed to the prophets, peace be upon them, from God Almighty. It is said: revelation is informing in secret, and it may be used to mean the passive participle. (Al-Sanbali:) Apparent and hidden: revelation is applied to both literally and metaphorically, or by common usage. (Al-Qamar:) Three types, but rather four types. The fourth type is what He, exalted, heard without the medium of the angel, and it is the sacred hadith. Thus said Bahr al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali. Al-Kirmani said in his commentary on al-Bukhari: The Quran is miraculous in its wording through the medium of Gabriel, while the sacred hadith is not miraculous, and it descends without mediation. Ibn al-Malik said in his commentary on al-Mashariq: The sacred hadith is what God informed His prophet by inspiration or dream, then God informed about that meaning with His own expression. The difference between it and the prophetic hadith is that if he expresses the revealed meaning with his own words and attributes them to Him, it is sacred; otherwise it is prophetic. So said Ali al-Qari. (Al-Qamar:) "By a decisive sign" means by necessary definitive knowledge that this conveyer is an angel sent from God Almighty. What is transmitted from Surat al-Najm, up to the verse "Have you considered al-Lat and al-Uzza, and Manat, the third, the other?" The devil inserted this word: "Those are the high swans, whose intercession is desired." Some said that the prophet knew that this word was from the speech of Gabriel, peace be upon him, and from divine revelation, so he recited it with his blessed tongue. Others said that the devil recited it so that those present knew it was on the tongue of the prophet, peace be upon him, and the polytheists rejoiced saying that Muhammad praised their gods. This became famous. Then Gabriel, peace be upon him, came and said: "This word I did not say, and it is not from revelation, but rather it is a saying of the devil." All this is fabricated by heretics to nullify the law. The truth is that the devil has no entry into his noble declaratory statements. If that were so, the trustworthiness of transmission would be removed, and guidance would be entirely annihilated. We seek refuge with God from that. So they said. (Al-Qamar:) And it means what descended by the tongue of the angel. (Al-Qamar:) "From the Trustworthy Spirit" i.e., Gabriel, peace be upon him, for he is trustworthy. (Al-Qamar:) "The Trustworthy Spirit" etc. "Al-ruh" with dammah means that by which the life of souls exists; it is masculine and feminine, and the former is more famous. Upon it is the saying of al-Hariri: "And the soul almost reached the collarbones." And the revelation, Gabriel, Jesus, the blowing, and the command = Chapter on the actions of the Prophet 7.A. Explanation of the types of revelation means the Quran about which God Almighty said: "Say: The Holy Spirit has brought it down from your Lord with truth." (Al-Nahl:102) The second: what he explained by his saying: "Or it is established by him by the indication of the angel without explanation by speech," as Ali said: "The Holy Spirit breathed into my heart that no soul will die until it completes its provision." The third: what he explained by his saying: "Or it appears in his heart without doubt by inspiration from God Almighty, that He shows him with a light from Him." This is called inspiration (ilham). The saints also share in it, although their inspiration may contain error and correctness, while his inspiration does not admit of error. He did not mention what comes by the phantom (hatif) because it was not from his way, or because religious rulings are not established by it. Likewise, he did not mention what comes in dreams because it was at the beginning of prophecy; religious rulings are not established by it. = And the dream, the Holy: prophecy, the command of God and His decree. The spirits are also applied to a category of minerals, and according to alchemists to distilled waters from medicines etc. It is said: they went out with spirits of the evening, meaning with its first parts. The Greatest Spirit is God Almighty, and the spirit of one of the three hypostases. The Trustworthy Spirit among Muslims is the title of Gabriel, peace be upon him. "Aqrab". (Al-Sanbali) means the Quran that, etc. As for hadiths, some of them were brought down by the Trustworthy Spirit, and some by another angel. (Al-Qamar) "Holy Spirit" is added to holiness, which is purity, as one says Hatim al-Jud (Hatim of generosity) and Zayd al-Khayr (Zayd of goodness), and what is meant is the sanctified spirit. And Hatim the generous, and Zayd the good, and the sanctified purified from sin, as in al-Kashshaf. He is called spirit because just as the soul gives life to bodies, so Gabriel gives life to religion through revelation. (Al-Qamar) "or he established" means with his necessary knowledge that the conveyer is an angel sent from God Almighty. (Al-Qamar) "by the indication of the angel" that because the spirit, due to its subtlety, corresponds to the angel; so God creates in the spirit knowledge of the angel, and the soul recognizes by some form of the angel that the angel intends this. This is the indication of the angel. (Al-Qamar) "its provision" the completion of the hadith: "So fear God and be moderate in seeking." (Al-Muhashshi) "or appears" means with necessary knowledge that this inspiration is from God Almighty. (Al-Qamar) "by inspiration from God" means a casting into the heart without acquisition while awake. (Al-Qamar) "by the phantom" etc. taken from al-hataf; it is said: the dove cooed, extended its voice; and so-and-so shouted; from it: "call out to the Ansar" i.e., call them and claim them. In al-Qamus: "he called so-and-so and called him" praised him; "I heard a phantom calling" if you hear a voice and do not see anyone; the tongue also says the phantom is one whose voice is heard but his person not seen. "Aqrab". (Al-Sanbali) "not established by it" etc., and the purpose is revelation by which legal rulings are usually established. (Al-Qamar) It was reported by Ibn Hibban from Ibn Mas'ud as marfu', and in another narration: the Holy Spirit breathed into my heart that no soul will die until it completes its term and provision, so fear God and be moderate in seeking. The hadith has other meanings. Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in al-Qana'ah and authenticated by al-Hakim, and it is mentioned by the authors of al-Gharib. [Ishraq al-Absar 27]
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is from Noor al-Anwar, a Hanafi usul work. It classifies revelation (wahi) received by the Prophet (saw). The main division is into apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin). Apparent revelation is further divided into three types: (1) the Quran revealed through the angel Gabriel with audible words and a decisive sign ensuring recognition; (2) indirect indication from the angel without speech, as in the hadith about the Holy Spirit breathing into the heart; (3) direct inspiration (ilham) into the heart without any intermediary. The commentary adds a fourth type: sacred hadith (hadith qudsi) revealed without the medium of an angel. The text also refutes a false story about the 'gharaniq' verses, affirming that the devil has no influence on the Prophet's transmission. Additionally, it explains why revelation via phantom voices or dreams is not included for establishing legal rulings. The passage highlights the Hanafi emphasis on the certainty of prophetic inspiration and the separation of Quran and hadith qudsi from ordinary prophetic hadith.

Key Terms
الوحي (al-wahy): Communication from Allah to a prophet, either directly or through an angel.
ظاهر (zahir): Apparent revelation, perceived through the senses (hearing) or clear indication.
باطن (batin): Hidden revelation, such as inspiration (ilham) without sensory perception.
الإلهام (al-ilham): Inspiration cast into the heart, without angelic or sensory mediation.
الروح الأمين (al-ruh al-amin): The Trustworthy Spirit, i.e., the angel Gabriel (Jibril).
روح القدس (ruh al-qudus): The Holy Spirit, also referring to Gabriel or a divine breath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many types of apparent revelation are mentioned in the original classification (without the commentary's addition)?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of revelation systematically distinguishes the Quran, angelic indications, divine inspiration, and hadith qudsi, each with unique authority in Islamic law.

Three Types of Divine Revelation (Wahy)
Explaining the three categories of external revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three categories of external wahy and explain their respective authority in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Divine revelation to prophets includes three types: Quran, angelic inspiration without words, and direct inspiration (ilham) – each with distinct infallibility.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar classifies the external revelation (wahy) that forms the foundation of Islamic law. Understanding these categories helps you grasp the sources of Shariah: the Quran, the Sunnah (including non-verbal prophetic guidance), and prophetic inspiration. The author also clarifies that while saints may receive inspiration, only prophetic ilham is infallible and legally binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
Read the passage and list the three categories of wahy mentioned: the Quran, angelic indication without words, and direct inspiration (ilham).
The first type is verbal revelation through Jibril; the second is non-verbal angelic communication; the third is direct inspiration from Allah.
2
Distinguish the medium for each
For each type, note the medium: the Quran is sent down by the Holy Spirit (Jibril) with words; the second type is communicated by an angel without articulate speech; the third is placed directly into the heart by Allah without any intermediary.
The hadith of Ali ("the Holy Spirit breathed into my heart") exemplifies the second type.
3
Compare infallibility
The passage states that the Prophet's ilham is infallible, whereas the ilham of saints can be mistaken. Understand why only prophetic inspiration establishes legal rulings.
This is a key distinction: saintly inspiration is not a source of law.
4
Note what is excluded
The author excludes revelation through a hidden voice (hatif) and dreams. Determine the reasons: either these were not part of the Prophet's experience or they do not establish legal rulings.
Dreams occurred at the beginning of prophethood but are not a continuing source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أفعال النبي بيان أقسام الوحي يعني القرآن الذي قال الله تعالى في حقه: قُلْ نَزَّلَهُ رُوحُ الْقُدُسِ مِنْ رَبِّكَ بِالْحَقِّ، والثاني ما بينه بقوله: أو ثبت عنده [؟] بإشارة الملك من غير بيان بالكلام كما قال علي: "إن روح القدس نفث في روعي أن نفسا لن تموت حتى تستكمل رزقها" والثالث ما بينه بقوله: أو تبدى بقلبه بلا شبهة بالهام من الله تعالى بأن أراه بنور من عنده، وهذا هو المسمّى بالإلهام، ويشترك فيه الأولياء أيضًا وإن كان إلهامهم يحتمل الخطاء والصواب، وإلهامه عليه لا يحتمل نفس الإلهام إلا الصواب، ولم يذكر ما كان بالهاتف؛ لأنه لم يكن من شأنه عليه، أو لم تثبت به أحكام الشرع، وكذا لم يذكر ما كان في المنام؛ لأنه كان في ابتداء النبوة لم تثبت به أحكام الشرع.
Chapter on the Actions of the Prophet. Explanation of the divisions of revelation. That is, the Qur'an which Allah said regarding it: 'Say, the Holy Spirit has brought it down from your Lord with truth' (16:102). The second is what he explained by his saying: 'or it is established in his mind by the gesture of the angel without explanation by words' as Ali said: 'Indeed the Holy Spirit breathed into my heart that a soul will not die until it completes its provision.' The third is what he explained by his saying: 'or it is displayed in his heart without doubt by inspiration from Allah, showing him by a light from Him.' This is called inspiration (ilham). The saints also share in it, although their inspiration is subject to error and correctness, while his inspiration does not admit of error in itself. He did not mention what comes through the hatif (unseen voice) because it was not his practice, or because legal rulings are not established by it. Likewise, he did not mention what comes in dreams because it was at the beginning of prophecy and legal rulings are not established by it.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the types of revelation (wahy) that establish legal rulings. The author first mentions the Qur'an, revealed through Jibril (the Holy Spirit) in words. Second, revelation through angelic indication without articulate speech, as exemplified by the hadith of Ali where the Holy Spirit inspired meaning directly. Third, ilham (inspiration) where Allah places knowledge in the heart without intermediary. The author notes that saints also receive ilham, but their ilham can err, whereas the Prophet's ilham is infallible. The author excludes revelation through a hidden voice (hatif) and dreams from the categories that establish legal rulings, either because they were not part of the Prophet's experience or because they occur only in early prophethood and not as a basis for law.

Key Terms
وحي (waḥy): Communication from Allah to a prophet, divided here into three types: direct words (Quran), angelic inspiration without words, and direct inspiration (ilham).
إلهام (ilhām): Inspiration placed by Allah directly into the heart, yielding certainty without a medium.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which type of revelation is shared by saints but is not infallible?
A) The Quran
B) Angelic inspiration without words
C) Ilham (direct inspiration)
D) Revelation through dreams

Key Takeaway
Prophetic wahy comprises three categories, with only the Quran and prophetic sunnah (including non-verbal inspiration) being authoritative sources of law; saintly ilham is fallible and not a source.

How Previous Prophetic Laws Become Binding
Establishes that previous prophets' laws mentioned without disapproval become part of our Sharia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition under which a previous prophetic law becomes binding in the Hanafi school, and apply this rule to differentiate between punitive and general laws.

Core Idea
A past law binds us only when the Quran narrates it without condemnation.

In this passage, the author addresses a critical usul principle: the authority of shara'i' man qablana. The Quran contains many stories of earlier prophets and their legal rulings. How do we know which of those rulings apply to us? The passage provides a clear criterion: if the Quran reports a law without criticizing or altering it, that law becomes part of our Sharia. The author supports this with verses showing that certain prohibitions on Jews were punitive and not general, and with the command to follow the guidance of previous prophets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Read the passage and state in your own words the condition the author sets for a previous prophetic law to become binding on Muslims.
Look for the phrase 'when they are narrated in our book without rejection'.
2
Examine the Negative Proof
The author cites verses about Jewish prohibitions (4:160, 6:146). Explain why these do not become binding on Muslims.
Note the phrase 'That We repaid them for their transgression'.
3
Analyze the Positive Proof
Identify the verse (6:90) that commands following the guidance of previous prophets. Explain how it supports the principle.
Consider the Hanafi rule: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Apply the Principle
Given a Quranic story about a previous prophet that contains a specific law not criticized, state whether that law becomes binding.
Use the example of the prohibition of sodomy from the passage's title.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أفعال النبي في حق قوم لوط عليه يدل على حرمة اللواطة علينا، ومثال ما أنكره علينا بعد القصة: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَبِظُلْمٍ مِنَ الَّذِينَ هَادُوا حَرَّمْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ طَيِّبَاتٍ أُحِلَّتْ لَهُمْ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَلَى الَّذِينَ هَادُوا حَرَّمْنَا كُلَّ ذِي ظُفُرٍ وَمِنَ الْبَقَرِ وَالْغَنَمِ حَرَّمْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ شُحُومَهُمَا﴾ ثم قال: ﴿ذَلِكَ جَزَيْنَاهُمْ بِبَغْيِهِمْ﴾ فعلم أنه لم يكن حرامًا علينا، ثم هذه الشرائع التي تلزمنا إنما تلزمنا على أنه شريعة لرسولنا عليه لا على أنها شرائع للأنبياء عليه السلام السابقة؛ لأنها إذا قصت في كتابنا بلا إنكار صارت تلك جزء من ديننا، وقد قال الله تعالى لنبينا عليه: ﴿أُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ هَدَى اللهُ فَبِهَدَاهُمُ اقْتَدِهْ﴾.
A section on the actions of the Prophet concerning the people of Lut indicates the prohibition of sodomy upon us. An example of what He denied upon us after the story: His saying: 'So because of wrongdoing from those who were Jews, We forbade them good things which were [formerly] lawful to them.' And His saying: 'And to those who were Jews We forbade every [animal] with undivided hooves, and from the cattle and sheep We forbade their fat.' Then He said: 'That We repaid them for their transgression.' So it was understood that it was not forbidden upon us. Then these laws that bind us only bind us as being a Sharia for our Messenger, not as being Sharia of the previous prophets; because when they are narrated in our book without rejection, they become part of our religion. And Allah said to our Prophet: 'Those are the ones whom Allah has guided, so from their guidance take an example.'
Source pages p. 615

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule explaining how the laws of previous prophets relate to the Muslim ummah. The author argues that when the Quran narrates a previous law without any condemnation or alteration, that law becomes part of our Sharia. He supports this with the verse commanding the Prophet to follow the guidance of earlier prophets. The discussion uses the examples of dietary prohibitions imposed on the Jews as a punishment for their wrongdoing, showing that those prohibitions are not binding on Muslims because they were specifically punitive. Thus, the principle is that silence or endorsement in the Quran transmutes past revelations into our own legal heritage.

Key Terms
شرائع الأنبياء السابقة (shara'i' al-anbiya' al-sabiqa): The legal codes of earlier prophets before Prophet Muhammad (PBUH)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition makes a past prophetic law binding on the Muslim ummah according to this passage?
A) It must be explicitly commanded in the Quran.
B) It must be narrated in the Quran without condemnation.
C) It must be confirmed by the Sunnah.
D) It must be practiced by the early Muslims.

Key Takeaway
A previous prophetic law becomes part of our Sharia only when the Quran narrates it without any criticism or alteration.

Al-Quran as Source
intermediate
8 min
The Authority of Ijma': Qur'anic Proofs
Explains three Qur'anic proofs for Ijma' and refutes objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Qur'anic proofs for Ijma', explain the wajh al-dalalah of each, and evaluate the Hanafi response to objections.

Core Idea
Ijma' is a definitive proof because the Qur'an describes the Ummah as just and best, and equates following the believers with obeying the Messenger.

This lesson examines the foundational Qur'anic evidence for the authority of Ijma' as presented in Noor al-Anwar. The commentator cites three verses and then addresses sophisticated objections. Understanding these proofs and the Hanafi rejoinders is essential to grasp why Ijma' is considered a decisive source of law in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Qur'anic proofs
List the three verses: 2:143 (middle nation), 3:110 (best nation), 4:115 (way of the believers).
Each verse is cited to establish the reliability of the community's consensus.
2
Analyze the first proof (2:143)
The term 'middle' (wasat) implies justice. A just community cannot collectively err, so their consensus is authoritative.
Objection: justice does not preclude ijtihad error. Response: error in ijtihad is not sin, but consensus ensures correctness through divine protection.
3
Analyze the second proof (3:110)
The Ummah is described as 'best'. If their consensus could be error, they would not be the best.
Objection: error in some rulings does not negate overall goodness. Response: the verse indicates perfection in religion.
4
Analyze the third proof (4:115)
Following other than the way of the believers is equated with opposing the Messenger, making the way of the believers binding.
Objection: the conjunction may be redundant. Response: the way of the believers is general and not reducible to prophetic command.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds Ijma' as a definitive proof based on these verses and rational arguments, rejecting the views of Mu'tazila, Rawafid, and Khawarij.
The dissenting groups are considered negligible by the text.

باب الإجماع

بيان حكم الإجماع
﴿وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطاً لِتَكُونُوا شُهَدَاءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ﴾، وصفهم بالوسطية، وهي العدالة، فيكون إجماعهم حجة، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ﴾ (آل عمران: ١١٠) والخيرية إنما يكون باعتبار كمالهم في الدين، فيكون إجماعهم حجة، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرَ سَبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ نُوَلِّهِ مَا تَوَلَّى﴾ (النساء: ١١٥) فجعلت مخالفة المؤمنين مثل مخالفة الرسول، فيكون إجماعهم كخبر الرسول حجة قطعية وأمثاله، وقد ضلّ بعض المعتزلة والروافض فقالوا: إن الإجماع ليس بحجة؛
وكذلك: أي كما جعلنا قبلتكم أفضل القبل جعلناكم أمة وَسَطًا أي خيارًا أو عدولاً لتكونوا شهداء على الناس يوم القيامة بتبليغ الأنبياء علية الأحكام الإلهية إليهم عند جحودهم بتبليغهم ، ويكون الرسول عليكم شهيدًا بعد التكم، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) فيكون إجماعهم حجة فإن العدل هو الراسخ على الصراط المستقيم، وليس فيه الزيغ عن سواء السبيل، ولقائل أن يقول: إن العدالة لا تنافي الخطأ في الاجتهاد؛ إذ هو ليس فسقا، بل المجتهد المخطئ مأجور ، فلا دليل في هذه الآية على قطعية إجماع المجتهدين من عصر واحد (القمر) کنتم خير أمة: الخطاب إلى تمام الأمة المحمدية فللموجودين في ذلك الزمان أي الصحابة لم تنجيزا، وللمعدومين في ذلك الزمان عند الوجود أخرجت أي أظهرت للناس. (القمر) فيكون إجماعهم حجة: إذ لو لم يكن إجماعهم حقًا وحجة لكان ضلالاً فكيف يكون الأمة الضالة خير الأمم؟ وقال صاحب "التلويح": إن الضلال في بعض الأحكام بناء على الخطاء في الاجتهاد بعد بذل الوسع لا ينافي كون المؤمنين العالمين بالشرائع الممتثلين الأمم، وبعد التسليم فلا دلالة قطعًا في الآية على قطعية إجماع المجتهدين من عصر واحد.(القمر)
للأوامر خير
توله ما تَولّى أي نجعله واليا لما توَلّاه من الضلال بأن نخلي بينه وبينه في الدنيا.(القمر) مثل مخالفة الرسول إلخ فإنه توعد على متابعة غير سبيل المؤمنين كما توعد على مخالفة الرسول باستيجاب النار، فكان إتباع غير سبيل المؤمنين حرامًا، فوجب إتباع سبيل المؤمنين، فكان الإجماع حجة فإنه سبيلهم؛ إذ السبيل ما يختاره الإنسان قولاً وعملاً ولقائل أن يقول : إن اتباع غير سبيل المؤمنين هو مشاقة الرسول بعينه، والفرق الاعتباري مفهوما يكفي لصحة العطف كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿أَطِيعُوا اللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا الرَّسُولَ﴾ (النساء:٥٩) مع أن طاعة الرسول عين طاعة الله تعالى في الوجود الخارجي، فحينئذٍ لا أثر لثبوت الإجماع من هذه الآية، كذا قال صاحب "التوضيح"، وقدح عليه صاحب "التلويح" بأن العطف وإن كان صحيحًا لكن سبيل المؤمنين عام لا مخصص له
بما ثبت إتيان الرسول به، فلا ضرورة للتخصيص مع أن حمل الكلام على الفائدة الجديدة أولى.(القمر) بعض المعتزلة إلخ وكذا الخوارج ، وهم شرذمة قليلة من الحمقاء، لا يعتد بهم لأنهم حادثون الاتفاق يشككون في ضروريات الدين مثل السوفسطائية في الضروريات العقلية. (السنبلي)

بيان حكم الإجماع
لأن كل واحد منهم يحتمل أن يكون مُخطئًا، فكذا الجميع. ولا يدرون قوة الحبل المؤلف من الشعرات وأمثاله، ثم إنهم اختلفوا في أن الإجماع هل يشترط في انعقاده أن
الشعر
يكون له داعٍ مقدّم عليه من دليل ظني أو ينعقد فجأةً بلا دليل باعث عليه بإلهام وتوفيق
من
كخبر الواحد والقياس
الله بأن يخلق الله فيهم علمًا ضروريًا ويوفقهم لاختيار الصواب؟ فقيل: لا يشترط له
أهل الإجماع أي بالحكم المجمع عليه
الداعي، والأصح المختار أنه لا بد له من داع على ما قال المصنف :
قد يكون من أخبار الآحاد والقياس، أمّا أخبار الآحاد فكإجماعهم على عدم
أي مستند الإجماع
أي التي تفيد الظن
والداعي جواز بيع الطعام قبل القبض والداعي إليه قوله علي: "لا تبيعوا الطعام قبل القبض"،
ولا يدرون قوة إلخ : وليس في شعره ما تلك القوة، وهذا ردّ لما قال بعض المعتزلة والروافض. (القمر) داع: أي السبب الذي يدعوهم إلى الإجماع. (القمر) فقيل: لا يشترط إلخ وفيه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يقول إلا بالوحي ظاهرا كان أو باطنا وبالاستنباط من المنصوص والأمة ليسوا بأعلى حالا منه ، فهم أولى بأن لا يقولوا إلا من دليل، وهو الداعي (القمر) أنه لا بد له إلخ فإن الفتوى بدون الحجية الشرعية حرام، فلا بد لأهل الإجماع من سند يستخرجون منه حكمًا ويجمعون عليه. وفائدة الإجماع بعد وجود السند سقوط البحث وصيرورة الحكم قطعيًا. (القمر) من داع إلخ وهو المختار الأصح دليله أولا أن الفتوى بلا دليل شرعي حرام كما قال في قمر الأقمار، والدليل الثاني أن يستحيل عادة اتفاق الكل لا لداع، فلا يوجد اتفاق من غير دليل كما يستحيل عادة اتفاق الكل على طعام واحد لعدم الداعي قال المخالفون: لو لزم الداعي فما فائدة الإجماع؛ إذ يكفي الداعي والسند، قلنا: الفائدة القطعية للحكم بعد ما كان ظنًا، ومن ههنا ذهب بعض الحنيفة إلى قطع عدم قطع السند. (السنبلي) أخبار الآحاد اتفاقًا كذا في عامة الكتب. [فتح الغفار: ٣٥٤] والقياس وهو قول الجمهور فهو جائز؛ لأنه لا مانع يقدر إلا الظنية، وليست مانعة كالآحاد وواقع كالإجماع على خلافه أبي بكر قياسًا على إمامته في الصلاة. [فتح الغفار: ٣٥٤] والقياس إلخ يخالفه الظاهرية وابن الطبري، فمنهم من منع جواز كون السند قياسًا عقلا، وبعضهم منع وقوعه وإن جاز عندهم عقلاً. (السنبلي) لا تبيعوا الطعام إلخ : في "المشكاة" وعن ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من ابتاع طعاما فلا يبعه حتى يستوفيه، متفق عليه، والمراد بالاستيفاء .القبض كذا في "اللمعات". (القمر)
جرير
وهو حديث ابن عباس قال : نهى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يباع الطعام قبل أن يُقبض، متفق عليه. قال ابن عباس ها: وأحسب كل شيء مثله. [إشراق الأبصار : ٢٩]
Chapter of Ijma'. Statement of the ruling of Ijma'. "And thus we have made you a middle nation that you may be witnesses upon the people." He described them with moderateness, which is justice, so their consensus is a proof. Likewise His statement: "You are the best nation brought forth for mankind" (Aal-Imran: 110). Goodness is only by virtue of their perfection in religion, so their consensus is a proof. Likewise His statement: "And whoever opposes the Messenger after guidance has become clear to him and follows other than the way of the believers - We will turn him to what he has turned" (An-Nisa: 115). Thus opposing the believers was made like opposing the Messenger, so their consensus is like the report of the Messenger, a definitive proof, and similar examples. And some of the Mu'tazila and Rawafid went astray and said that Ijma' is not a proof. Likewise: Just as We made your qibla the best of qiblas, We made you a middle nation, i.e., chosen or just, so that you may be witnesses upon the people on the Day of Resurrection concerning the conveyance of divine rulings by the prophets to them when they deny their conveyance, and the Messenger will be a witness over you after your completion. Thus said al-Baydawi. (al-Qamar) So their consensus is a proof, for the just is the one firm on the straight path, and there is no deviation in it from the right way. But one may say: Justice does not preclude error in ijtihad, for it is not sin; rather the erring mujtahid is rewarded. So there is no evidence in this verse for the definitiveness of the consensus of mujtahids from one era. (al-Qamar) "You are the best nation": The address is to the entire Ummah of Muhammad - for those present at that time, i.e., the Companions, and for those absent at that time upon existence "brought forth" i.e., manifested to the people. (al-Qamar) So their consensus is a proof: For if their consensus were not truth and proof, it would be misguidance, so how can the misguidance of the Ummah be the best of nations? And the author of al-Talwih said: Misguidance in some rulings based on error in ijtihad after exertion of capacity does not preclude believers knowledgeable in sacred laws following commands from being the best of nations. And even if conceded, there is no indication at all in the verse for the definitiveness of the consensus of mujtahids from one era. (al-Qamar) "We will turn him to what he has turned" i.e., We will make him a guardian over what he has turned to of misguidance by leaving him and it in this world. (al-Qamar) "Like opposing the Messenger etc." Because He threatened following other than the way of the believers just as He threatened opposing the Messenger by necessitating the Fire. So following other than the way of the believers became forbidden, so following the way of the believers became obligatory. Thus Ijma' is a proof because it is their way; for the way is what a person chooses of sayings and actions. And one may say: Following other than the way of the believers is the very same as opposing the Messenger, and the conceptual distinction in meaning suffices for the correctness of conjunction, as in His statement: "Obey Allah and obey the Messenger" (An-Nisa: 59) even though obedience to the Messenger is identical to obedience to Allah in external existence. So in that case, there is no effect for establishing Ijma' from this verse. Thus said the author of al-Tawdih. And the author of al-Talwih objected to him that while the conjunction is correct, the way of the believers is general with no specification, so there is no need for specification, and interpreting the speech with a new benefit is preferable. (al-Qamar) "Some of the Mu'tazila etc." And likewise the Khawarij. They are a small faction of fools, not to be regarded because they are latecomers who cast doubt on the necessities of religion, like the Sophists on intellectual necessities. (al-Sanabili) [PAGE_631] Chapter of Ijma'. Statement of the ruling of Ijma'. Because each one of them may be mistaken, so also all. And they do not know the strength of the rope composed of hairs and the like. Then they differed about whether, for its validity, Ijma' requires that it have a cause (da'i) preceding it from a speculative proof, or that it occur suddenly without a proof prompting it through inspiration and divine success from Allah, by Allah creating in them necessary knowledge and granting them success to choose the correct? So it was said: It does not require the cause. The sound and preferred view is that it must have a cause, as the author said: It may be from ahad reports and qiyas. As for ahad reports, it is like their consensus on the prohibition of selling food before taking possession, and the cause for it is his statement: "Do not sell food before taking possession." "And they do not know the strength etc.:" There is no strength in that (weak) strand. And this is a rebuttal of what some Mu'tazila and Rawafid said. (al-Qamar) "Da'i": The reason that calls them to Ijma'. (al-Qamar) "So it was said: It is not required etc." In it is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) only speaks through revelation, whether apparent or hidden, and through deduction from the revealed texts. The Ummah is not higher in status than him, so they are more entitled to only speak from a proof, which is the da'i. (al-Qamar) "That it must have etc." Because issuing a fatwa without legal authority is forbidden, so the people of Ijma' must have a source from which they extract a ruling and upon which they agree. The benefit of Ijma' after the existence of the source is the removal of inquiry and making the ruling definitive. (al-Qamar) "From a cause etc." And it is the preferred, sound view. Its proof: First, issuing a fatwa without a legal proof is forbidden, as mentioned in Qamar al-Aqmar. The second proof is that it is customarily impossible for all to agree without a cause, so agreement without proof is impossible, just as it is customarily impossible for all to agree on one food without a cause. The opponents said: If a cause is required, what is the benefit of Ijma'? For the cause and source suffice. We say: The benefit is the definitiveness of the ruling after it was speculative. And from here, some Hanafis have held to the definitiveness of the source even if it is not definitive. (al-Sanabili) Ahad reports (are valid as a cause) by agreement, as in most books. [Fath al-Ghaffar: 354] And qiyas (is valid); this is the view of the majority. It is permissible because there is no preventing factor except its speculativeness, which is not a preventer, just like ahad reports. And it has actually occurred, such as the consensus on the caliphate of Abu Bakr based on analogy with his leadership in prayer. [Fath al-Ghaffar: 354] The Zahiris and Ibn al-Tabbari oppose qiyas; some of them forbid it rationally as a source, others deny its occurrence even if they consider it permissible rationally. (al-Sanabili) "Do not sell food etc." In al-Mishkat: From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever buys food, let him not sell it until he takes possession of it." Agreed upon. And by "taking possession" is meant receipt (qabd). As in al-Lam'at. (al-Qamar) Jarir. And it is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: He said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade selling food before it is taken possession of. Agreed upon. Ibn Abbas said: I think everything is like that. [Ishraq al-Absar: 29]
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage from Noorul Anwar with its commentary (by Mulla Jeevan) presents the ruling (ḥukm) that Ijmaʿ (consensus of the Muslim community) is a definitive proof (ḥujjah qaṭʿiyyah). The commentator opens by citing three Qurʾānic proofs. First, the verse 'We have made you a middle nation' (2:143): 'middle' implies justice and moderation, so the consensus of such a just community is authoritative. Second, 'You are the best nation' (3:110): perfection in religion entails that their agreement cannot be error. Third, 'Whoever opposes the Messenger and follows other than the way of the believers' (4:115): equating divergence from the believers with divergence from the Messenger establishes that the collective way (sabīl) of the believers is binding. The commentator then records objections: justice does not preclude ijtihād error; the conjunction of 'obey Allah and obey the Messenger' (4:59) shows that following the believers is identical to following the Prophet, so the verse adds nothing. The response (from al-Talwīḥ) asserts that 'way of the believers' is general and not reducible to prophetic command. The passage then rejects dissenters (Muʿtazila, Rawāfiḍ, Khawārij) as negligible. On page 631, the discussion shifts to the condition of a cause (dāʿī) for the formation of Ijmaʿ. The author affirms the preferred (mukhtār) view: Ijmaʿ requires a preceding proof (dalīl ẓannī) that impels the mujtahids to agree, because issuing a fatwa without proof is forbidden and universal agreement without a cause is impossible in practice. The cause may be an āḥād hadith (e.g., the prohibition of selling food before taking possession) or qiyās (analogy), as exemplified by the Companions' consensus on Abū Bakr's caliphate based on analogy with his imamate in prayer. The commentator notes that some (Ẓāhirīs, Ibn al-Ṭabbarī) reject qiyās as a cause. The passage concludes with hadith texts on the sale of food. The overall weight of the arguments supports the Hanafī position that Ijmaʿ is a definitive proof founded on admissible sources.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijmāʿ): Consensus of the mujtahids of the Muslim community on a religious ruling after the death of the Prophet.
داعٍ (dāʿin): A cause or proof (dalīl) that prompts the mujtahids to form consensus.
سبيل المؤمنين (sabīl al-muʾminīn): The collective way or path of the believers, i.e., their consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Qur'anic verse is used to argue that following the way of the believers is obligatory and equates to obeying the Messenger?
A) 2:143
B) 3:110
C) 4:115
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Ijma' is a definitive proof in the Hanafi school, established by multiple Qur'anic verses that characterize the Ummah as just, best, and whose way is obligatory to follow.

The Condition of a Cause (Dāʿī) for Ijma'
Discusses the necessity of a cause (dāʿī) for Ijma' and permissible types of proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a cause (dāʿī) is required for Ijma', identify the preferred view, and cite examples of causes from āḥād hadith and qiyās.

Core Idea
Ijma' requires a speculative proof (dāʿī) because issuing a ruling without evidence is forbidden and universal agreement without cause is impossible.

After establishing the authority of Ijma', the text addresses a crucial methodological question: Does Ijma' need a preceding proof to activate? The Hanafi school affirms that a cause (dāʿī) is essential, and it can come from speculative sources like a single-transmission hadith or analogy. This lesson dissects that debate and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Some scholars held that Ijma' can occur spontaneously without a cause, while the sound view requires a cause.
The cause is a proof (dalīl) that impels the mujtahids to agree.
2
Explain the proofs for requiring a cause
First, issuing a fatwa without legal proof is forbidden. Second, it is customarily impossible for all mujtahids to agree without a cause.
The text compares it to the impossibility of all agreeing on one food without a cause.
3
List the types of causes
The cause can be an āḥād hadith (e.g., the hadith prohibiting sale of food before possession) or qiyās (e.g., the analogy for Abu Bakr's caliphate).
Some groups like the Zahiris reject qiyās as a cause.
4
Examine the example of the hadith
The hadith 'Do not sell food before taking possession' served as the cause for the Ijma' on that ruling.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and others.
5
Examine the example of qiyās
The consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate was based on analogy with his leadership in prayer. This shows qiyās can be a cause.
This demonstrates that speculative sources can generate definitive consensus.
6
State the benefit of Ijma' despite a cause
Even though the cause is speculative, Ijma' makes the ruling definitive, raising it from ẓann to qaṭʿ.
This is a key benefit: Ijma' removes inquiry and prevents further ijtihad.
